\textit{When Del-chan found out how I'd ended up joining the biology club---how I'd joined because a certain person had manipulated me---he got angry on my behalf. And, respecting my free will, he told me it was okay to quit. At that seaside park we visited for the first time, while looking out at the beautiful sea.}

\textit{In the end, I didn't change my mind. Because I wanted to experience youth with the people who'd pushed me forward.}

\textit{It's certain that because of that, Del-chan became a major presence in my life. There's also no doubt that he became a wonderful companion---a kindred spirit.}

\textit{But was that enough reason to fall for him as a member of the opposite sex?}

\textit{Del-chan only did what he thought was right. If I suddenly aimed feelings of love at him over nothing more than that, he'd only be confused. It might be one thing if we'd become important to each other over a long time, but it's only been three months since we met.}

Was I really such an easy girl that I could lose control of my feelings in that short a time?

Is there actually any reason for this unstoppable feeling?

$\delta$

As I looked for a seat in the lounge area, which had started to fill up, I kept thinking.

Why had Iwama been so forceful like that?

She wasn't the kind of person who would `aah-hn' a member of the opposite sex she didn't like. I thought I'd understood that much over the past three months. Then why?

It would be easy to come up with the hypothesis that she actually `likes' me. But I know Iwama isn't that kind of person. She's someone who has lived her life sacrificing the things she `likes.'

I suspect it's precisely because she's sacrificed her own `likes' that Iwama is so friendly to everyone. It's because she doesn't pick and choose that she can be so good with everyone. I'm just one more face in the crowd, on the verge of being captivated by someone as wonderful as her.

In short, there was no reason for Iwama to like me.

So there had to be another valid reason she'd done that `aah-hn.' The most likely explanation was that she absolutely wanted me to eat my favorite peach. Then why had she wanted me to eat it so badly?

Wait... could it be she noticed the thing with the menus?

If Iwama had realized she'd failed to show me the seasonal menu, and that as a result I hadn't been able to order the peach parfait I actually wanted, then her stubbornly sincere personality would explain why she'd tried so hard to make me eat the peach no matter what.

But how on earth could she have been so sure?

Unless she could somehow hear what was in my heart, she shouldn't have known that I actually wanted to eat the peach.

If there was any possibility, it was that she'd realized I was lying when I said, ``Didn't the waiter take them?'' while hiding the menus on my lap.

Lies have a way of telling the truth all too clearly. That lie alone could have been enough to expose what I was really after.

But for Iwama to see through that lie, she would've needed some way to confirm the menus were on my lap. Since she hadn't been paying attention to the menus until the next customer arrived, she shouldn't have noticed I'd hidden them from the start. And even though I'd been quite careful, Iwama had never once moved in a way that would let her see under the table. Even when she took the photo of the parfait, my lap shouldn't have been visible from where her phone was.

Between the moment Iwama started worrying about the menus and the moment she did the `aah-hn,' could she have discovered the menus hidden on my lap and become certain I was lying...?

If she did find them, what kind of trick had she used---?

``How about here? There are two seats together.''

I came back to myself at Iwama's voice. People had begun to increase in the mid-afternoon, but a pair of counter seats against the wall was vacant.

``Sounds good. Let's put our things down and go get some books.''

We headed toward the science shelves, carrying only our valuables. I focused on the mathematics books.

``Out of the six of us, we're especially weak in math, aren't we?''

I had no choice but to nod at Iwama's words. I had a seventy-two. Iwama had a seventy. Our scores were basically the same. Even Hijiri, who was in the liberal arts track, had an eighty, and the other three were all hovering around the hundred-point mark.

``Well, I think we're still near the top of the grade. The others were just too strong.''

``Everyone is so amazing! I was aiming for a seventy-five, but I didn't make it.''

``Why was seventy-five your goal?''

``There's a theory that getting a seventy-five in the five core subjects is equivalent to a perfect score at a normal high school. I wanted to work hard on the practical subjects too, so considering the study time involved, I decided to set that as my benchmark for the core five.''

Iwama had scored seventy-five or higher in everything except math. She'd properly reached what could be called the equivalent of a general perfect score.

``That's admirable. I completely gave up on social studies and the practical subjects.''

``You don't use them much for entrance exams! I think that's normal, though.''

\textit{Well, knowing Iwama, she'd probably work hard on the practical exams too without cutting corners.}

``By the way, what did you set as your target score for the practical subjects?''

``A perfect score, of course.''

``The teachers would be happy to hear that.''

After talking this much about it, I couldn't help wanting to ask about her actual scores. But it would've been rude to ask about marks that hadn't even been posted yet. Just as I was thinking we should leave the exam talk there, Iwama made a suggestion, looking a little embarrassed.

``If you'd like... should we show each other our score sheets later?''

Since Iwama was the one suggesting it, I simply replied, ``Sounds good.''

I pulled a few interesting-looking books from the math shelf and went back to the seats we'd claimed with our bags. Before we got into math, we took out the score sheets for all our subjects from our bags and showed them to each other.

I was stunned at a glance.

From Health and Physical Education and Music to Information, Iwama's scores were all perfect hundreds.

Since I'd already shown mine, it was too late, but my scores were all around sixty. Just like with social studies, they were the result of doing the bare minimum review and aiming for the line between passing and failing.

While my rank was higher in the five core subjects, Iwama was overwhelmingly ahead when it came to all subjects combined.

\textit{I'd always thought she had a versatile talent. But I never imagined it went this far.}

\textit{I genuinely felt that the girl studying right next to me was someone I couldn't possibly compete with on a human level. If Iwama had focused only on the five core subjects... our rankings surely would've been reversed.}

``That's amazing.''

That was all I could say. That day, I spent the entire time being taught both physics and math by Iwama.

The mystery of the parfait incident wasn't solved until after I got home. It was the mirror. When demonstrating optical communication, Iwama had used a small mirror. If she'd tilted that mirror at a forty-five-degree angle on her own lap, she would've been able to see mine. Looking back, there definitely had been a moment when Iwama seemed to be thinking about something while looking down at her own lap.

\textit{She saw through my lie, caught onto my ulterior motive, and in the end, I was the one being looked after. It was a total defeat on my part.}

\textit{Iwama is just too exceptional. So much so that I'm simply no match for her.}

Even though the exams were over, I stayed up late studying that night. I devoured the books I'd borrowed, trying my best to understand the parts Iwama and I had predicted would be on the tests.

That was when I found something strange in my pencil case.

A black scrap of paper that looked like half of a business-card-sized card. Ominous words had been foil-stamped onto it.


\textbf{Beware the Faculty of Science Orientation}

\textit{There is an impostor among the invitees}

% ==============================
%        Chapter 2
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Chapter 2\\
    ``The Faculty of Science Orientation Murder Case''
\end{center}
\label{sec:ch2V3}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Chapter 2}
\vspace{1cm}

$\delta$

``We will now begin the Reiwa 6 Faculty of Science Orientation!''

Saturday, July 20th. Clear skies. The Faculty of Science students had been hauled out of bed bright and early on the first day of summer vacation, and as they gathered in the gym at eight in the morning, Mikage-senpai opened the event from the podium at the edge of the stage.

``To repeat, the main goal of the Sci-Ori is to deepen the bonds between students. As part of that, we'll be holding an orienteering event of the Science Faculty, by the Science Faculty, and for the Science Faculty.''

He clearly had no intention of dragging the speech out. We students were gathered in the gym, loosely grouped by club, listening to our senior speak while standing. Even though it was summer vacation, everyone was in uniform.

``Now then, the upperclassmen have been working on preparations since the start of the fiscal year, and the first-years since the end of the recent exams, all for these two days. First, let us introduce the guests from our partner companies who have lent us their support!''

Mikage-senpai stepped down from the stage as he spoke. He headed toward a group of adults standing alongside the three club advisors, watching over us like parents at a school open house. There were twelve of them in all---the invited guests.

``These individuals have supported us by providing the funds and supplies needed for this Sci-Ori, and some of them have even helped with the preparations themselves. On behalf of the Science Faculty, I would like to offer my heartfelt thanks.''

Mikage-senpai bowed, and a massive round of applause broke out from the students.

I clapped along with them while carefully sizing up the twelve invited guests one by one.

\textit{Among them was an impostor.}

\textit{Or at least, someone believed there was.}

Mikage-senpai introduced the guests one by one without missing a beat. Most were in their forties or fifties, and the majority were men. That was why the one who stood out the most was a foreign woman who looked to be around thirty.

Her name was Claire Larsson, and she was an executive at an international consulting firm. She was apparently in charge of the STEM education division. Among the invited guests, most of whom were in dress shirts or work clothes, she stood out all the more in her casual sleeveless outfit.

Her sharp Western features would no doubt have been considered beautiful even in her home country. She looked like the kind of actress you only saw in movies. With her beautifully waved chestnut hair, clothes that clearly showed off the lines of her body, and a low-cut neckline, it definitely wasn't my imagination that the gym got noticeably louder when she gave her greeting.

``I'm re---ally looking forward to seeing what all of you can do. Please be good to me for these next two days!''

When she gave her greeting in fluent Japanese with an American-style accent, a large round of applause erupted.

``If she were my boss, I'd work myself to death.''

Mizasaki stood beside me, beaming as he clapped with all his might. \textit{Dying from overwork would just be a nuisance to her.}

The other two who stood out were men introduced as Tsunanagai High School alumni. A man named Bakuma from a major general contractor, and a man named Kurauchi from a major metal manufacturer. Both looked to be in their thirties; Bakuma-san looked like a businessman in a blue vest neatly fitted over his light-blue dress shirt, while Kurauchi-san looked like a field worker in loose gray work clothes.

\textit{It might have been rude to think it was exactly what you'd expect, but the sharp-looking Bakuma-san was a former American football player and a dyed-in-the-wool athlete, while the plain-looking Kurauchi-san was a former chemistry club member and a dyed-in-the-wool science guy.}

Once the introductions were over, Karato-senpai led the twelve guests out of the gym.

``Now then, the orienteering over the next two days will be a grueling, no-holds-barred competition with glory and a banquet at a high-end yakiniku restaurant on the line.''

Mikage-senpai returned to the stage and flashed a cruel smile behind the podium.

``The details of each event will remain secret until right before they begin. Those of you who already know, be careful not to spoil anything for the selected members. And! As I believe was mentioned in the pamphlets handed out beforehand, we've received very special permission from the principal for everyone to stay overnight at the school!''

A burst of excited cheers went up. Spending the night at a school where everyone was normally required to leave by final dismissal was the kind of thing you almost never got to experience unless there was some kind of emergency.

``I'm sure these two days will be full of surprises. Now then, that's enough explanation from the representative, so let's bring out the orienteering Game Master.''

When Mikage-senpai signaled to the wings of the stage, Hongo-senpai came out with a light step.

``Hii! I'm Hongo, the Game Master. I was in charge of designing and coordinating the orienteering. I'm sure it'll catch you all by surprise, so look forward to it!''

\textit{I'd expected it, but seeing that smile still made my blood run cold. The terrifying Hongo-senpai had designed this grueling competition. I couldn't even imagine what was waiting for us.}

``The overall premise of the orienteering is simple: the winners will be the team that gets their hands on the trophy first during tomorrow's third task. I'll say that again. The winning team is the one that gets the trophy first.''

It wasn't that the trophy would be handed over after victory had been decided; rather, whichever team secured the trophy first would be the winner. In other words, the trophy was probably hidden at the goal.

``And now, I'd like to announce a special surprise just for this year! We'll now be assigning the teams, so will the six selected members please come up onto the stage?''

A wave of genuine agitation, very different from the earlier chatter, swept through the gym.

\textit{What does she mean, team assignments?}

\textit{A surprise?}

Since we'd been called, I headed to the stage with Iwama. Beside me, Iwama looked up at me anxiously.

``Wasn't it supposed to be club against club?''

``I thought so too...''

Come to think of it, I didn't think the seniors had ever actually said it would be club against club. Two first-year students would be selected from each of the physics, chemistry, and biology clubs. Then it would be a three-way team battle. That was all they'd said. They'd never said how the teams would be formed.

``Hii, thanks. Now, everyone, line up side by side according to the teams I call out.''

Hongo-senpai smiled at the six of us who had gathered on the stage.

``First, Team X! Watari-kun, Mikage-san, Izuta-kun.''

\textit{The blood drained from my face. `Wait... if that's how it is---'}

``And Team Y! Hijiri-kun, Togakushi-kun, Iwama-san.''

Voices of doubt began to spread through the gym. There were only six selected members. If they were split into groups of three, that would only make two teams, which meant it wouldn't be a three-way battle.

``And Team Z! Everyone else! All first-years are participating this year! Let's all give it our best!''

\textit{It was absurd. No matter how I looked at it, it was completely insane.}

\textit{On top of having the first- and second-ranked students in the grade against me, even Iwama had ended up on the enemy side; was I seriously supposed to take on everyone else too?}

\fullpageimage{5.jpg}

\thispagestyle{plain}
\vspace{1cm}
$\gamma$

I had completely assumed I'd be fighting alongside Del-chan, but that assumption was overturned in an instant.

After we'd studied together so much!

``You've got quite the look on your face. But it's okay. It's probably fairer than all of you think! This orienteering event is an information war. The key will be how you gather the information that leads you to the `answer'.''

Hongo-senpai looked more amused than anyone as she watched our agitation and confusion.

``For example, in the first task, Teams X and Y will have to go out into the city and gather information themselves. There are two identical sets of information placed in the same locations, so there won't be any fighting over them.''

Everyone probably understood that part. The problem was what the much larger Team Z would be doing.

``At first, everyone in Team Z won't be able to move around freely, because each of you will have assigned duties. So you'll gather information as a group by watching footage broadcast by the upperclassmen and sharing what you learn.''

In other words, it wasn't just about passing through checkpoints like in ordinary orienteering; what mattered was obtaining some kind of information at those points.

``Of course, Teams X and Y have restrictions too. For the next two days, the six selected members may use only what they've been given and whatever they obtain along the way. Your smartphones will also be confiscated. Now, isn't that nice?''

Orienteering was supposed to be a competition where you found your way with a map and compass. I'd prepared myself for that. It wasn't.

``I'll leave it at that, because saying too much would make it boring. Now then, does anyone have any questions?''

At that, Osawa-kun (the blond boy in the physics club who's close with Mizasaki-kun) immediately raised his hand.

``If Team Z wins, do we all get to eat top-tier yakiniku?''

The first-years other than the selected members suddenly got noisy. I didn't miss the gleam in Mizasaki-kun's eyes.

``Of course. Though from a budget standpoint, I'd really like X or Y to do their best.''

How much would it actually cost to feed top-tier yakiniku to around twenty high school students?

If it came out to tens of thousands of yen per person... I really didn't want to think about it.

``Understood! Then we're definitely going to win!''

Mizasaki-kun answered the fired-up Osawa-kun with a ``Yeah!'' A lot of the boys followed suit.

``Good. Anyone else? Are the six selected members good?''

We probably weren't, but no one raised a hand.

``And now, the absolute rule. This is important, so make sure you remember it!''

Hongo-senpai held up a remote and pressed a button, and the projector lens lit up white.

Those of us standing on the stage turned around. Three rules were displayed on the screen.

\begin{center}
Do not engage in interference that makes continuation impossible

Do not engage in acts of destruction that are beyond recovery

Do not stop the competition unless a declaration of cancellation is made
\end{center}

All of them were fairly ominous rules, but the last line was particularly creepy. It made it sound as though situations that would make you want to stop the game were already being taken for granted.

``Did you all get a good look? Well, I'll be posting these in various places, so please keep them in mind at all times. Now, that really is the end of the explanation. The first task starts at ten, so everyone, make sure you're at your posts by then. Dismissed!''

When Hongo-senpai spread her arms wide, the entire gym erupted in a massive round of applause.

I casually glanced over at Del-chan. He was looking my way at that exact same moment.

\textit{Ideally, I would have been fighting at his side. I would have run through the streets with him. Maybe that was just my own selfish hope, but I felt like Del-chan felt the same way.}

Wanting to know for sure, I stepped off the stage and went to Del-chan first.

``That was unexpected, huh?''

\textit{It was unfair of me to test the waters without even saying what I meant.}

``After all the trouble you went to teaching me, it looks like it was all for nothing, Iwama.''

``No, not at all. Studying together was a lot of fun.''

``Then I'll gladly put what you taught me to use.''

Feeling the conversation start to drift, I decided to say what I really felt.

``It feels a little lonely, doesn't it?''

``\dots\dots Yeah.''

\textit{Regret hit me at once, like I'd forced those words out of him. What on earth was I doing?}

``But after working together all this time, a little rivalry isn't so bad.''

\textit{That was so like Del-chan, teasing me with wording that made us sound like a couple.}

``It's a showdown between science geeks with our pride on the line. If we're doing this, let's make it a real match.''

``Yeah! Let's do our best\dots\dots scientifically!''

The words came out before I could stop them, but even I didn't really know what that catchphrase of mine was supposed to mean.

$\gamma$

Following the third-year in black-rimmed glasses, the twelve invitees headed in a line toward the reception room.

From within the line, that person looked back at the cheerful students.

The preparations were complete. The doomed game was about to begin.

The vast majority of high school students making an innocent fuss were blameless, but it couldn't be helped. The Science Club Orientation was an event destined for a tragic conclusion.

If the plan proceeded smoothly, it would happen as soon as today.

$\delta$

``Hey, Izuta. You got a second?''

Hijiri called out to me just as I stepped out of the restroom.

``If it'll only take a second.''

Despite that, Hijiri led me over to a wall by the athletic field. It was an open spot where no one could eavesdrop, but still close enough to get to without changing into outdoor shoes. We stood there with our backs against the wall.

``Hongo-senpai is a genius at manipulating people. She flipped the script right at the start with those unexpected teams.''

``She's probably planning to stir things up by playing us against each other and throwing the game into chaos.''

``This probably isn't the end of it. She'll betray our expectations time and time again. That's likely how the plan goes.''

``I can't wait to see it.''

``Yeah.''

Underneath his genuinely eager tone, there was something rigid there too.

``\dots\dots You brought me out here because of that card?''

``Yes. I wanted to share my thoughts as they stand now.''

Hijiri pulled his student handbook from his pocket and slid out the item hidden within its cover. To anyone watching, it probably looked like we were just checking the school rules.

Inside the handbook was a small black card. Words were inscribed on it in silver foil.

\begin{center}
Without letting anyone notice

Secretly find the imposter
\end{center}

The top of the card was jaggedly torn. Naturally, this card was the counterpart to the one I had received. When held together, the edges aligned perfectly, forming a business-card-sized rectangle.

``Beware the Science Club Orientation. There is an imposter among the invitees.''

``Without letting anyone realize, secretly find the imposter.''

Put together, the messages formed four lines of ten characters each.

Last Saturday, this had been slipped into my pencil case, and Hijiri had received his half the same way.

And we both came to the same conclusion.

---\textit{Since it's torn, the rest of the text must be somewhere else.}

Since the message was sensitive, we discreetly asked around about a black card without revealing the details, and that led us to each other fairly quickly.

That's how Hijiri and I ended up sharing a single message.

Hijiri and I were both members of the Tsunanagai High School Science Club, our names were recorded on the Eight Immortals list, and we had both been selected for the Science Club Orientation. But if you were looking for our biggest common factor, you couldn't ignore that enormous prime factor: the ``Tengu Festival Incident'' during Golden Week.

That incident had drawn the ire of a powerful authority and resulted in a sharp reduction in donations to Tsunanagai High School. What happened then forced us to share a secret we couldn't tell anyone, and that had forged a special bond between us.

Now that a suspicious message had arrived, we had no choice but to be on our guard.

``A tip-off, or a warning of a crime? Either way, we can't deny the possibility that something might happen at the Science Club Orientation.''

Hijiri voiced the conclusion we had already reached once before.

``I still think this is probably just part of the game Hongo-senpai set up, though.''

``I'd like to think so too. Those people weren't exactly trustworthy to begin with.''

``Doesn't that line about `not stopping the competition unless there's an official cancellation' sound like foreshadowing for Hongo-senpai or Mikage-senpai pulling something outrageous?''

``It certainly did. But even so, we have to prepare for the worst.''

Hijiri spoke calmly and looked at me.

``What surprised me today was the number of invitees. Twelve people coming from such prestigious, well-known companies.''

``An `imposter' being mixed in among those twelve feels a little too perfect.''

``True. But if an `imposter' really was mixed in this time, they're not doing it for thirty pieces of silver. I have a hypothesis.''

Hijiri lowered his already quiet voice even further.

``Seeing the invitees the senpai had gathered made me certain. They work for major corporations, and on top of that, they're in positions to move serious money. Do you understand what it means to invite twelve people like that?''

``\dots\dots Donations.''

``Exactly. Donations to Tsunanagai High School from the alumni association are expected to drop sharply because of that incident. We're talking millions, maybe even tens of millions of yen. And Mikage-senpai is the one being held responsible for it. He probably wants to find some way to make up for that loss.''

``So he's running this Science Club Orientation as an event to raise funds?''

``Yeah. It's a spectacle. He'll have the top students compete in an elaborate game, film it with professional-grade equipment, and show it off to the invitees. `What do you think? Instead of making a one-time contribution, why not become our sponsor?' That's the pitch.''

``\dots\dots And the imposter came to sabotage that?''

``Doesn't everything fall into place if you look at it that way? The people who turned against us after that incident aren't going to be happy if the science club succeeds. Donations plummeted because of a blunder by a student council officer from the science club---and they want to use that to drag the club down. It would be a problem for them if the Science Club Orientation succeeds and secures sponsors.''

\textit{Just what I'd expect from Hijiri. He really understood the politics at school.}

``But\dots\dots how would they make it fail?''

``That's exactly the `worst case' I was talking about. I think they'll cause a major accident in a situation where the blame falls on the science club, leaving them no way out. It seems they couldn't get the event cancelled, either.''

A chill ran down my spine, despite it being a summer morning.

``Injuries. Deaths. Burning down a building. Breaking something irreplaceable. If they can make it look like the science club caused some irreversible accident, they can deal a devastating blow. The Science Club Orientation is the perfect chance for that, isn't it? Dangerous things are being done, and outsiders can get in as invitees.''

``No way, that's\dots\dots It can't be that easy to frame someone.''

``True. If it's proven to be the work of an outsider, the club can't be blamed. They have to make it a perfect crime. They need to cause an accident in a situation where it'll be judged the science club's fault no matter what. The fake invitee would have to set it up under those constraints.''

I thought. A perfect crime. Framing the science club. The situations where that would be possible had to be limited.

But was it even possible to stop it completely?

``I know how you feel, Izuta. You want to call it off. But wait. At the end of the day, this Science Club Orientation is also our way of cleaning up the mess we made. I don't want to ruin it over an inference based on a mere forty characters. If anything, I think we should do everything we can to make it a success.''

Hijiri was right about that. Mikage-senpai had gathered all those invitees to make up for the drop in donations caused by what happened with us. That much was certain. Hijiri and I were in a position where we should wish for the success of this Science Club Orientation more than anyone. We couldn't let it get cancelled just because we'd received a suspicious message.

``\dots\dots You're right. We have to do it.''

I said it, but the anxiety wouldn't go away. \textit{It would be one thing if the only ones in danger were Hijiri and me. But if it was someone else---like Iwama, who'd been looking forward to this so much---}

``Izuta, let's make a promise.''

Hijiri looked me straight in the eye with a serious expression.

``It's only natural to feel anxious. I feel the same way when I think about someone important getting hurt. That's why the two of us will do everything we can to protect the people within our reach. We'll keep our senses sharpened and miss none of the signs of danger. We'll stay on alert the whole time, assuming there's an imposter among the invitees.''

As if that still wasn't enough, Hijiri added one more thing.

``I swear I'll protect your teammate, Iwama-san, even if it costs me my life.''

``\dots\dots It's not like I'm only worried about Iwama.''

``I know. But the selected members move around the most and draw the most attention, so they're at the highest risk of an accident, and if something does happen, the impact will be huge. If I were the enemy, I'd target one of the selected members.''

\textit{Hijiri had a point. The six of us were at particularly high risk.}

``Got it. I'll stay as alert as I can and protect everything within my reach. I'll also keep an eye out for any suspicious moves from the invitees.''

``It's a promise. And one last thing.''

Hijiri held out his right hand, asking for a handshake.

``It's also our job to make the Science Club Orientation a success. Let's both give it everything we've got.''

``That's exactly what I want.''

When I took his hand, he gripped mine hard enough that it was almost painful. Hijiri's glasses glinted.

``It goes without saying, but I never pull any punches in a competition like this.''

$\gamma$

The selected members gathered in the first-floor conference room that was being used as the waiting area. It was a large room containing nothing but desks, chairs, and a whiteboard. Team X and Team Y took opposite sides of the room. Each desk had light snacks and drinks on it, along with tools like soldering irons and screwdrivers. I wondered whether there was a chance we'd be doing some kind of work here too.

I'd thought we'd be changing into tracksuits, but apparently we were doing the first day's morning session in our uniforms. Come to think of it, running through the streets was probably just a figure of speech. If students started running around a tourist spot on a weekend with that many people around, it'd be awful publicity for Tsunanagai High School.

There was still plenty of time before the ten o'clock start. The upperclassmen and the people on Team Z should have been moving to their assigned positions around then. Since we had nothing else to do, those of us on Team Y went ahead and introduced ourselves.

Hijiri-kun and I already knew each other fairly well. As for Togakushi-kun, we'd only ever seen each other when the selected members were announced, so this was the first time we'd actually spoken.

``I'm Togakushi. I hate trouble, but if I'm doing this, I'm going to win. I'm counting on you guys.''

He spoke in a quiet, low voice, and very quickly. His mind must have moved just as fast. I got the impression his mouth was struggling to keep up with how fast he was thinking. His striking look---white hair and bloodshot eyes---was the same as when we'd first met, but I found his concise way of speaking oddly likable.

``Of course. Let's win this.''

With his usual dignified air, Hijiri-kun offered Togakushi-kun a handshake. Togakushi-kun obliged, though he looked like he couldn't be bothered. It felt like he'd weighed the hassle of shaking hands against the hassle of refusing and gone with the former.

``By the way, is that white hair natural?''

``It's obviously bleached.''

``I see. I thought maybe it reflected UV light or something.''

Hijiri-kun sounded like he was joking, but I didn't really get it. Togakushi-kun gave a short, derisive laugh, then popped open a can of white Monster Energy and took a drink.

To be honest, the mood was a little awkward.

Having the number-one and number-two brains in the grade on my side was incredibly reassuring. But I had a feeling the two of them didn't really mesh. They were practically complete opposites. It was just a gut feeling, but Togakushi-kun struck me as the type who valued efficiency and kept relationships casual, while Hijiri-kun seemed like the type who aimed for perfection and valued close bonds.

Looking over at the three on Team X, they seemed to be chatting in a much more friendly, open, easygoing way.

Honestly, I'm jealous\dots!

$\delta$

``Being teamed up with you seriously sucks. Don't hold me back, small fry.''

``You can say the same right back at yourself.''

Watari and I had hated each other ever since middle school. Calling it ``bad'' was putting it mildly; it was the absolute worst. Just looking at his thug-like face---with his long brown hair and a piercing in one ear---was enough to piss me off.

We were both science-track students with similar grades, and we'd been competing forever, but in every other respect, we were oil and water. Watari had grown up in England and was good at English, while I was better at Japanese than English. Watari was athletic and popular with girls, while I was the exact opposite.

``Did the biology club at least do anything for your stamina? If you gas out halfway through, I'm leaving you behind, Delta.''

``What about you, Watari? Have you actually been studying science? Your finals didn't look so great.''

``Don't get cocky. Of course you'd win if it's just biology and chemistry.''

``Your Japanese score was pretty impressive too.''

``That's that damn teacher's fault for being so picky about kanji. He took off points just because I didn't flick one stroke right.''

With Watari constantly picking at me like that, I couldn't help answering back like a kid.

``You two are as close as ever, I see.''

Our voices overlapped as we snapped ``Who is?'' at Mikage's smiling face. That just made it look even more like we really were close. \textit{I swear on my life, our relationship was the absolute worst.}

``But whatever, with Mikage here, I guess there's no point in arguing too much.''

``Yeah, I guess. I'll play nice for now, since I don't have a choice.''

And so, purely because we had no other option, we agreed to work together.

``Still, this is ridiculously unfair. Why are first and second place both stuck over there?''

Watari grumbled as he drank from one of the canned juices that had been set out for us.

I could definitely understand how he felt. Going by the Eight Immortals rankings, that side had first, second, and seventh place. We, on the other hand, had fourth, fifth, and sixth. And seventh place was Iwama. As far as I was concerned, there was no way Iwama was below us in scientific ability. She'd just focused more on the practical subjects for finals.

And then there was Hijiri\dots\ he was the one person in the entire grade I least wanted as an enemy. For some reason, I just couldn't picture myself ever beating Hijiri in a contest.

``But I think the balance is actually pretty good,'' Mikage said, his pleasant smile never wavering.

``Over there, they're all high achievers---generalists who score well across the board. But Togakushi-kun only joined the chemistry club recently, and Hijiri-kun had originally planned to go into the humanities---Iwama-san is the only one with the kind of experience you'd expect from the science clubs. On the other hand, this side is made up of specialists in our own fields.''

``Is that so\dots?''

Mikage nodded confidently at Watari's doubt.

``Delta-kun has biology and chemistry. Watari-kun has physics. And I have mathematics. We've all been at this for a long time.''

It felt like my share of the load was a little heavy, but he was right---the balance wasn't bad.

``So the senpai took all that into account when they split up the teams?''

``Yeah. Knowing her, I'm sure she did.''

$\gamma$

Shortly after nine, Mikage-senpai came to the conference room.

``Oh, you all look lively. Got a minute? I'd like to show you around the site, if you're up for it.''

``The site?''

Mikage-senpai nodded with a refreshing smile at Hijiri-kun's question.

``Exactly. Once you're through this orientation, you'll be the core members of the science club starting next year, and that means you'll be on the management side. Think of this as a kind of preliminary walkthrough.''

Those of us on Team Y looked at one another. Togakushi-kun whispered to us in his usual rapid-fire way.

``We might find some hints. Let's go.''

No one objected. Delta and the others must have thought the same thing, because everyone left the conference room.

Led by the senpai, the first place we went was a room called the ``Sub-Control Room'' next to the audiovisual room. It wasn't a room students normally got to enter. When he opened the heavy door, I saw rows of monitors showing color bars in the dark room, with countless glowing switches on the desk in front of them. Rolling chairs were scattered in front of the desk. It looked like people sat there to work the switches. Part of the wall was a long horizontal window, and through it I could see the stage in the audiovisual room on the other side.

``The filming crew is starting to take their positions now, and the footage from all those cameras comes here. Six-cam, can you show the selected teams something?''

That last part was directed at the intercom Mikage-senpai had picked up from the desk. It was a communication device with a single earpiece and microphone. A response seemed to come through the earpiece, and the senpai flipped a switch. A brick wall appeared on one of the monitors.

``Well, it's basically like this. All the footage gets recorded for the time being, but the only shots shown to the public are the ones I choose here. Then we add music and commentary so everyone can enjoy it.''

Hijiri-kun looked at the footage and whispered to us.

``I think that brick wall is from Iizaki Tunnel. I wonder if it's one of the checkpoints.''

That caught me a little off guard. To know the location just from a piece of wall!

``Nice, Hijiri.''

Togakushi-kun spoke in a low, emotionless voice. His eyes darted around the sub-control room as if he were trying to wring every scrap of information out of it. The two of them had already started competing.

I'd thought Hijiri-kun and Togakushi-kun were complete opposites, but they were perfectly aligned on one point: they wanted to win. And they had no intention of cutting corners to do it.

Realizing that this was the mindset of the people at the top of the grade lit a fire under me too, and I steeled myself.

Sorry, Del-chan, but I'm not going to lose!

``Oh, the invitees are here. Let's head to the audiovisual room.''

Mikage-senpai switched all the monitors back to color bars and pointed toward the audiovisual room visible through the window. I could see the invitees from the sponsoring companies walking down the center aisle in a line.

When we left the sub-control room and stepped into the audiovisual room, it looked a little different from usual. The desks and chairs in the front row had been removed, and in their place were spacious leather seats---like green-car seats on a train or business class on a plane. A small round table was placed beside each chair. On a long table against the wall were bottle coolers filled with all kinds of bottles, along with rows of different glasses. They were probably meant to watch the broadcast while enjoying drinks. The invitees being shown to their seats looked genuinely surprised.

``The only time I've ever seen spectator seating like this is in a death game.''

At Watari-kun's spot-on observation, Del-chan---

``You've actually watched a death game?''

---fired back with a response that was just as spot-on. They were just as perfectly in sync as when he talked with Mizasaki-kun.

As he led us along, Mikage-senpai gestured toward the stage at the front.

``Images will be projected on this screen in real time. At the podium in front of it, a smooth-talking host and a commentator will keep the conversation going. Of course, there'll inevitably be some downtime, so the plan is to explain the tasks here while mixing in live demonstrations.''

Looking closer, I saw what were probably demonstration props set up at the side of the stage. They were covered with black cloths, but some of the bigger items weren't completely hidden. I squinted, trying to make out what was there. The large black translucent sheet was probably a polarizing filter. Light was a wave that vibrates in many directions, and this material could extract only the waves moving in a particular one. It was used in things like LCD screens and sunglasses. Aside from that---

``Oh! So these are today's stars?''

The woman who stood out the most broke away from the group of invitees and came over to us. It was Claire-san. She was beautiful, with flowing chestnut hair.

She trotted over in an oddly cute way, fixed her eyes on Del-chan---the one standing closest---and then, to my utter disbelief, proceeded to ruffle his hair all up. Del-chan just stood there in shock and let her do whatever she wanted. And to make matters worse, his eyes were fixed on her chest, swaying right in front of him.

\fullpageimage{6.jpg}

\thispagestyle{plain}
\vspace{1cm}

``Everyone's so cute! I wonder if you call it a seiheki in Japanese, but I just love hot guys in glasses! Let's be friends, Sho.''

\textit{Roger that!}

\textit{I had to wonder what a grown adult was doing messing with high school students like this. Was that kind of boundarylessness normal in the West? And Del-chan was being Del-chan, of course. He was totally charmed, grinning like an idiot\dots}

``What's `Four-eyes'?''

At Mikage-san's question, Watari-kun replied with a displeased look and a single word: ``Glasses.'' \textit{I hated myself for getting hung up on something so pointless---thinking it just as easily could have been Hijiri-kun instead.}

\textit{I found myself wondering what hormone was supposed to suppress jealousy. I was going to look that up later.}

``They're about to take on a tough game, so please don't tease them too much.''

\textit{I didn't think he'd picked up on how I felt,} but Mikage-senpai stopped Claire-san anyway.

``Oh, sorry. You're right---do your best, everyone!''

Claire-san clenched her fists in front of her chest, winked at Del-chan, and walked off.

``Kurauchi-san and Bakuma-san aren't here, though.''

Hijiri-kun pointed that out without warning. \textit{If I remembered right, those two were supposed to be Tsunanagai High School alumni.}

``Ah, I've got those two helping out with some work off-site. Since they're graduates, they said they'd rather be out in the field sweating alongside their juniors than sitting here watching.''

``I see. So that's what was going on.''

Hijiri-kun looked like he was turning something over in his mind. \textit{Was it just my imagination? It looked like Del-chan, his hair still all ruffled, met his eyes for a split second.}

$\delta$

Of all places, the starting location was the audiovisual room. Two long tables had been set up on the stage, each with a black backpack and a familiar thin paper booklet on top.

It was the exam questions.

The visible cover read ``Science Department Orientation Exam Questions -- Day 1, Afternoon Session.'' Beneath that was ``July 13, Reiwa 6 -- 10:00 to 15:00,'' followed by a single line of instructions.

\begin{center}
Do not open this exam booklet until given the signal to start.
\end{center}

``I'm sure you're curious, but don't touch anything on the table just yet!''

Hongo-senpai, who had led us up onto the stage, said cheerfully.

Tense BGM---what Watari called ``like an escape game''---filled the audiovisual room as ten invitees watched us from the front row. Behind them, several upperclassmen who seemed to have school duties were watching us with evaluative eyes. There were also upperclassmen at the podium, acting as moderator and commentator while testing their microphones. Above all, Team X and Team Y each had a two-person upperclassman camera crew with them---Cam 1 and Cam 2---aiming video cameras with microphones at us. Just being in a setting like this was enough to make anyone nervous.

There were about five minutes left until 10:00. Hanging from the side of the black backpack were three things that looked like ID holders. One for each of us. At the moment, with our wallets, smartphones, and even our house keys taken away, the only things we could rely on were the items we'd been given. I wondered what was inside those holders.

``Um, today's July 20th, right?''

From Team Y's side, Hijiri spoke up and pointed that out. Come to think of it, he was right. The date on the cover of the exam booklet was the 13th. Whether it was a mistake or not, the date was off by a full week.

``That's right. I, Hongo Nagisa, do not make mistakes, so rest easy.''

Hongo-senpai said with a smile that looked far more sadistic than cheerful. She glanced once at the large stopwatch hanging around her neck, then turned to face us all.

``All right, let me explain! The first task itself is simple. Use the clues hidden around Tsunanagai City to deduce a certain truth, then come report your answer to me in person. The details are written on the papers I'll hand out once it's 10:00.''

Senpai held up an envelope that presumably contained the documents.

``The important part is that you return to the school and report that truth to me directly. I'll be in the sub-control room the whole time. The deadline is 15:00. Be careful, because if you go past that, you'll be disqualified.''

That meant we had five hours. Depending on where the locations were, that sounded like more than enough time. But then I wondered what we'd do about lunch---and right as that thought crossed my mind, Hongo-senpai added an extra note.

``During the task, everyone will be required to take a lunch break. The rule is that between 12:00 and 13:00, you must stay at one establishment for at least thirty minutes without moving. Break that rule, and you'll be disqualified too, so make sure to rest properly and eat lunch.''

\textit{I see. That was a relief. At the same time, though, I couldn't help feeling that the condition Senpai had imposed hinted at a situation where ``you really wouldn't have time to stop for lunch.''}

``Also, a word of advice. By working through those exam questions, you'll naturally be able to figure out where in the city you need to go, but it's possible you may reach the truth before visiting every location. Of course, it's perfectly possible to clear the first task that way.''

She pointed one light-blue-painted index finger straight at the ceiling.

``But that may cause problems for you later, so if possible, I recommend visiting every single one. There are two copies of every clue, and they're exactly the same, so both teams will be able to get them!''

I sorted through everything she'd just said in my head.

Start at 10:00. Visit the locations in the city indicated by the exam questions and deduce ``a certain truth.'' Take at least thirty minutes for lunch between 12:00 and 13:00. Return to the sub-control room by 15:00 and report that ``truth'' directly to Hongo-senpai. Even if we didn't visit every location, we could still clear the first task, but apparently that would put us at a disadvantage in the second and third tasks.

\textit{It sounded easier than I'd expected. I'd been worried we'd end up in a direct clash with Team Y, but if this was how it worked, we might be able to finish the task without getting in each other's way too much.}

``One minute until the start. Everyone in position and ready?!''

Hongo-senpai exchanged looks with the moderator and commentator, then turned toward the window at the back of the audiovisual room. In the dark sub-control room, Mikage-senpai was making a big circle with both hands.

``Cam 1-san, Cam 2-san, ready?''

The two crew members standing beside us nodded. The crew on Team Y's side nodded as well. Only then did I notice that both crew members assigned to us were exceptionally tan and muscular, while the two on Team Y's side looked much more like indoor types. I wondered whether that meant anything.

When I glanced toward Team Y, my eyes met Iwama's. A smile stronger than a mere grin played at her lips.

``Yes! It's 10:00! First task, start!''

Senpai briskly handed out the papers in front of us. I tore my gaze away from Iwama and looked back at the desk.

The very first line of the extra handout contained the ominous word ``Murder.''

\begin{center}
\textbf{Report and Proposal regarding the ``Science Dept Orientation Murder Incident''}
\end{center}

On Saturday, July 13, 2024, at the event ``Science Dept Orientation'' held by the science-related club group of Prefectural Tsunanagai High School, commonly known as the ``Science Dept,'' second-year student E-mi died. The cause of death was a fall. While attempting to cross scaffolding set up at a checkpoint, it collapsed, and she fell to the bottom of the valley, struck her head, and died instantly. The accident occurred at 19:05, during preparations for the following day.

I, the great detective Hongo Nagisa, have already arrived at the truth. This was a murder. The bolts on the scaffolding had been deliberately removed in order to harm her. The culprit is one of the following four people.

\begin{center}
・A-suke \quad ・B-ko \quad ・C-taro \quad ・Doctor D
\end{center}

However, the culprit has extenuating circumstances. Surely even you first-years don't want a murderer to come out of the Science Dept. I am willing to turn a blind eye to the truth and report it to the police as nothing more than an unfortunate accident.

Therefore, I have a proposal for you. If you can uncover the truth of ``who the culprit is'' and report it to me by 15:00 today, I shall delay my report to the police in consideration of your efforts.

This is a challenge from me.

To reiterate, every statement made by me, the great detective Hongo Nagisa, is the truth, and there is no room for doubt.

Good luck to you all!

\begin{flushright}
Great Detective Hongo Nagisa
\end{flushright}

``You've got to be kidding me. So it's a murder mystery game.''

Watari, who'd finished reading at almost the exact same time I had, muttered right beside me.

``Murder mystery game?''

``You don't even know that? It's like a Madamis.''

``Don't explain the original term with an abbreviation.''

``Shut up. The nuance is a little different in English and Japanese. Would it make more sense if I called it a deduction game or a criminal investigation game? You roleplay as a detective or a cop and try to identify the culprit, like in a mystery.''

``Identify the culprit\dots\ and the clues for that are hidden in the exam questions?''

I could hardly believe clues for identifying a murderer would be hidden in a booklet that looked like a normal exam handout. When I turned to Mikage, who was reading hers at that very moment, she held the booklet out to me.

``There aren't any direct clues, but there are three math and science problems in here. It looks like two of the answers will come out as numerical values.''

``Numerical values? How are those supposed to point us to the checkpoints?''

While Watari kept grumbling, I rummaged through the backpack we'd been given. There was a large map inside. When I unfolded it, I saw that it covered the entire Tsunanagai City area.

I wondered whether numbers were written at the checkpoints. As I scanned it wide-eyed---

``Found them. There are suspicious numbers written in the margins of the map.''

Meaningful-looking numbers like $\frac{1}{4}$ or $\sqrt{2}$ were written along the map's vertical north-south axis and horizontal east-west axis. Seeing that, Watari muttered.

``So the system is that solving the problems gives us the values that reveal where we're supposed to go?''

``Wait a second. This is the exam from the 13th, so we're supposed to treat it as the exam handed out during the Science Dept Orientation in a world where a second-year named E-mi died...?''

As my thoughts started to tangle, Watari-kun calmly nodded at my question.

``That's right. This exam is a story within the story. The place where E died is one of the checkpoints, so we won't know where it is unless we solve this. Since there are three questions, there are probably two other checkpoints with evidence or something like it left behind.''

``Evidence at the other checkpoints too? Why would you think that?''

``That's just how these games work. It'd be stupid if all the evidence were in one place, wouldn't it?''

``Huh? What do you mean, stupid?''

As we bickered, an announcement rang out through the audiovisual room.

【Whoa, Team X has already jumped into a heated debate! No, is it a quarrel?】

Before I knew it, the camera was filming us from the side while we argued. Maybe because he wanted to look good on camera, Watari-kun fell silent, swallowing the retort that had been on the tip of his tongue. The camera panned down to the handouts in our hands.

I could feel the upperclassmen in the room reacting. Their eyes were fixed on the screen. When I looked back, the full text of 【Report and Proposal regarding the ``Science Dept Orientation Murder Incident''】 was being projected there. Apparently, this was the first time the upperclassmen were seeing that document too.

【Game Master Hongo's surprise has exploded! The first task is, of all things, a murder case!】

``Why don't we start by splitting up the exam questions and solving them?'' Mikage suggested, ignoring the announcement. I had no problem with that. I started reading from the beginning.

\begin{center}
\textbf{Question 1}
\end{center}

{\bfseries
There is a bowl in the shape of a hemisphere with radius $1$, with the vertex as the base. The rim of the bowl is fixed horizontally, and water is filled to a height where the distance to the plane formed by the rim is $\frac{\sqrt{3}}{3}$. Determine how much of the length of a straight rod of length $2$ can be submerged in this water. The thickness of the bowl and the rod may be ignored.
}

It looked hopeless from the very start. I tried picturing the setup, but I couldn't make sense of it at all. A rod with length $2$ wouldn't fit all the way inside the bowl. That was because it was the same length as the rim's diameter. If one end were aimed at the bottom and tilted the right way, part of it would probably be submerged. But how much of it would that be? More than that, where had the number$\frac{\sqrt{3}}{3}$ even come from? Was it one of those values chosen to make the answer come out neatly?

Watari-kun was glaring at the problem too, his expression grim.

``This is basically more math than physics. You'd probably set up an equation with the rod's angle as a variable, use trigonometric functions, and then differentiate it, but I'm not confident I can solve it cleanly.''

``Leave this to me. I solved a similar problem ages ago. It was the first question on the 2012 University of Tokyo science-math exam. I don't remember the answer, obviously... but give me fifteen---no, ten minutes, and I can work it out.''

Mikage rummaged through the backpack and pulled out a clear folder containing copy paper and a pencil.

``Seriously? That's incredible.''

If even Watari-kun sounded impressed, Mikage had to be the real deal. To begin with, I didn't even understand what it meant to have solved a university entrance exam problem ages ago. Resigned to being the one left behind, I moved on to the next problem.

Question 2 on the next page was obviously chemistry, and Question 3 on the page after that was obviously biology. Either of those looked solvable in ten minutes. There was just one problem.

``I need some way to check a codon table. I think there was one posted outside the biology room, but if I stop working in the meantime, I'll lose too much time. Can I leave Question 2 to Watari-kun for now?''

``Got it. Then I'll leave Question 3 to you.''

I'd checked the clock while nodding, so I knew only about three minutes had passed since the start. Which was exactly why the words from the next table stunned me.

``Solved it. Time's precious. We're leaving.''

The one who said it while briskly folding up the exam paper was Togakushi-kun, his ghostly white hair standing out as ever.

\textit{What on earth could he possibly have solved in three minutes?}

While I stood there in a daze, the three members of Team Y gathered their things and walked out of the audiovisual room.

$\gamma$

The plan had been for Hijiri-kun and me to check the contents of the backpack while Togakushi-kun solved the exam questions. So I was shocked when he said ``Solved it'' before we'd even finished checking the supplies.

\textit{No matter how you looked at it, that was way too fast!}

I stuffed the things spread out on the table back into the backpack, and Hijiri-kun swung it over his shoulder. Meanwhile, Togakushi-kun snatched up the map from the desk, kept it together with the exam questions, and headed straight for the exit. The two of us hurried after him as he strode up the aisle without even looking back.

``I just want to check the codon table. Was there anything in the supplies that looked like it might have it?'' Togakushi-kun asked as we stepped out of the audiovisual room. Among the things in the backpack, the only items that looked useful for solving the problems were paper, a pencil, and an eraser. But---

``Yeah. I've got the codon table memorized. It starts with AUG---the start codon, methionine.''

Hijiri-kun said that before I could even point out that one was posted on the whiteboard in front of the biology room, which left me twice as shocked. \textit{A codon table is basically a codebook used when proteins are made from genetic information; it shows which amino acids correspond to sets of three bases chosen from A (Adenine), U (Uracil), C (Cytosine), and G (Guanine). There are 64 possible combinations and 20 kinds of amino acids. Did he really have all of that memorized?}

``Then I'll leave the decoding to you. We're leaving the school and making our move. The place from Question 1 is pretty far away.''

Togakushi-kun showed us the map while continuing to stride briskly toward the entrance.

``Wait. How did you figure out where to go from that problem?''

The question Hijiri-kun asked---the very same one I was wondering---clearly struck Togakushi-kun as a hassle.

``Multiply the vertical and horizontal axes.''

Apparently, he thought that was explanation enough. Numerical values had been written in the margins of the map of the entire Tsunanagai City area. Togakushi-kun pointed to the intersection of $1/3$ on the map's horizontal axis and $\sqrt{3}$ on its vertical one. Multiply those two, and you got $\sqrt{3}/3$. Was that the answer to Question 1?

``I see. This place is the Kannon Caves. Even by bus, it'll take about twenty-five minutes from the school.''

So we were taking the bus. I detached one of the transit pass holders from the backpack Hijiri-kun was carrying.

``If we're taking the city bus, there's a one-day city pass in here. Looks like it gives us unlimited rides.''

``The standard strategy is to deal with the troublesome part first. We'll head to those Kannon Caves or whatever they're called first.''

Togakushi-kun made the call immediately. Hijiri-kun checked the wristwatch attached to the backpack and offered a suggestion.

``There's a bus that works perfectly. If we hurry and catch the one leaving the stop in front of the school at 10:08, we can get to the Kannon Caves directly. We'll get there a little after 10:30.''

``Seriously?''

``Of course I'm serious. There's definitely a bus for Oku-Tsunanagai leaving at 10:08.''

\textit{I wondered if Hijiri-kun had the transit schedule memorized too\dots}

Changing into sneakers at the entrance, we ran down the ginkgo-lined path and out past the school gate. The two camera crew members hurried after us. We had barely reached the bus stop when a bus came up the road.

Bound for Oku-Tsunanagai. It was the very bus that went past the Kannon Caves.

``Whoa! That's amazing!''

Hijiri-kun shot me a satisfied smile when I blurted that out without thinking.

``When I say `definitely,' I mean definitely.''

$\delta$

For a few seconds, Watari and I stared at the door Team Y had gone out through, probably both wearing idiotic expressions. The only sound was Mikage's pencil racing across the copy paper.

``What does he mean, `Solved it'? It's only been three minutes.''

``It's a bluff, right? They probably left early to rattle us, then figured they'd solve it on the move. It's not like they have to solve everything here. They still need to go somewhere to check a codon table too.''

The scratching of the pencil stopped abruptly. Mikage nodded to us.

``I think Delta-kun is right. We should work through the problems at our own pace first.''

``Right. I've copied down the base sequence. I'll go check it against the chart outside the biology room.''

I grabbed the sheet of copy paper where I'd written down the necessary parts of Question 3 and ran up the aisle.

\begin{center}
\textbf{Question 3}
\end{center}

\textbf{The DNA sequence shown below corresponds to an exon. Decode it.}

\fullpageimage{7.jpg}

\thispagestyle{plain}
\vspace{1cm}

An exon is the part of a DNA base sequence that serves as the blueprint for making proteins. There is also another part called an intron, which gets removed in a process called splicing before translation, but we didn't need to worry about that for this task.

In other words, all I had to do was read and decipher the DNA sequence shown in the diagram.

The problem was figuring out where to start reading and in which direction. The genetic code uses three bases to specify one amino acid, but if the starting position is off by even one base, the result changes completely. So what I needed to look for was the start codon---the sequence that marks where translation begins.

Since the start codon in messenger RNA (mRNA) is ``AUG,'' it would be ``ATG'' in the original DNA, where Uracil (U) is replaced by Thymine (T). Also, because translation proceeds from the 5$'$ end to the 3$'$ end of the mRNA, that sequence simply had to appear in that direction on the sense strand of the original DNA---the meaningful side of the double helix. Sure enough, there was only one such sequence in the diagram.

There was indeed a codon table posted in front of the biology room. But there was no sign of Team Y. \textit{Had they really finished the decoding in that split second, gone somewhere else to find a codon table, or---}

Hijiri's face suddenly flashed through my mind. \textit{Ah. That had to be it. That was exactly the kind of thing he'd do.}

\textit{Just because he was a Physics Club member aiming for law school didn't mean that ridiculous genius wouldn't have a reason to memorize a codon table. And with Iwama there too, there was no way they wouldn't have thought to look for the start codon on the DNA double strand in the right direction and translate from there.}

``Dammit,'' I muttered under my breath as I kept decoding the DNA sequence. Amino acids have abbreviations; for example, Methionine, which is specified by the AUG start codon, is written as ``Met'' or ``M.'' This time, I assumed I was supposed to string together the single-letter symbols.

The next one after Methionine was ``ACA,'' which meant Threonine, ``T.'' The next was ``CAC,'' which meant Histidine, ``H.'' ``CGG'' was Arginine, ``R.'' ``GAA'' was Glutamic acid, ``E.'' The next one was ``E'' too.

THREE\dots\dots If I excluded the ``M'' for Methionine, which had to be there because of the start codon, it looked like it would form an English word. The genetic code also contains sequences called stop codons---``UAA,'' ``UAG,'' and ``UGA''---which I'd memorized with a mnemonic that sounded like a scream when someone gets hit: ``Uaaa, uagh, uga,'' and translation stops when it reaches one of them.

When I finally reached the corresponding ``TAA''---since this was DNA, the U became a T---the string of letters I got definitely seemed meaningful.

\begin{center}
THREEQTRS
\end{center}

I wondered what QTR meant. It didn't seem like it meant Qatar. I was pretty sure there weren't three Qatars. Time was too precious to waste on that, so I ran back to the audiovisual room.

Beside Team Y's empty desk, Mikage was staring intently at the map, while Watari-kun was still wrestling with a problem. The moment I got there, Mikage spoke up.

``Sorry I'm late. The answer is $\frac{\sqrt{3}}{3}$. If you want to get that from the numbers written on the map, the only possible combination uses $\frac{1}{3}$. Take one from the vertical axis and one from the horizontal, and the coordinates point to the Kannon Caves.''

The copy paper Mikage had been using was filled with graphs of circles intersecting straight lines, along with sines, cosines, and tangents. I was genuinely glad I hadn't been the one stuck solving that.

``Thanks\dots\dots In that case, the answer to Question 3 should be a numerical value too.''

When I showed Mikage ``THREEQTRS,'' Watari-kun leaned over from the side.

``Oh, `three quarters'---$\frac{3}{4}$, huh?''

So QTR didn't mean Qatar at all, but ``quarter,'' as in one-fourth. \textit{Come to think of it, there aren't that many words starting with Q, so I should've realized it myself.}

``So the checkpoint is at the intersection of 3 and $\frac{1}{4}$.''

I said that with the kind of look that implied I'd known it all along, and Mikage quickly found the spot and pointed to it.

``The West Tunnel. It's on the side where the coastal bypass heads toward Koshizaki.''

``Right. What about you, Watari-kun? Did you solve yours?''

After hesitating for less than a second, Watari-kun tugged on my sleeve with a frustrated look on his face.

``Help me out here, ex-Chemistry boy.''

\begin{center}
\textbf{Question 2}
\end{center}

\textbf{The number of structural isomers for an alkane with carbon count $a$ is 18. The minimum carbon count $b$ for an alkane to have exactly 10 stereoisomers is $b$. Find $\frac{a}{b}$.}

The problem Watari-kun was working on was about alkane isomers.

``Alkane'' is the general term for hydrocarbons made up only of single bonds between carbon and hydrogen, represented by the formula $\mathrm{C}_n\mathrm{H}_{2n+2}$. Even people unfamiliar with organic chemistry have probably heard of methane ($\mathrm{CH}_4$) or propane ($\mathrm{C}_3\mathrm{H}_8$). As the number of carbons in an alkane increases, the number of ways those carbons can connect multiplies, causing the number of ``isomers''---substances with the same molecular formula but different properties---to explode. Of these, ``structural isomers'' are ones with different carbon skeletons, while ``stereoisomers'' are ones with the same connections but different three-dimensional arrangements, such as mirror images of each other.

``I think $a$ is probably 8, but what does it mean for there to be exactly ten stereoisomers? You can't get 10 just by raising two to the number of chiral centers.''

``You'll get it if you think it through. The number goes down if there's a plane of symmetry in the molecule. Don't you even know what a meso compound is?''

``Why the hell would I know that as a first-year in high school?''

\textit{I felt like that applied to this entire Science Dept Orientation in general, but I let it slide.}

``You just need to make one plane of symmetry and place two chiral centers on either side of it. Then all you have to do is find the smallest number of carbons needed to create chirality.''

Since I was dealing with Watari-kun, I explained it without holding back, even as the venue commentary started making a fuss beside us.

【As a lowly Physics Club member, I have absolutely no idea what they're talking about!】

【To give a brief explanation, the `chirality' they're mentioning refers to a state where four different things are bonded to the four arms extending from a single carbon atom---】

Watari-kun clicked his tongue loudly, probably finding the commentary annoying, and then worked out the answer.

``$b$ is 12. The answer to Question 2 is $\frac{2}{3}$. There really are ten stereoisomers if you take symmetry into account.''

``Right. Then the location is---''

``Tsunanagai Station. It's exactly at the intersection of 2 and $\frac{1}{3}$.''

Mikage immediately gave us the answer we needed. Normally, I would've found her presence incredibly reassuring, but we were obviously behind Team Y, so we didn't have the luxury of relaxing.

``That's everything solved. Let's head out.''

Watari-kun started stuffing the things on the desk into the backpack as if it were the most obvious thing in the world.

I checked the clock. 10:14. It was nothing compared to Team Y leaving in three minutes, but I decided to be satisfied with having kept the gap to eleven minutes.

We'd solved the problems, but the real race started here.

$\gamma$

``The next bus isn't for another two hours. Izuta and the others will probably want to take it, but if they do, they'll end up breaking the lunch-break rule. Hongo-senpai is pretty nasty. If they take too long on the exam, the only bus left for them will be the one after that. And since there isn't a convenient one for the return trip, they'll have to walk part of the way.''

When we got to the Kannon Caves bus stop, Hijiri-kun cheerfully sized up the situation while looking at the timetable. A bus would be coming in thirty minutes that could take us back to the city, but since Del-chan and the others had missed the 10:08 bus, it looked like getting back from this checkpoint would be really rough for them.

\dots\dots Actually, wasn't Togakushi-kun the abnormal one for solving those problems in just three minutes? Wasn't everyone actually supposed to be taking the same bus in the afternoon?

``Let's go.''

Looking like he didn't want to waste even a second on small talk, Togakushi-kun started walking along the road.

The Kannon Caves bus stop sat partway along a road that ran from the city center toward Oku-Tsunanagai and into the mountains. The road ran alongside a deeply cut river and was surrounded by nothing but dense green trees.

``Once we're done here, we'll check the station next, hit the tunnel last, and then head back. Sound good?''

``Okay.''

Togakushi-kun accepted the plan Hijiri-kun and I had worked out on the bus with two syllables. He'd spent the entire ride asleep, claiming he'd get carsick otherwise.

We'd solved the genetic code from Question 3 on the bus with Hijiri-kun's help. He really did have the entire codon table memorized, which I still found a little ridiculous, so we were able to work out the answer right away. Hijiri-kun even claimed to have memorized the timetables for the major bus stops in the city, which was getting hard to believe at this point, and said our team would be able to get back to school on a comfortable schedule.

All that was left was to find out what was waiting for us at the checkpoints.

When I spotted a Tsunanagai High School uniform farther down the road, I became sure that Togakushi-kun's answer to Question 1 had been correct. Truthfully, Togakushi-kun's intermediate steps were such a complicated mess that I couldn't read them at all, so I had no idea how he'd arrived at that answer.

``Oh, Gamma-san! Hey!''

One of the students in uniform was Mizasaki-kun, waving cheerfully at us.

It looked like the Kannon Caves were across a suspension bridge off the road. On the other side of the bridge was a small clearing with a tarp tent set up in it. Mizasaki-kun, who had been waiting for us in front of the suspension bridge, came running over as if he couldn't wait any longer.

``I saw you heading this way on the broadcast, Gamma-san. You don't need tea yet, do you? But please put on some insect repellent before you cross the bridge. There are tons of mosquitoes since we're near the water.''

``Thank you!''

After taking the insect repellent, I had Togakushi-kun and Hijiri-kun stand still so I could spray wherever they wanted. Since I was wearing a skirt, I made sure to protect my own legs too.

Mizasaki-kun took the spray back and hurried across the suspension bridge toward the tent. The reason became obvious right away. On the other side of the bridge, the camera crew waiting at the checkpoint had already taken up a position to catch us head-on. They'd probably decided on the angle ahead of time.

Feeling a little self-conscious, I let Togakushi-kun go first and crossed the suspension bridge after him. Togakushi-kun crossed the bridge looking completely indifferent to the camera. Behind me, Hijiri-kun was smiling and waving at the camera, but I figured it was probably better not to do that.

Once we finished crossing the bridge, a second-year student who had been watching a monitor from a folding chair under the tarp tent showed us a large board. The instructions for what we had to do at this location were written on it.

Inside the square area measuring 50 meters East of this tent and 25 meters North and South respectively, there are exactly the listed numbers of mature trees of the following species:


$\cdot$ Arakashi / Quercus glauca (3 trees)

$\cdot$ Shirakashi / Quercus myrsinifolia (4 trees)

Choose one species and find the centroid of the shape formed by the points at the bases of those trees. The investigation documents containing the clue are located there.

※ There are two identical investigation documents, printed front and back, so please take only one.

Great Detective Hongo Nagisa

``Interesting. They've placed a biology problem at the end of a math problem. In other words, the system is designed to make things difficult if you split up and act independently.''

While Hijiri-kun was voicing his admiration, Togakushi-kun came back carrying a shovel from somewhere---a full-sized one you hold with both hands, called a ``scoop'' in Eastern Japan and a ``shovel'' in Western Japan. Looking closer, I saw a blue tarp spread out in one corner of the tent, with ropes, pegs, and other tools laid out on top of it.

``Which one is the Arakashi?''

Togakushi-kun asked listlessly.

``Oh, I know that one! Hang on, I'll find it...''

I figured it would be easier to find them myself than try to explain them out loud. Arakashi was one of the trees Del-chan had taught me during Golden Week. Since it was an evergreen, its leaves were thick and glossy. They were almost elliptical, with serrated edges toward the tip, and they were often widest near the end. They also produced acorns.

First, I started walking around, scanning the ground for Arakashi leaves.

``Found one!''

I spotted the leaf I was looking for almost immediately. There was a tree right nearby too. Hijiri-kun came running over.

``This is an Arakashi? Amazing. Fallen leaves all look the same to me.''

I almost said that I used to be the same until Del-chan taught me, but I stopped myself.

``The shapes are a little different. These get broader toward the end, and the outline near the tip is jagged.''

``I see. Now that you mention it. Should I look for trees with the same leaves on them too?''

``Yeah! Please.''

Hijiri-kun and I ran through the woods searching for the other two. Meanwhile, Togakushi-kun wandered around aimlessly with the shovel dangling from one hand. Maybe he just wasn't very interested in searching for trees.

``Found one! This is it!''

Almost at the exact moment Hijiri-kun shouted, I found the third one.

``Over here too!''

Then, out of nowhere, Togakushi-kun, who had been wandering around aimlessly, drove the shovel into the ground with a thud.

``I'm digging.''

``Wait, but we still haven't found the centroid...''

``This is the centroid.''

Apparently deciding it was a waste of time to explain, Togakushi-kun started digging into the ground without another word. Hijiri-kun and I ran back over to him.

``You mean you were figuring out the centroid while we were out looking for the trees?''

``Exactly. If it's a triangle, you just find the intersection of the medians. The soil's soft here.''

Before my brain could catch up, Togakushi-kun dug up a Ziploc bag with a piece of paper inside. The nearby camera crew and Mizasaki-kun, who was watching from behind them, stared in shock.

Just what you'd expect from the top student in our grade. Togakushi-kun was fast at everything he did.

The square sheet of paper he pulled from the Ziploc bag looked like more investigation material.

\begin{quote}
Let me introduce the suspects' personal belongings. This information has been reliably confirmed.

\noindent $\blacksquare$ A-suke: A black instant camera. A so-called Cheki. On the day of the incident, he carried it around with him and took photos of his friends. There is a printing defect, and every photo has three white spots on the right side.

\noindent $\blacksquare$ B-ko: A red-and-white amulet. Handmade by her mother and knitted with red and white yarn. Small items can be placed inside. B-ko carried it with her at all times, not just on the day of the incident, and no one else knew about it.

There are also items left behind at the far end of the scaffold in front of the Kannon Caves, so be sure to check them.

\begin{flushright}
Great Detective Hongo Nagisa
\end{flushright}
\end{quote}

``This is the murder scene! We struck gold right away.''

``Is there anything on the back?''
