``I'm not suspecting him. I just want to keep track of everyone's movements for now.''

\textit{Words straight out of a detective drama came out of my own mouth.}

``I guess that's fine. Kurauchi-san brought lunch by car and stayed with us the whole time after that. As for the other guests, Bakuma-san came to Kannon-kutsu with us that morning and gave the scaffolding a final check before things started. He was the one who had it set up, after all.''

``Bakuma-san had it set up? That scaffolding?''

``Yeah. He's in construction, so this kind of thing is nothing new to him. But suspecting Bakuma-san would be barking up the wrong tree. Even when that Hijiri guy was stomping and jumping all over it while Team Y crossed, the scaffolding didn't fall. If Bakuma-san, who was only there in the morning, had rigged something, it should've collapsed while Hijiri was on it, right?''

The only guests outside should've been Bakuma-san and Kurauchi-san. Bakuma-san visited Kannon-kutsu before the game started and after the scaffolding fell. Kurauchi-san was around that area from noon until it fell. Team Y had crossed the scaffolding before it collapsed, and there hadn't been any problems at that point.

\textit{If I were to take the murder threat at face value and suspect the guests, Kurauchi-san would be the most suspicious. Of course, I couldn't say anything for certain without looking into what had caused the scaffolding to fall, but still\dots}

``You're overthinking it, Delta. It's true the safety precautions were sloppy, but there's no point in pinning the blame on anyone. Next is the second task. On the school grounds at 17:00. Make sure you get some proper rest until then.''

I watched Mizasaki walk away after giving my shoulder a gentle pat, unable to say a word.

\textit{First, I wanted to talk to Hijiri.}

$\gamma$

Togakushi-kun was sleeping in one of the beds in the nurse's office. It wasn't because he was especially unwell; apparently, he used it pretty often. I had suggested that Del-chan sleep in the nurse's office too, but looking thoroughly exhausted, he had flopped down on the floor the moment he entered the waiting room without even wiping off his sweat.

``Isn't the floor hard?''

``The heat conductivity is just right.''

Del-chan answered in a limp, weak voice, wearing an expression he didn't usually show. \textit{This was probably what he was like with his family at home.}

``Are you okay? It might be heatstroke.''

``It's not that\dots\dots I just like lying on the floor.''

Del-chan closed his eyelids right in front of me. \textit{He must have been terribly tired.}

``It was tough, wasn't it? The first task.''

``Yeah\dots\dots Sounds like Iwama and the others did pretty well.''

He was speaking with his eyes closed. It almost sounded like he was talking in his sleep.

``That's right! Hijiri-kun and Togakushi-kun were amazing. Everything went so smoothly, even though I didn't do anything.''

``Iwama was the one who found the ring-cup oak, wasn't she?''

After hearing that, I couldn't find the words for a while. Aside from when we'd run into each other in front of the station, we'd spent the whole time apart, and yet Del-chan had still been thinking about me even though I was on a different team.

``\dots\dots That's right. Because Del-chan taught me about it. Who would've thought it would come in handy here?''

He didn't answer. I saw that he was breathing with a regular rhythm.

Even with a girl sitting right beside him, he was utterly defenseless.

We were the only two left in the room, but I looked around anyway just to be safe, cleared my throat loudly to make sure Del-chan was really asleep, and then gently removed his glasses.

\textit{I just thought it might be dangerous if he rolled over with his glasses on. It's not like I particularly wanted to see his sleeping face without them.} That's why I immediately stood up and set the glasses on the desk. Then I noticed several disposable wet wipes left on the table.

Delta still had beads of sweat on his face. \textit{On impulse,} I pulled a wipe from the pack and crouched down again. \textit{If the sweat dried like that, it'd feel sticky and gross when he woke up. I wiped the sweat from his face and neck purely out of kindness.}

\dots\dots What was I even doing?

\textit{I came to my senses.} I threw the wet wipe into the trash like I was disposing of evidence and left the waiting room. The other selected members, aside from Togakushi-kun, should have been in the audiovisual room. I wasn't entirely sure, but apparently they were serving some kind of fancy drink there.

When I went to the audiovisual room, Hijiri-kun, Mikage-san, and Watari-kun were swirling wine glasses alongside Hongo-senpai and Claire-san. Since this was a high school, the red liquid in their glasses probably wasn't actually wine.

I heard most of the guests had already gone home, and everyone was finishing off the drinks that had been served earlier. Hongo-senpai poured me some grape juice as well. It wasn't from concentrate, but 100\% straight juice made from domestically grown Kyoho grapes.

``Oh? Sho's not coming?''

Seeing that I had come alone, Claire-san pointed it out. She was seated right next to Hijiri-kun. It really did seem true that she liked boys with glasses. She was clearly the type to be honest about what she liked.

``He seemed tired, so he's sleeping.''

``Goodness, that's a real shame.''

Claire-san resumed her conversation with Hijiri-kun. She looked like she was having a great time. She was leaning her bare shoulder against him as if the age gap meant nothing at all. If she did that to a subordinate at her company, she'd probably be facing disciplinary action for sexual harassment. Hijiri-kun didn't seem to mind, and unlike Del-chan, he didn't look flustered in the slightest. \textit{I found myself thinking it might be easier if Hijiri-kun just accepted all of her so-called ``fetishes.''}

``Sorry, Rio-chi. I stuck you in a pretty difficult group.''

Hongo-senpai spoke to me with a bottle of grape juice in hand.

``Difficult?''

``Yeah. Those two guys really didn't get along, did they? Even though their abilities make them a perfect match. I didn't mean for it to turn out that way, but I ended up making Rio-chi play the go-between.''

``No, not at all. I didn't see it that way.''

``Really? Well, if that's how you see it.''

After topping off my glass, senpai headed over to Mikage-san and Watari-kun. The two members of Team X looked deep in thought as they studied those square investigation sheets. Team Y had also noticed it. Written on the backs of those three sheets were messages that didn't seem to have anything to do with the `Science Department Orientation Murder Case'.

Since we were on opposing teams, it'd probably just be a nuisance if I joined in. Since there was no point in standing there drinking juice by myself, I drifted over toward Hijiri-kun and Claire-san.

I wondered what those two were getting along so well talking about, only to find they were deep in a high-level discussion about the situation in America. Hijiri-kun really knew everything. Apparently, things are expected to get pretty turbulent when the president changes next year. Hijiri-kun rattled on at top speed, saying that if the administration changed, major shifts in immigration and tariff policy would be unavoidable; students hoping to become researchers might have to rethink where they studied abroad, manufacturers might be forced to make major changes to their export businesses, and even science-track high school students needed to keep a close eye on America. Claire-san seemed knowledgeable about that sort of thing too, and she was actively keeping up with him.

\textit{This was a little different from what I had imagined. Maybe it wasn't so much that Hijiri-kun had a thing against women, but that he was simply the type to keep talking about whatever interested him no matter who he was talking to. \dots That made it hard to join in.}

``Iwama-san, you don't dislike peaches, do you?''

Just as my discomfort was about to hit its limit, Hijiri-kun turned around as if he had eyes in the back of his head. He held a bottle of peach juice in his hand. The glass I'd been sipping from just to give myself something to do had just run dry.

``Not at all. May I have some?''

``Of course. If I drink too much of it, my mouth starts to itch.''

Taking him up on the offer, I stepped closer, and Hijiri-kun trickled just a tiny bit of juice into my glass before stopping. As I stared at him in surprise, wondering what kind of joke this was, he tilted his head.

``Oh. I thought everyone in the sciences did a rinse first.''

That was a stereotype. Rinsing, or conditioning, is a procedure used in things like neutralization titrations, where you wash the equipment with the solution you're about to use next. It's done to keep the concentration from being altered by water droplets or other factors, but apparently there are some people in this world who do the same thing even with drinks. My father also always rinses his sake cup when drinking different types of Japanese sake. But not everyone in the sciences does that sort of thing. I'm the kind of person who doesn't care if a little Kyoho grape juice gets mixed into my peach juice.

``Only some people do.''

While saying that, I drained the little bit of juice he'd poured me and held out my glass again. Hijiri-kun refilled it with peach juice, looking satisfied. He had the label facing up. It was a perfectly science-track sort of gesture.

From there, I got drawn into the conversation, and the three of us spent a while lively discussing the situation in America. Before I knew it, the mystery written on the backs of those papers was still unsolved, and it was already nearly 16:00.

What made me look at the clock was Bakuma-san, one of the guests, walking into the audiovisual room carrying a sliced watermelon. His business attire and the watermelon on the tray were a bit of an odd combination.

``I've been handing it out to the management team too. Mikage-kun told me there were members in here as well.''

It was a seedless watermelon. Since it was easy to eat in a setting like this, I was grateful. Everyone broke off their conversations, gathered around Bakuma-san, and gratefully took a slice.

I was surprised the moment I took a bite. It was nicely chilled and sweeter than any watermelon I'd ever had before.

``Delicious!''

``My family grows watermelons and melons back home. They send them to me, so I always have more than enough to share.''

As Bakuma-san watched us eat the watermelon with a pleased expression, Hijiri-kun asked him,

``Where's your family home?''

``Oh. It's in Shikoku.''

``Then it's either Ehime or Kochi... and if your family grows melons too, could it be Kochi?''

Bakuma-san's eyes widened in surprise.

``How did you know?''

``No. I just went with the place that seemed most likely based on production volume. It's very good. And nicely chilled too.''

``Oh, so this was the top-secret cargo Bakuma-san was talking about!''

When Claire-san said that, I wondered what she meant, and Bakuma-san smiled bashfully.

``That's right. In a cooler. I was worried because the inside of the car gets hot, but I'm glad everyone liked it. Watermelon definitely tastes better cold.''

For some reason, Hijiri-kun seemed especially interested in Bakuma-san and asked another question.

``Judging by the curve of the rind, that must've been a pretty big watermelon. Did you fit that large a cooler into your Panamera?''

``You notice the strangest things. That car actually has a lot of room. Or rather, you even noticed that? It's a little embarrassing for a show-off like me.''

Even as he called it embarrassing, Bakuma-san looked happy to have a chance to talk about his car.

\textit{I was certain.}

\textit{This was Hijiri-kun's conversational skill.}

\textit{Drawing fully on his vast store of knowledge, he brought up America for Claire-san and fruit or cars for Bakuma-san, steering the conversation toward topics each of them would enjoy.}

\textit{That was how he won people over.}

\textit{I ought to learn from him.}

``I heard the Panamera got a real workout. The ride quality must be way too good for a bunch of high schoolers.''

``Not at all. If anything, it's too big for a town like this. There wasn't even anywhere to park it in front of Kannon-kutsu. Still, I'm glad if the kids enjoyed it.''

``Does that mean you went to Kannon-kutsu too, Bakuma-san?''

``Well, yeah. I was the one who arranged the construction, after all. I went there this morning, and since the Panamera was too big, I figured I'd ask Kurauchi-kun to handle anything that came up, but then I got a call saying the scaffolding had collapsed or something. In the end, I had to park in an empty lot a few hundred meters away and make the trip on foot twice.''

Hearing that, maybe it was just my imagination, but Hijiri-kun's glasses seemed to glint.

$\gamma$

That person was irritated by the unexpected interference.

They never thought they would fail.

It was supposed to be a perfect plan.

How on earth could something like that happen by chance?

I have to cause another incident somehow.

An incident that will bring the Science Department Orientation to ruin by tomorrow---

$\delta$

``Did you solve the Golden Egg code?''

I had been sleeping facedown on the desk in the waiting room when Hijiri's voice woke me. Since I still had my glasses on this time, I knew the time right away. 16:00.

``What's a Golden Egg?''

``Oh. Have you never read Harry Potter, Izuta?''

``I read it a long time ago, but what about the Golden Egg?''

``If you haven't solved it, then never mind. By the way, I just heard about it. The scaffolding incident.''

Hijiri pointed toward a corner of the meeting room. The two of us went over, dragged a few chairs into an empty corner by the wall, and sat down side by side. According to Hijiri, ``No one will overhear us from outside here, and no one will be able to plant a wiretap,'' but \textit{I wondered whether it was really necessary to be that cautious inside the school.}

``It's okay. You have nothing to worry about. I'm here.''

Hijiri casually spoke words that only a hero could say. But those groundless words were strangely reassuring.

``First, tell me everything. Let's think about this together.''

Prompted by him, I placed my hands on my knees, lowered my gaze a little, and quietly told him what had been bothering me. After listening in silence for a while and giving a few nods, Hijiri spoke in a serious tone, still sitting in the same posture with his head slightly lowered.

``I feel exactly the same way, Izuta. We can't afford to take the scaffolding incident lightly. It's a malicious act, and we need to face it with the utmost caution. We have to prevent any further crimes from happening, and if possible, I want to identify the culprit as soon as we can.''

``\dots\dots It's just like a mystery novel.''

Words that sounded like they belonged in a mystery novel had slipped out of my own mouth.

``You're right. The contents of that card have started to feel all too real.''

Hijiri's words brought back the memory of that black card the two of us had received.

---Beware the Science Dept Ori. There is a fake among the guests.

---Find the fake secretly so that no one notices.

``Is that really an accusation? If so, why was it written in such a vague way?''

``Who sent it, and why? Does the sender know who the culprit is, or is the sender the culprit, trying to issue a murder threat?...''

Hijiri thought for a moment before continuing.

``I'm sure it's connected to the T-incident. But I can't make sense of the intent. Is it meant as a provocation, or a distraction? Since we can't trust it, we have no choice but to set it aside for now. Let's just keep in mind that the GW matter may be affecting this case.''

\textit{That warning letter had been sent specifically to Hijiri and me, strongly calling back to the Tengu Festival Incident during Golden Week. But it wouldn't be good to narrow our focus by worrying only about the guests because of that. Still, it was hard to ignore. It was a real nuisance.}

``Isn't there a chance Hongo-senpai planned something and sent us that card?''

``I looked into that too, but based on their alibis, it seems Hongo-senpai and Mikage-senpai couldn't have planted the cards in our luggage. On the Saturday we received them, preparations for the Science Dept Ori were already in full swing. Apparently, they were at school the whole time with the Science Department management team.''

``Is that really an airtight alibi? Maybe they had someone else do it.''

``If we had a hula hoop from the future, we could probably break that alibi.''

\textit{Hijiri probably thought he was being clever, but I wasn't in the mood for it right then.}

``Jokes aside, if they got Mikage-san involved, it might be possible. But it's hard to imagine those upperclassmen pulling in someone who doesn't know the truth of the T-incident.''

``True. If we go down that route, asking Mikage might settle it.''

\textit{Mikage had been present at the scene of the scaffolding incident. She should understand the gravity of the situation. If she knew anything about that card, she would surely tell us the truth.}

``Now then, Izuta, shall we finally get to the heart of the matter? The scaffolding collapse incident. The strangest thing about it, more than anything else, is how closely it resembles the murder case in the mystery game Hongo-senpai presented.''

``And apparently, only a handful of people knew what was in that game until 10:00 today.''

``In that case, you'd naturally want to suspect Hongo-senpai, but the first thing I want to make clear is that Hongo-senpai herself is acting as though she knows nothing about the scaffolding collapse. I haven't had a chance to question her yet, but at the very least, she's behaving as if she has nothing to do with it.''

``Besides, there'd be no benefit to sabotaging the scaffolding in the first place. If the Science Dept Ori fails, the ones who lose out are Mikage-senpai and Hongo-senpai, since they'd lose the sponsorships they were supposed to get.''

``That's an important point. So here too, just like with the warning letter, let's set Hongo-senpai's involvement aside for now. If she really was involved, it'll all come out on its own without us forcing the issue.''

\textit{Talking with Hijiri made me feel like my thoughts were falling into place better than when I was worrying on my own.} I said my thoughts out loud.

``Did someone deliberately cause an incident to mimic the game, or was the resemblance just a coincidence? If it's the former, why?''

``It would be pretty foolish if someone got inspired by the game, thought, `So that's one way to do it!', and then immediately went and committed the crime.''

``On the other hand, what if the resemblance itself was the point? By making it look like the game, they could make people think it was part of the event.''

``That does seem likely. In fact, even though Izuta could've died if things had gone just a little worse, almost no one is treating that incident seriously. Even I didn't hear about it until just now.''

\textit{I remembered the tone Mizasaki had used. There had been far too great a gap between the way we reacted.}

\textit{If that was the culprit's goal.}

``It's still only speculation, but let's assume that's why it was made to resemble the game... the problem is, who planned something like that? If they're planning anything else, we have to stop them.''

``For now, I've secured some physical evidence that may serve as a clue. It seems a contractor already removed the scaffolding, including the floorboards Bakuma-san recovered, but I've arranged to have it all set aside. If there are any traces of tampering left, that'll be evidence.''

``Just what I'd expect from you. You move fast. Can we check it soon?''

``Hard to say. It had already been transported away. If I push for it, I might be able to have it brought to the school, but that'd probably turn into a major ordeal.''

``I suppose so...''

``For now, it'll be hard to narrow down the culprit through physical evidence. First, let's make our own list of people we need to be wary of. If the T-incident is involved, then someone with a strong motive for wanting the Science Dept Ori to fail would be an outsider. It makes the most sense to start by suspecting the guests.''

Hijiri raised the index finger of his right hand, which was resting on his knee.

``Among the guests, the most suspicious at the moment is Kurauchi-san, who went to Kannon-kutsu sometime between 10:00 and the incident. As for the other candidates, there's Bakuma-san, who arranged the construction. I also want to keep Claire-san in sight as another possibility. She said she wasn't going home today and would be staying with us.''

``Stay? Why?''

``She said something about wanting to deepen their interaction. Aside from the alumni, Kurauchi-san and Bakuma-san, Claire-san was the only one who made a move like that. While the other guests left, she alone stayed behind.''

``The guests already went home? Even though there's still the second task?''

``Apparently, they'll edit the footage shot tonight and have them watch a digest version tomorrow. A lot of them were people in high-ranking positions, too. They probably thought it would be rude to keep them there too long.''

\textit{I see. But wouldn't someone have to stay up all night to edit it?}

``But she was in the audiovisual room the whole time, wasn't she? It'd be hard for her to tamper with the scaffolding.''

``I think so too. But the point of this discussion isn't to narrow things down yet; it's to identify candidates and weigh them. There's always the possibility of an accomplice or someone helping from the sidelines. Right now, how well we can anticipate danger matters more than how accurately we can identify the culprit. We shouldn't narrow our focus while we're still short on information.''

``Understood. Then for now, let's keep an eye on those three as the guests.''

``And we'll keep our guard up for any danger. While staying alert for suspicious movements, including from the students, we'll gather physical evidence and work toward finding the culprit. I'll speak with Hongo-senpai properly later.''

\textit{Watching Hijiri calmly lay out everything that needed to be done somehow filled me with a strong sense of security. I felt a little as though I had a great detective beside me on some remote island.}

``The culprit clearly wants to cause an incident in a way that will never be exposed and will definitely be pinned on the Science Department. That makes this a situation where we can't expect them to make a mistake, but at the same time, it's one where we can limit what they do. If we don't let our guard down, it should be quite hard for the culprit to make a move.''

``Doesn't that apply to us too? We want to avoid blowing this up into a major ordeal, right?''

``Of course. Our goal, and the condition for success, is to make the Science Dept Ori a success without any trouble. But it'll be okay. We can do it.''

``\dots\dots I guess so.''

As I nodded, I ran through the unresolved mysteries once more.

The card that had reached Hijiri and me, evoking the Tengu Festival Incident.

The message written on it, saying there was a fake among the guests at the Science Dept Ori.

And the accident that had actually occurred at the Science Dept Ori.

The strange resemblance between that incident and the content of the game.

\textit{With all of that hanging over us, could we really make it through the Science Dept Ori?}

$\gamma$

In the corner of the waiting room, Del-chan and Hijiri-kun were talking with their heads huddled together.

I came back with a plate of watermelon for Del-chan, but froze for a moment, wondering if I'd just seen something I wasn't supposed to.

``Oh, Iwama-san, you're back too,'' Hijiri-kun said, standing up and walking over as if nothing had happened.

``He was slumped over in the corner, so for a moment I thought he might be dead, but he was just sleeping. I was just relieved.''

Delta seemed to be prioritizing comfort over coolness now. Sitting in the chair, he looked a little tense, but otherwise seemed okay. I walked over and placed the watermelon on a nearby desk.

``Bakuma-san gave us this. It's really good.''

``\dots\dots Ah, thanks.''

Just hearing his voice made me uneasy. He sounded even more exhausted than I'd imagined.

``Do you not have much of an appetite?''

``No, it's not that. If anything, I was just craving something with sugar and fluids.''

Del-chan immediately picked up a piece of watermelon and stared at the red flesh for a while.

``I had some too, and it was very good,'' Hijiri-kun added.

Only then did Del-chan finally take a small first bite. \textit{I thought he liked all kinds of fruit, but maybe he wasn't that fond of watermelon.}

``It's good. Very refreshing.''

``I'm glad!''

\textit{It was a pretty safe comment for a fruit lover to make, but hearing it still relieved me.}

``You're very kind, Iwama-san. Bringing watermelon to the enemy... I wouldn't have thought of that,'' Hijiri-kun said.

``Rather than `enemy'... well, we're both in the biology club...''

\textit{I wished I could've used a better word than ``club members''---like ``friends'' or ``comrades''---but saying that in front of Hijiri-kun felt a little embarrassing.}

``You really are kind. Just a minute ago, Watari and I were insulting each other even though we're in the same physics club.''

As if on cue, Watari-kun and Mikage-san came back into the waiting room. They were both tall and carried themselves with a certain maturity, which made them look pretty formidable standing side by side. \textit{Of course, Del-chan was that sort too, but he came off as more gentle than intimidating.}

``Oh, everyone's here except Togakushi-kun!''

Mikage-senpai appeared from behind them, ruffling Mikage-san's hair almost absentmindedly.

``I have an important announcement. It has nothing to do with the outcome of the game, but it's an annual tradition. I want you to choose one male and one female representative from among yourselves.''

For some reason, he had an arm around Mikage-san's shoulder like he was shielding his little sister.

``For what purpose?''

Senpai answered a curious Hijiri-kun with a smile.

``Simply put, it's a bit of a ritual. You'll be lighting the campfire. Together, like cutting a wedding cake. Nagisa and I did it the year before last.''

Nagisa was Hongo-senpai. Apparently, the two of them were going out now.

\textit{I felt like I understood why senpai was shielding his sister, like he was silently saying, ``Don't you dare pick her.''}

But if that was the case, that left me as the only girl...

``Togakushi-kun wouldn't want to do it even if we asked, so the five of you decide. The deadline is the end of the second task. The campfire lighting is scheduled for around the end of dinner once the second task is over. Just let me, Nagisa, or Rora-chan know. See ya!''

Mikage-senpai ruffled his sister's hair again, as if staking his claim, and left the waiting room.

For a while, no one said a word.

\textit{I realized that Hijiri-kun, Watari-kun, and Mikage-san were all looking at Del-chan and me.}

$\delta$

``If I end up as the representative, can I ask Delta-kun to be my partner?''

``I guess there isn't much choice.''

We split off to opposite ends of the room for strategy meetings about the second task, but the first thing we ended up discussing was which boy-girl pair would light the campfire.

``Why me? Watari would be fine, wouldn't he?''

``If Hijiri or I got paired with Mikage, there's no telling what Mikage-senpai would do to us back at the club,'' Watari said.

``As long as you take responsibility, I don't think Nii would actually kill you,'' Mikage said.

``If I don't take responsibility, he really will kill me, won't he?...''

Watari didn't look interested in the slightest. He looked over at me.

``I mean, wouldn't Delta and Iwama work fine?''

``In what way is that `fine'?''

``You're both in the biology club. Since Togakushi from chemistry is sitting this one out, doesn't that make you the most balanced boy-girl pair?''

``Do you hate the idea?''

Mikage pressed me on it. I didn't know how to answer.

``It's not that I hate it, but\dots\dots''

Compared to what I'd just been discussing with Hijiri, this felt absurdly lighthearted. \textit{I wondered if this was what people meant by an ``alternating bath.'' My head felt like it was going to spin.}

Still, after going through the ordeal of forcing down the watermelon Bakuma-san brought and spending several minutes in a bathroom stall fighting back nausea, I'd managed to switch gears to some extent.

\textit{There was no way it had been poisoned, but my body didn't seem willing to believe that.}

\textit{The watermelon Iwama had gone out of her way to bring me tasted like nothing at all.}

\textit{It hurt like hell to have to suspect someone of malice.}

\textit{I knew perfectly well that something as obvious as rigging the watermelon to cause a food poisoning outbreak and ruin the Science Dept Ori was unlikely.}

\textit{Even so, I'd gone as far as wrapping a small leftover piece of watermelon in plastic and hiding it in the biology room freezer.}

\textit{Just in case I needed it as evidence.}

``Well then, decide whether you'll pick me or Gamma-san by the time the second task is over.''

While I'd let my guard down, the conversation had taken a strange turn. \textit{Oh well. If it came down to it, I'd shove it onto Hijiri. A fearless guy like him would probably handle being Mikage's partner just fine. Even if it ended up being Iwama---}I glanced toward the other side of the waiting room and saw Iwama looking like she was enjoying discussing the mystery with Hijiri; I dropped my gaze to avoid meeting hers.

\textit{If it's for Iwama, I'll do it. Since it involves dangerous work with fire.}

``Now then, shall we get to work cracking the code too?'' \textit{Making the Science Dept Ori a success mattered too.} I lightly tapped the desk to change the subject.

On the desk, the three sheets of investigation materials collected in the first task were lined up face down. What Hijiri had called the ``Golden Egg code'' was written line by line on the back of each.

The order didn't seem to matter much, but when arranged in a way that felt right, they read as follows:

\begin{center}
Search for the path, relying on unheard voices.

Listen closely, borrowing the ears of a giant.

At coordinates where the land stretches endlessly, invisible waves will show the way.
\end{center}

``Isn't this impossible already? It makes no sense, and we have less than thirty minutes until the second task.''

``Maybe it's a clue for the third task. Even though there was only a two-hour gap, that woman called us to the audiovisual room and killed our time. If she wanted us to solve it by the second task, she wouldn't have done that.''

Mikage's point was sound. I nodded and added:

``Maybe we'll be able to obtain other clues during the second task.''

``Yeah. It's possible. I caught a glimpse of it, but the management team was drawing some lines on the school grounds. If it starts at five, there's a chance we won't be doing the path-finding task today.''

That said, since we had nothing else to do, we turned back to the coded text.

Watari and Mikage seemed to think that `unheard voices' and `ears of a giant' basically referred to receiving a message through some scientific means. I agreed. The expression `standing on the shoulders of giants'---borrowing the accumulated wisdom of great predecessors---is often used in academia. It was a phrase Iwama liked, and Hongo-senpai, the Game Master, had used a similar expression back in the spring too.

Watari explained it to me while pointing at the remaining line.

``The `invisible waves' are probably radio waves or something. I guess they could just be sound waves too, but if there's actual sound playing at the scene, it'd be pretty dumb for that to clash with the idea of `unheard voices.'''

``Were you able to make sense of the first half of the last line?''

``No idea. It suddenly turned into some kind of J-pop lyric.''

True, you could easily imagine lyrics like that. `Coordinates that stretch endlessly across the land'. A coordinate is just a single point, so calling it something that ``stretches endlessly'' was a strange way to put it.

``If we're supposed to receive radio waves somewhere, there was a radio in the backpack, wasn't there?''

``This thing. We'll probably use it, but it's just a normal radio. It doesn't have any recordings loaded on it or anything.''

Watari pulled a portable radio out of the backpack. It was small enough to fit in one hand, with a short single-ear earphone plugged into it. It had a switch to toggle between AM and FM, and a dial to tune the frequency. Looking at the back, I found a battery compartment with two perfectly ordinary AA batteries inside.

I turned it on, put the earphone in my ear, and tried tuning through the stations, but all I heard were ordinary radio broadcasts here and there.

``Is there anything else noteworthy about it?''

In response to my question, Mikage pointed toward my ear.

``It's short. The earphone cord. It's only about twenty centimeters long.''

``It's definitely inconvenient, but is that actually a problem?''

``The FM reception's pretty scratchy, right? This radio seems like the kind that uses the earphone cord as an antenna, but this one's too short. There might be some meaning to that.''

``What's an earphone antenna?''

``You don't even know that? It's an antenna that uses the earphone cord.''

``Don't act like you've explained it just by breaking the word apart.''

``What a pain. AM radio picks up signals with a small internal antenna, but FM uses the earphone cable as the antenna instead. You can't receive radio waves without a piece of metal of the right size. This radio doesn't have a rod antenna, does it?''

A rod antenna was probably that stick-like kind. The kind that extends like a baton when you pull it out.

``Could that be a clue?''

``Who knows. There's also the possibility they just cheaped out on the parts.''

In the end, we couldn't solve the code before Hongo-senpai came to fetch us.

$\gamma$

``I'll explain again once we get to the school grounds, but you won't need to bring anything for the second task! We're doing it on school grounds, so there's no need to get ready to head out into town. You can stay dressed exactly like you are.''

\textit{So that's how it is,} I thought as I stood up. We still hadn't been told what exactly we'd be doing, and the three-line code written on the backs of the papers we'd received in the first task hadn't made much sense to me either.

When the five of us left the waiting room together, Togakushi-kun was standing there, rubbing his sleepy eyes.

``Sorry. My brain's not working. Just think of me as backup.''

He spoke to Hijiri-kun and me in a whisper.

``It's okay! You worked so hard on the first task, so I'll work even harder on the next one!''

``I feel like I can go all out again. No matter what comes our way, let's win this cleanly.''

The six of us followed Hongo-senpai toward the school entrance. The sky outside the window was still blue. But the sun had already dipped quite a bit, so it looked like it would be a little more bearable.

It felt strange that there was no one else in the school building besides us. Apparently, the Science Department had reserved the whole place. It was very quiet, and with the hallway lights turned off, it felt like a school from another world.

Tsunanagai High School was surrounded by mountains on three sides, except for the south. The sun looked ready to sink behind the mountains.

When we stepped out onto the school grounds, the Science Department students were already gathered there. Three large objects that looked like PVC pipes had been set up there, and three concentric circles had been drawn in white in the middle of the field. I had no idea what we were about to do, but the way everyone had gathered there, buzzing on a summer evening, made it feel like a festival.

``This is... a potato cannon!''

Hijiri-kun spoke to Togakushi-kun and me with an excited look.

``One end of that pipe is sealed, and you put flammable gas inside, jam a potato into the muzzle, and ignite the gas. Then it explodes and sends the potato flying. The physics club did this during our Golden Week training camp.''

I could see that Watari-kun had noticed the same thing and was explaining it to Delta and Mikage. Delta looked uneasy. \textit{He'd seemed a little out of it ever since the first task ended.}

``Is that circle a target?''

``Probably. I wonder if they'll have us do something like curling or darts with the potatoes we fire.''

While we were talking, we made our way over to the other students. Hongo-senpai, who had been leading us, broke away from the group and climbed up onto the morning assembly platform, heading for the microphone.

``Alright, everyone! Since it's now five o'clock, I'd like to begin the second task!''

The chatter died all at once. Out on the field, where almost no car noise reached because of the hills behind the school, the only thing echoing was the sound of cicadas.

Hongo-senpai soaked up everyone's attention with a pleased expression as she made a grand declaration.

``The second task is the `Science Game'! While the first task tested your basic knowledge, this one will test your practical skills. We'll be holding one competition each for physics, chemistry, and biology, and you'll compete for points in all three. Your start time tomorrow will be decided by your total score, so do your best!''

The first-years who weren't on the selected teams cheered. Mizasaki-kun's eyes were sparkling too.

``Also, the first-place team in each competition will receive a deluxe prize. They might even come in handy during the third task, so be sure to aim for them too. And here they are...''

Karato-senpai, who was standing by behind the assembly platform, held out a tray to Hongo-senpai. Hongo-senpai took one from the tray and raised it high overhead.

``First, the first-place prize for the physics competition is this flip phone! It's old and doesn't have a SIM card, but it can take photos, pick up radio signals, and connect to Wi-Fi. If there's a free hotspot, you can even use it to search the internet! I want this...!''

I certainly wanted it. However, Team X probably wanted it the most. We already had a portable radio, and Hijiri-kun could basically handle the camera and internet side of things for us.

``Next, the first-place prize for the chemistry competition! Ta-da! A regular calculator! With this, you can do complicated calculations in an instant! Since it's not a scientific calculator, though, it only handles basic arithmetic, and the display only goes up to ten digits... also, it runs on solar power, so you can't use it in dark places. Keep that in mind!''

Would we be going somewhere that dark in the third task? Or was it---

``And the first-place prize for the biology competition is... lo and behold, this ear-phorn---I mean, earphones! They're just ordinary wired earphones, but they're about a meter long and stereo! You might even be able to listen to the same song with that special someone! Wired-earphone fans, go for it!''

The prizes were getting steadily worse. Team Y had Togakushi-kun in place of a calculator, and even though our earphones were monaural, we already had a set. If we were going to aim for anything, it would be the flip phone from the physics competition.

Still, I couldn't help wondering.

\textit{Would the calculator really be used as a calculator?}

\textit{Does the rule about ``not engaging in irreversible acts of destruction'' mean we can take apart the things we've obtained, as long as we don't do anything irreversible?}

$\delta$

The six members of the selected teams were each given a brand-new lab coat specially made by the Science Department for use in the second task. The words ``Investigation of Reason'' were printed across the back in large black cursive iron-on letters. Apparently, we were allowed to keep them once the Science Dept Ori was over, but I didn't feel much like wearing mine in class.

``This is damn ugly. What are we, naval officers?'' Watari grumbled, but in the end, all the selected members, including him, put on the Science Department lab coats.

Fujiwara-sensei, the physics club advisor, was out on the school grounds. He looked like a younger, heavier version of the famous portrait of Einstein. In other words, he had gentle, drooping eyes, a mustache, and messy hair. Knowing that Fujiwara-sensei and the third-year physics club members would be keeping a close watch on safety made me feel a little more at ease.

Just as Watari had outlined for me, the physics competition was ``Potato Cannon Darts.'' The rules were simple: starting with Team X, each team would take turns firing one potato per round over three rounds, for a total of three shots per team, and compete to see whose potatoes landed closest to the target. At the end of the game, the distances from the three potatoes to the target would be added together, and that total would become the score. Naturally, the team with the lower score would win.

Each of the three team members had to take one turn as the shooter. I wasn't thrilled that I had to take a shot; I'd obviously never stuffed a potato into a water pipe before, I didn't know that much about physics, and my instincts for ball games were questionable at best.

Team Z was apparently planning to use a different set of three representatives for each competition. The first-years, led by Mizasaki and Osawa---the blond physics club member---had been arguing over various things, but after Hongo-senpai pressed them, they finally seemed to have settled on their lineup.

While Team X and Team Y were checking the items laid out for them, Team Z's three members finally showed up at their area a little late. I couldn't believe my eyes. Hongo-senpai introduced them cheerfully.

``Now then, these three will be competing for Team Z! From the physics club, Osawa-kun and Toudo-kun, and a special guest who you all know, second-year physics club member, Hyakuzawa-san!''

\fullpageimage{8.jpg}

\thispagestyle{plain}
\vspace{1cm}

I had met her once before. It was before Golden Week, when she'd treated me to apple pie at the ``Fukumaden'' dormitory for out-of-prefecture students. Even in her school uniform, she was dressed just as revealingly as she had been back then; her skirt was as short as the rules allowed, and she'd rolled her shirt sleeves up high enough to bare her shoulders.

She was tall, short-haired, and sharp-eyed. The kind of person you wouldn't want to pick a fight with.

But that wasn't the problem. Hijiri pointed it out immediately.

``Hongo-senpai, Hyakuzawa-senpai is a second-year, isn't she?''

``That's true. Sorry, that's on me. When I defined Team Z, I guess I didn't phrase it clearly enough. Since I said `everyone else,' by definition that ended up meaning everyone except the selected members.''

``That's sophistry.''

``Sorry, Jiri-chi. In this Science Dept Ori, my words are the absolute rules.''

Jiri-chi---Hijiri---looked utterly unconvinced, but reluctantly held his tongue.

---And for Team Z! Everyone else! This year, all first-years will participate!

It was true that senpai hadn't actually said, ``Everyone else from the first-years is Team Z.'' Even if you interpreted it as ``everyone else in the Science Department,'' it would still be true that all the first-years were participating.

\textit{But would Hongo-senpai really make a slip like that?}

\textit{And was Hyakuzawa-senpai really such a powerhouse that Osawa and the others would go out of their way to exploit a loophole in the rules just to bring her in...?}

``Sorry. Let's give up on the flip phone. We should aim for second place.''

Watari already looked like he'd accepted defeat. \textit{What was this supposed to mean? As far as I knew, Hyakuzawa-senpai was just a professional-level apple pie baker and someone who looked a little intimidating.}

``Why are you being so timid? That's not like you.''

``You don't know?''

Watari from the physics club let out a knowing sigh.

``That person is probably the least human being in this entire school.''

The whistle blew, and the first round began at once. Drones even rose into the air with a noisy hum, probably for filming. In the end, I missed my chance to ask why Hyakuzawa-senpai was said to be beyond human. Following Watari's instructions, I practiced how to hold the potato cannon, which was about two meters long in total.

The potato cannon had a simple construction. It consisted of a one-meter PVC pipe for loading the potatoes and another, thicker one-meter PVC pipe for the gas, joined together in a straight line. The end of the thick pipe was sealed with a threaded cap to keep the gas airtight. A piezoelectric element, the kind used in gas stoves or lighters, was attached to the side of the pipe; pressing the button sent a spark through a wire inserted inside. This would cause the gas to explode, launching the potato from the tip.

Watari picked out the first shell from the potatoes packed in a cardboard box and used a small knife to shape it so it could be loaded into the thin pipe. Mikage was opening a brand-new bottle of hairspray.

``Just treat the first shot as a test run. It's not like it'll go well for us anyway. Just make sure you remember the gas volume, the weight of the potato, and the launch angle so we can use that for the next shots.''

``Got it. That makes me feel a bit better.''

``Don't just shoot it sloppily, though. This counts toward our score too.''

Watari shoved the potato, which he had shaved down in just one section with the knife, into the thin barrel.

``I don't have a scale, but I've got a rough idea of the weight. I'll count the seconds while I hold down the spray nozzle.''

``How much should we use?''

``With that brand, let's start with three seconds. If you put in too much, there won't be enough oxygen and it won't explode.''

``Team X, please start when you're ready---''

Hongo-senpai's voice prompted us, and everyone there turned to look our way. Two cameras were filming us from nearby. Before Mikage could spray the gas, I spoke up.

``I have one last thing I want to check.''

Even if it was only hairspray, we were still causing an explosion. I checked for any weak points in the barrel's connections. Even when I tugged on it, it didn't budge. It was probably fine, but I wanted to be sure.

``Alright, it's fine. Don't stand behind me. I can't say for sure the cap won't go flying off.''

``Obviously.''

I stepped out to the line drawn as the firing point. The target was exactly fifty meters away. Mikage sprayed the gas inside and firmly tightened the cap. Watari gave me instructions from the side.

``First, we're aiming for maximum distance. Set it to forty-five degrees. A little higher. Haven't you ever even seen a set square? Higher still. Yeah, right about there. Hold it steady and fire.''

\textit{Don't assume I can set it to forty-five degrees instantly just because I've seen a set square.}

``The wind's blowing from right to left. Aim at one o'clock.''

Mikage told me. \textit{What, am I on a battlefield or something?}

``Hey, it shifted. Higher. Aim thirty degrees to the right and keep the angle at exactly forty-five. It'll get harder to pull off as time passes. Line it up and fire quickly.''

``Shut up---'' I kept the words to myself, adjusted the barrel upward, and pressed the piezoelectric element.

With a muffled thump, I felt the recoil jolt through my hands as the potato shot out of the pipe with more force than I'd expected. I felt like my aim had wavered because of it, but the potato traced a beautiful arc, bent with the wind, and landed just beyond the target.

Not bad.

Out of the three concentric circles drawn at five-meter intervals around the target, it had landed inside the outermost one. In other words, the error was within fifteen meters.

``Oh! Not bad at all. Pretty impressive for Delta.''

Watari slapped me hard on the back. If I hadn't been wearing the Science Department lab coat, it would have left a handprint.

``We did it. Just like we planned.''

Mikage was smiling happily too. I'd only done what I was told, but apparently I'd done well. Everyone around us was clapping. I could see Iwama clapping loudly too.

``Incredible! It landed inside the target! We'll measure it at the end, but that looks like about fourteen points. That's a huge result without a test shot. Next is Team Y! Please start when you're ready!''

As Hongo-senpai kept things moving, the management team placed a small sticker on the potato I'd fired. Since eight more potatoes were about to go flying, they were making sure they could tell which team each one belonged to.

The first shooter for Team Y was Togakushi. Just like me, he seemed to have no idea what was going on and was getting an explanation from Iwama and Hijiri. I couldn't hear what they were saying, but Iwama seemed to be giving more detailed instructions than Hijiri. \textit{Well, when it came to Iwama, it wouldn't have been that strange if at some point in her sixteen years she'd wanted to find out how far she could launch a potato.} I felt relieved when I saw Hijiri checking the strength of the barrel, just like I had.

The three of them stood at the firing point. Togakushi took his stance and aimed.

A bang rang out, sharper than the sound ours had made. But that wasn't necessarily a good thing.

The potato flew an absurd distance, cleared the net, and vanished into the trees on the back hills.

``Ooh! That's an out-of-bounds home run! I forgot to mention this, but if the error is more than fifty meters, if you can't fire, or if the potato falls apart, no record will be taken and it'll be treated as an error of exactly fifty meters. That's fifty points for this one!''

Iwama and Hijiri smiled as they comforted Togakushi. Loud applause broke out again.

Watari analyzed the situation while clapping half-heartedly.

``They used too much spray. They didn't get any useful data out of that. Looks like we can win this.''

Next up was Team Z. Their first shooter was Toudo from the physics club. He was the engineering-minded physics geek type and wore thick glasses; he usually hung around with the blond Osawa beside him and Watari, who was standing next to me with a grim look on his face. Mizasaki and I often called them the ``O-To-To Trio,'' using the first letters of their surnames. \textit{I liked the name because it sounded silly.}

Hyakuzawa-senpai was carving a potato while giving instructions to Toudo and Osawa. Unless my eyes were deceiving me, senpai had actually rolled her shirt up enough to reveal her midriff. There was barely enough fabric left to rival a swimsuit. \textit{I wanted to believe otherwise, but maybe that was just her personal taste.}

While senpai filled it with gas, Toudo sat on the ground and braced the bottom of the barrel into the sand. I see. That would probably reduce errors caused by human movement. Senpai leaned over Toudo from behind, close enough to captivate any ordinary guy, and adjusted the aim. The moment she pulled away, he fired.

The potato traced a perfect arc and landed with a plop inside the circle.

``As expected of Ngo-chi! Is that ten or eleven points? Her skill's showing right from the very first shot!''

``Is it really that impressive? It only looked about four meters off from ours.''

When I said that, Watari gave a short, mocking laugh.

``Just watch. Ours was luck, but Hyakuzawa-senpai's was calculated. When you factor in everything from the friction between the potato and the pipe to the humidity, there are margins of error you can't avoid without a test shot. That ten meters is exactly that margin.''

Even with that explanation, I didn't really understand. We entered the second round.

For Team X, Mikage was up second. She used the rag we'd been given to thoroughly wipe out the inside of the barrel, aired it out to get it as close to its initial state as possible, and then loaded the potato and spray.

This time too, I used three seconds and set the angle to a little over 60$^\circ$. I didn't know the detailed calculations, but apparently, if the potato's initial velocity stays the same, the flight distance is proportional to $\sin 2\theta$ when the elevation angle is $\theta$. He said that since we wanted to cut the distance down to about 80\%, we'd raise the angle by roughly fifteen degrees.

Mikage read the wind, adjusted the horizontal aim, and fired. The potato flew a little higher than mine had, and as a result, it landed closer to us.

``Team X is incredible! They adjusted based on the first result! Since it landed on the line, that's exactly five meters. Congratulations!''

Next was Team Y's Hijiri. Togakushi held up three fingers toward Iwama, and Iwama spent exactly three seconds spraying the gas into the barrel. It looked like they'd decided to copy us. But if the potato's weight was different, the initial velocity would change, and the flight distance would change with it.

Even so, they put up a good fight on their second try. The potato Hijiri launched landed just outside the triple circles.

``Success! This time, we have a valid result. For Team Y, that looks like about sixteen points!''

Then came Team Z. Once again, Hyakuzawa-senpai took complete command, and Osawa stepped up to the firing point. Osawa looked a little dissatisfied, perhaps because senpai hadn't pressed in nearly as close to him this time when giving the go-ahead.

They fired. The next moment, the entire school grounds erupted in noise. I let out an ``Ah'' before I even realized it.

The potato had landed dead center on the target without the slightest error.

``Wow! Ngo-chi is finally showing her true strength! She closed the gap perfectly and dropped it right on top of the target!''

``\dots\dots Is that even possible?''

``It sure is.''

Come to think of it, I felt like Hijiri had mentioned someone in the physics club who could accurately manipulate physical phenomena by eye. And that he didn't think she was the same species of \textit{Homo sapiens} as the rest of us.

And yet, Hyakuzawa-senpai, who had done nothing but give instructions so far, still hadn't shown her true abilities.

We entered the third round. Watari didn't get greedy; he aimed under the same conditions as Mikage and dropped his potato around the fifteen-point mark, just like I had. He said the potato might have been a bit light. Iwama went last for Team Y, and after applying the adjustments successfully this time, her potato landed about eight meters from the target.

Hyakuzawa-senpai of Team Z ordered Toudo and Osawa to watch from a distance and handled all the preparations herself. First, for some reason, she walked around near the target, carefully studying the condition of the ground, then meticulously carved a potato she'd picked herself before heading to the firing point alone.

Everyone watched her in silence, wondering what she was about to do. She took her time loading the potato and the spray, crouched down to brace the barrel, took a breath, and fired.

At first, I thought something was wrong.

The potato didn't land on the target. If anything, it looked like it had fallen on the five-meter line, one ring out.

One of the upperclassmen on the management team ran over to the landing spot. I immediately saw him wave Hongo-senpai over. A buzz spread across the school grounds.

``What happened?''

``\dots\dots That's where my potato fell,'' Mikage said quietly.

``Alright! The final result is in! Try not to be too shocked, but it seems Ngo-chi's potato landed right on top of Team X's! It's hard to believe, but Team X's potato has been split clean in half!''

Since I genuinely couldn't believe it, we ran over to the landing spot.

It was like a joke.

Mikage's potato, the one with the ``X2'' sticker on it, had been cleanly split in two by the potato that fell from above. It must have softened from hitting the ground first. Maybe because it had acted as a cushion, Hyakuzawa-senpai's potato had stayed intact.

I was speechless at the absurd result.

\textit{If this had been a bow or a rifle, where the tools were standardized, I could still have accepted a feat like that. But this time, the method involved filling the gas yourself and firing potatoes with random shapes and weights.}

\textit{Just how much raw instinct and training would it take to make something like that possible?}

``Since the potato was destroyed, it's a no-count. It's a shame, but that's fifty points,'' Hongo-senpai told us as we stood there dazed.

``But it should've been five points when it landed.''

``I'm sure I said that the scores would be totaled at the end of the game.''

She definitely had said that. I saw Watari mutter something under his breath. It was probably ``Bitch.''

In this competition, the bigger the point gap, the more advantageous your start time in the third task would be. For Team Z, crushing Team X's potato---Team X being in second place---and widening the gap was more effective than simply landing on the target. Hyakuzawa-senpai had pulled that off with her transcendent technique.

Finally, the results were announced.

\begin{center}
Team X, 79 points (14 points, 50 points, 15 points)

Team Y, 74 points (50 points, 16 points, 8 points)

Team Z, 16 points (11 points, 0 points, 5 points)
\end{center}

With a terrifying point spread, it was a landslide victory for Team Z.

$\gamma$

Team Z took the flip phone we had been aiming for. I was still reeling from the outcome of the competition, but Hijiri-kun gave a sad smile as if he'd expected this all along.

``There was no way we could've won from the start. Hyakuzawa-senpai is superhuman, after all. It must've been Osawa's quick thinking; if they manage to get someone like that on their side, there's nothing we can do. Let's move on.''

``I'm in the same dorm as her, but I'd only ever thought of her as someone who liked cooking.''

``Apparently, cooking is a kind of tuning that lets her grasp the physical world. I don't know the details, but she said it's training that lets her understand the causal relationship between how prepared ingredients are handled and the taste, aroma, and texture that result, using her own hands and senses.''

``\dots\dots Is showing that much skin part of it too? Like reading the wind?''

``Yeah. When senpai gets serious, she exposes as much skin as possible so she can take in things like temperature, humidity, and wind direction. Apparently, she'd actually prefer to be naked, but she hesitates to go that far.''

\textit{I'm glad she at least has the sense to hesitate.}

While the excitement still hadn't died down, we moved to the chemistry room for the next competition.

In the spacious chemistry room, six large desks fitted with sinks and gas taps were lined up in a row. Three of them had been prepared with a full set of experimental equipment.

``The main venue is over here, but first, come to the classroom across the hall!''

After being given a quick look at the chemistry room, we entered the lecture room across the hall. Usually, it looked just like any normal classroom, with desks and chairs lined up in rows, but now almost all of them had been pushed into the corners, and folding tables had been set up in front of the blackboard instead. Seasonings, juices, and fruits were lined up on the tables. It looked like we were about to have a cooking contest.

For some reason, a single-person desk had been placed in front of the long tables, and even stranger, four small rectangular cushions I didn't recognize had been laid out on top of it.

``I wonder what those are?''

``Every item on the long table has only one of its kind.''

``\dots\dots True.''

``Iwama-san. Before we start, there's something I'd like to ask of you, is that okay?''

$\delta$

People were gathering one after another in the lecture room across from the chemistry lab. Going against the flow, Iwama and Hijiri went outside, so I peeked into the hallway to see what they were doing. At the far end of the dim corridor, away from the main flow of traffic, the two were engaged in some bizarre ritual. Hijiri held out their left arm with the elbow tucked in, almost like the ``small arms forward'' formation drill, while Iwama placed both hands on Hijiri's forearm and put her full weight on it. Eventually, both of Iwama's feet lifted off the floor.

I thought about it for a moment, but in the end, I decided to pretend I had seen nothing.

By the time Hongo-senpai started the announcement, the two of them had come back. Hijiri was slowly clenching and unclenching their left hand---the one Iwama had just been hanging her weight on. \textit{I'd have to ask about that later.}

``Round two! The chemistry competition is the `Shady Powder Championship'! You'll all use the items available in this lecture room to make a shady powder. The team that produces the shadiest powder wins!''

In response to Hongo-senpai's declaration, the students gathered in the lecture room gave a scattered round of applause.

Making a shady powder\dots\dots The moment I heard that, Mizasaki's face came to mind. It would be the perfect task for someone like him, who bragged that as long as he had the materials, he could synthesize TNT or even methamphetamine from memory.

But how on earth was ``shadiness'' supposed to be judged?

``This time, the criterion for shadiness is pH! We will dissolve up to one gram of the powder you've prepared into 300 milliliters of pure water and measure the pH of that aqueous solution. The team that produces the strongest acidity wins! Points will be calculated by subtracting two from the pH and multiplying the result by 100. If you work hard, you might even end up with a negative value!''

I thought it over. The key was probably the requirement that it had to be a ``powder.'' Strong acids are basically hard to keep in powdered form. For example, hydrochloric acid is hydrogen chloride gas dissolved in water, and sulfuric acid is a liquid even on its own. Nitric acid, which forms when nitrogen dioxide gas dissolves in water, should become solid dinitrogen pentoxide if properly dehydrated, but there was no way you could normally make something that dangerous. It was literally a raw material for explosives.

In that case--- I looked at the items lined up on the long table. What caught my eye were the vinegar, lemons, and similar items. We'd have to make do with weak acids. Acetic acid, the main component of vinegar, is a liquid, but citric acid, which lemons contain in large amounts, can exist in powdered form. It's even sold in pharmacies as a cleaning agent. It also had a decent level of acidity, so it wasn't a bad option. This was it.

``Now then, let's have three people from Team Z step forward. Have you made your decision?''

Being able to choose your members after hearing the competition overview felt like cheating. Along with two first-year chemistry club members, Mizasaki---the former chemistry club member---stepped forward looking full of motivation.

\textit{I knew.}

\textit{After spending three years with him in middle school, I was certain. No matter how many powerhouses the chemistry club had, the one we needed to watch most was Mizasaki.}

\textit{And I knew Mizasaki would casually try things that could cause an accident.}

``Everyone's watching, so don't make anything too dangerous,'' I warned him when I found an opening, but Mizasaki just gave me a playful wink.

``It's fine. This time, I have a special idea that uses a really safe method.''

\textit{That did nothing to reassure me.}

The nine representatives were given a chance to inspect the chemistry lab. On the workbenches assigned to each team, a set of reagents had been placed alongside the experimental equipment. Pure water, hydrochloric acid, dilute sulfuric acid, ethanol, sodium hydroxide, calcium carbonate, and so on. They were all unopened. That was probably for fairness, but it also ruled out things like contamination or swapped contents. I appreciated that.

Incidentally, there was no nitric acid. Even Mizasaki probably wouldn't be making explosives with this setup.

On the way back to the lecture room, I pieced together a method for extracting citric acid in my head.

If you add calcium carbonate powder to lemon juice, the citric acid displaces the carbonic acid, forming calcium citrate, which precipitates out. If you filter out and collect that calcium citrate, then add sulfuric acid, the citric acid will be displaced this time and calcium sulfate will precipitate instead. Since calcium ions and sulfate ions react in a one-to-one ratio, if you adjust things so the amount of calcium carbonate exceeds the amount of sulfuric acid, almost all the sulfuric acid should be removed, leaving the supernatant as an aqueous citric acid solution. If you heat that little by little, citric acid crystals should precipitate out.

\dots\dots No, would that even work?

Citric acid dissolves well in water. Which also means it's hard to get it to precipitate cleanly as crystals. Since it's organic, it will char if heated too much. In other words, it would take time. Would mixing in ethanol, with its lower boiling point, make it go any faster?

``The time limit is exactly forty minutes. Please prepare one gram of shady powder by then. If it doesn't clearly look like a powder, be warned that we'll measure the pH without dissolving it in anything.''

``Without dissolving it---does that mean the pH will be seven? That would make the score 500 points.''

After Hongo-senpai's explanation, Mikage spoke up. I nodded.

``That's a huge loss. We need to avoid that at all costs.''

``Also, when you submit your shady powder, you'll have to declare the name of the substance. But if you declare something that's a mixture other than a solid, or if it's judged that you've mixed in something undeclared to strengthen the acidity, you'll be disqualified just the same. In other words, secretly dripping sulfuric acid into the powder is out.''

That meant we really did have to compete with powder alone.

``Well then, we'll start after a three-minute thinking period! First, you'll take whatever you want to use from this lecture room. If there's a conflict over an item, it'll be settled by arm wrestling, so be ready if you're going for something popular. Thinking time, start!''

The three of us headed to the long table together and consulted in low voices.

``Thinking about it normally, it seems best to extract citric acid from lemons. What do you think?''

``I agree with Delta-kun. But with this, we might be able to cut down the time spent squeezing and filtering.''

The small bottle Mikage pointed to turned out, on closer inspection, to be 100\% lemon juice from Sicily.

``That's definitely the way to go. Crystallizing citric acid takes time. Better to shave off as many steps as we can.''

``What if the other teams go for it too?''

``Watari, win the arm wrestling for us. Those muscles aren't just for show, are they?''

``Fine. I'll do it. For now, I'll search the room and see if there are any loopholes.''

It would be ridiculous if there were citric acid powder hidden somewhere in the room. We searched around just in case, but everything unnecessary had been thoroughly cleared out of the otherwise ordinary lecture room; the only thing we might have been able to use was the chalk dust on the blackboard. Chalk is calcium carbonate. We were probably better off just using the reagents honestly.

``Alright! Thinking time is over! Now, no pushing and no running\dots\ start!''

We headed straight for the lemon juice. And just as expected, the three members of Team Y seemed to have had the same idea. We glared at each other across the bottle. Watari clicked his tongue.

``Are you guys aiming for the lemon juice too?''

``Unfortunately, yes. Time is precious. Let's get started with the arm wrestling.''

Hijiri pointed to the single desk that had been set there. The rectangular cushions were on top of it. They were probably there to keep anyone from hurting their elbows or the backs of their hands.

``Oh, so you're doing this? Then I'll be the referee!''

Hongo-senpai approached, looking like she was enjoying herself. Rock-paper-scissors would've been enough, but was pitting our physical strength against each other one of senpai's hobbies? \textit{Well, we had Watari, whose brain was made of muscle, so we'd be fine.}

``Watari, you're left-handed, aren't you? I'm right-handed, but my left hand's fine.''

Hijiri knelt on the floor, planted his left elbow on the cushion, and got into position for arm wrestling. Watari took the same position across from him, and the two clasped hands. Both glared at each other.

I remembered then. \textit{I recalled Iwama doing something to Hijiri's left arm out in the hallway earlier.}

And one look at Iwama told me I was right. She had the look of someone who had finally put everything together.

``Ready, set... go!''

For a while, neither of them budged. That alone was enough to surprise me. Watari never missed a day of strength training; whenever he arm-wrestled Mizasaki or me, he'd pin us in seconds with his non-dominant right hand. And right now, time was precious. There was no way he was just going easy on him.

And then Hijiri began to push. Watari's left arm started to tip outward.

``Ngh...!''

A strained sound escaped through Watari's clenched teeth. In the next instant, Watari's hand was slammed down onto the cushion in a single motion.

``Winner, Team Y! Now, please take the lemon juice!''

Hijiri regripped the left hand he had just pinned in order to shake it, then left for the chemistry lab with Iwama and Togakushi, lemon juice in hand.

``That bastard... even with glasses, he's freakishly strong. What the hell is with him?''

The glasses had nothing to do with it. I spoke to Watari, who was shaking his head in frustration.

``He was warming up in the hallway earlier. He'd already seen this coming before it even started.''

``As expected of Hijiri-kun. Losing was inevitable. Watari-kun is impressive in his own right, but Hijiri-kun's body is like tempered steel. That's an athlete's body. There isn't an ounce of extra fat on him.''

\textit{I found myself wondering when Mikage had gotten such a close look at Hijiri's body, but I kept it to myself.}

``No helping it. Let's squeeze the lemon. It's our next-best option.''

From the fruit lined up on the long table, I picked up the single lemon that had been placed there.

``Is one really enough? How much citric acid is there in a single lemon anyway?''

``About one lemon's worth.''

``Don't answer like a Vitamin C label. Are you really a former chemistry club member?''

``It'll be enough to get one gram. Time's precious. Let's move. Quickly.''

We headed for the chemistry lab, still bickering.

In the chemistry lab, Usugi-sensei, the chemistry club advisor, and several upperclassmen were keeping watch to make sure we didn't do anything dangerous. If the physics club advisor was Einstein, then the chemistry club advisor felt like Marie Curie. She had stern eyes, and all of her hair, bangs included, was pinned up. Normally, being watched by a teacher would have annoyed me, but this time I was grateful for it.

As I got to work, something caught my attention. It seemed Team Z had already made their choice while we were distracted by the arm wrestling. They showed no interest in the lemon juice or the lemons.

\textit{What on earth were Mizasaki and the others up to?}

$\gamma$

Togakushi-kun from the chemistry club said he was bad at hands-on work, so I took charge.

The difficult part was, as expected, the final step---getting solid citric acid out of the aqueous solution. As we heated it, the solution turned syrupy. I started to worry whether it would really turn into a powder at all. Citric acid is deliquescent, which means it naturally absorbs moisture from the air if you leave it alone. If it got damp, then when we weighed out one gram, too much of that weight would be moisture, and the actual amount of citric acid would drop. I wanted to dry it out as thoroughly as possible.

But all three teams were heating their solutions with gas burners, and with so many spectators packed in, the humidity in the chemistry lab was unusually high.

``They're interfering.''

Following where Togakushi-kun pointed, I saw Team Z using two gas burners to boil water in a pair of beakers. Thick clouds of steam were rising from them. No wonder the room felt so humid and stifling.

``It's clever. But won't that hurt them too?''

Hijiri-kun had a point. Since they were closer to the source of the steam, it should have affected their own work even more than ours.

``Maybe it isn't citric acid. Team Z didn't take any food from the long table. If it's a powder that isn't deliquescent, then maybe that much steam doesn't bother them. They only need to dissolve one gram in 300 milliliters, so it doesn't even have to be a crystal that dissolves easily in water.''

``But what else could it be? If it's a solid that makes water acidic, it has to be an organic acid.''

Togakushi-kun had a point too. Even if it wasn't citric acid---if it were malic acid or tartaric acid, for example---it would still dissolve easily in water. And it would char if heated too much. Could Mizasaki-kun and the others have made some acid we couldn't even imagine?

``Alright, that's it! Turn off the flames and stop what you're doing!''

Hongo-senpai spoke up. The time limit was over.

Team X submitted their powder first. Delta and the others had been forced to start from actually squeezing lemons because we won the lemon juice, and they looked bitter; apparently things hadn't gone very well for them. I felt a little bad for them.

``Alright, Team X, what did you make, and from what materials?''

``We extracted mainly citric acid from lemons.''

Delta answered and held out the white evaporating dish for her to see. Maybe because they'd run out of time and rushed the heating, the edges were bubbling and charred brown.

``The monitor check looks fine too! They said there was a final step involving sulfuric acid, but it should have been removed by the excess calcium ions. Now then, please weigh out one gram on this electronic scale.''

Delta folded the weighing paper with practiced hands, then, sweat running down his forehead---the chemistry lab had turned into a greenhouse thanks to Team Z's interference---scraped material from the evaporating dish and weighed out one gram of something that could barely be called a powder. After senpai checked it, he transferred it into the provided beaker. The light brown fragments dissolved into the 300 milliliters of pure water.

``Now then, while we dissolve that and measure it, Team Y, please!''

What did Team Z's ``shady powder'' look like, and how was it going to affect the pH measurement?

Prompted by Hijiri-kun and Togakushi-kun, I stepped forward with the evaporating dish in hand.

``What materials did you use, and what did you make?''

``We extracted citric acid from lemon juice.''

``That's the juice you won in that arm-wrestling match! The monitor check looks good too!''

Under Hongo-senpai's watchful gaze, I carefully weighed out the crystals---which were supposed to be citric acid---until the digital scale showed exactly one gram. After the check, I dropped them into the beaker.

Right beside it was the weighing paper Delta had used, still left there and not yet thrown away. The center was damp and slightly darkened. Just as I'd suspected, the moisture hadn't been fully removed. If there was still enough water left to soak into the weighing paper, then the actual amount of citric acid was probably reduced by about half.

``And finally, Team Z! What materials did you use, and what did you make?''

At Hongo-senpai's call, I looked back. Mizasaki-kun was standing there with his chest puffed out proudly.

``I couldn't believe my ears.''

``Uh, actually, believe it or not, I synthesized salicylic acid from headache medicine.''

Headache medicine?

Then it hit me at once. Something Togakushi-kun had said during lunch.

`If it was medicine, I was able to get some headache pills from the filming crew.'

``Since the three members of Team Z complained of sudden headaches after the game started, the management gave them two headache tablets each. Apparently, their headaches vanished like they were never there right afterward, but...''

Even Hijiri-kun looked dumbfounded by Hongo-senpai's explanation. I couldn't believe something like that was allowed.

``But headache medicine contains aspirin---that is, acetylsalicylic acid. Why, and how, did you turn it into salicylic acid?''

In response to senpai's question, Mizasaki-kun explained with a look of pure delight.

``Well, first of all, acetylsalicylic acid doesn't undergo intramolecular hydrogen bonding because of the acetyl group, which lowers its acidity. So I came up with the idea of removing it. I hydrolyzed it with sodium hydroxide, neutralized it with hydrochloric acid, and then recrystallized it. Super easy.''

In the glass petri dish Mizasaki-kun held up to the camera were beautiful white needle-like crystals.

After making sure they filmed it thoroughly, as though it were some prized work of art, Mizasaki-kun finally weighed out one gram and put it into the beaker at Hongo-senpai's prompting.

It was then that I noticed the three people lined up in front of the pH meter were biology club members rather than chemistry club members. Mizasaki-kun and Delta were former chemistry club members, and I was a former science club member. Since only about three months had passed since we'd entered school, it seemed the three of us who had built up experience in middle school had naturally ended up taking charge.

The results came in.

\begin{center}
Team X: 94 points (pH 2.94)

Team Y: 62 points (pH 2.62)

Team Z: 41 points (pH 2.41)
\end{center}

Having secured victory through quick thinking and skill, Mizasaki-kun laughed in satisfaction as he high-fived his teammates.

$\delta$
