By the time we stepped out onto the school grounds, the sun had already set. The western sky was dyed a vivid madder red, while the eastern sky had already sunk into a deep indigo. It was the evening cicadas that were singing. Their mournful `kana-kana-kana' echoed from the hills all around the field.

The biology competition Karato-senpai had devised was perfectly suited to this time of day. Called `Insect Catching Battle'. A chart was handed out listing the target insects and their point values: eight points for a rhinoceros beetle, five for a small stag beetle, ten for a giant stag beetle, and as much as fifteen for a jewel beetle. Every insect on the list was a species Karato-senpai had found around this school before, and the total came to exactly 100 points. For any insects caught within the time limit, the corresponding points would be subtracted, and the remaining total would become the score.

``Seriously, is this an elementary schooler's game?''

Even Watari, who spat out those words, seemed motivated, casually eyeing the streetlights in the bicycle parking lot.

Team Z had selected one representative from each club. It was a lineup where Kannabi from the biology club was being counted on by two boys who looked like complete indoor types. Unfortunately, Kannabi herself was the ultimate indoor type. \textit{This match was as good as won.}

The time limit was forty minutes. The search area was limited to the school grounds. After Karato-senpai and Tokumura-sensei, the biology club advisor, explained the precautions regarding dangerous creatures, each representative was given an insect cage and a powerful flashlight. Team X divided up our roles and scattered the moment the starting signal was given.

I was assigned the most important---and the most idle---role. Carrying everyone's flashlights and those tacky Science Department lab coats, I headed toward the back hills. After finding an open area facing the forest, I spread the three lab coats over the nets and branches and aimed the now-switched-on flashlights at them. The illuminated lab coats shone brilliantly. A light trap, making use of insects' phototaxis---their tendency to fly toward light. It was simple, but very effective.

Almost immediately, an unfortunate \textit{Anomala albopilosa} (two points) flew in, so I caught it. Of course, even Watari and Mikage, who had been assigned to search under the streetlights, could probably catch this many. Next came a drone beetle (two points), then one of the flower chafers (two points). They were all greenish beetles about the size of a fingertip, with tiny beady eyes. Normally, a light trap is something you leave alone for a while, but with a time limit this strict, I stayed right beside it so I wouldn't miss any visitors.

It was boring.

As I let the newly arrived \textit{Anomala albopilosa} rest on my hand and stared at it, an entirely unexpected visitor appeared, perhaps drawn by the strong light.

``Oh, Delta.''

She looked at me as though she'd stumbled across a rare insect herself. It was Kannabi. With an insect cage dangling from her hand and a flashlight pointed at me like some bug-catching kid, the sight of her suited her so poorly that I couldn't help laughing.

``Did you just scoff at me?''

``I was just barely holding back from laughing my heart out.''

``It couldn't be helped. They just assumed that since I'm in the biology club, I'd be able to catch insects.''

``That's a disaster. Did you manage to catch anything?''

Kannabi shook her head.

``To begin with, I can only tell a rhinoceros beetle or a jewel beetle apart. Scarabs and stag beetles all look the same to me.''

I briefly considered shoving the scarab-family beetles in my hand right up to the tip of her nose and lecturing her, but stopped myself. \textit{If she didn't even understand the classification, she was probably the type who didn't like looking at them in the first place.}

``By the way, what are you doing there?''

Kannabi pointed to the brilliantly illuminated lab coats.

``It's a light trap. You know insects gather around lights too, don't you, Kannabi?''

``Even though they're nocturnal. Just like us.''

\textit{I wasn't quite sure what she meant by `just like us'. Was she trying to say that introverts gather around the light?}

``Shouldn't you be looking for insects?''

``I haven't caught anything myself, but I already obtained a rhinoceros beetle. Mission accomplished.''

Peering into her insect cage, I saw a single magnificent male rhinoceros beetle inside.

``Rio secretly shared it with me. It seems she'd already caught one.''

It was admirable of her to hand a rhinoceros beetle to the enemy. After all, if Rei---who was being counted on just because she was in the biology club---had come back empty-handed, the members of Team Z wouldn't have thought well of her. \textit{I was impressed that Iwama could think that far ahead even in the middle of a competition. It wasn't something I could ever imitate.}

Rei suddenly looked around as if checking to make sure there were no cameras nearby. She needn't have worried. The cameraman had gotten bored of me after I spent the first five minutes not moving and had gone off to film other members.

``\dots\dots Have you solved the code written on the back of the investigation materials yet?'' Rei asked in a whisper as she stepped closer to me.

``Not yet.''

``I see. It seems Team Y is in the same situation.''

``Even Team Z doesn't know the meaning of that yet, do they?''

When I said that, Rei hesitated for a moment before giving a small shake of her head.

``No way, have you already solved it?''

``It's actually very simple. Once you can see the whole picture, that kind of code isn't much of a problem.''

``What do you mean by the whole picture? Does that mean we've overlooked something?''

Rei took another step closer and lowered her voice, mindful of our surroundings.

``Those three lines didn't give you enough information, did they? Think about what that means.''

This was Rei, who knew a lot about strange fields like psychology and folklore. She had to know a thing or two about codes as well.

``Meaning? Is there some other piece of information?''

``What if there were?''

Even if she put it that way... if there was something we hadn't obtained, there was nothing we could do about it now. It's not like we could just head out into town at this hour.

``What am I supposed to do? A hint like that doesn't really help.''

``I can't say much. I'd feel bad for Sakkii and Osawa-kun and the others. Everyone wants to win.''

After showing a bit more hesitation, Rei spoke.

``But I don't think the point of the Science Dept Ori is for us to deceive each other and clash like this. At least, that's the impression I got from the structure of this code. So, if I could give one piece of advice...''

When I nodded, Rei continued with a serious face.

``Talk properly with Rio, just the two of you.''

``What does that mean?''

Leaving me confused, Rei turned on her heel without answering.

Just then, something glinted. I noticed it right away. Right in the middle of Rei's back, perched on her shirt, was a jewel beetle gleaming green and red. Fifteen points. \textit{My hand reached out instinctively.}

\textit{That was a mistake.}

The accident happened because just as I reached out to pinch the jewel beetle, Rei---for whatever reason---chose that exact moment to stop walking. My fingertip jabbed into her back. There was a strange, audible `click.'

``Gyaaaa!''

Rei let out a hideous scream, and I immediately realized exactly what I'd done.

$\gamma$

The biology competition ended, and the results were out.

\begin{center}
Team X: 25 points

Team Y: 54 points

Team Z: 42 points
\end{center}

Team X, who had set up a light trap using their lab coats, took a commanding first place. It seemed they couldn't catch the jewel beetle or the giant stag beetle no matter what, but they still put up an excellent score by catching everything else. The prize---the long stereo earphones---was given to Team X.

Team Y ended up in third. We lost because, after deciding to split up and search individually, the kinds of insects each of us caught ended up being far too similar. While everyone was chasing high-scoring rhinoceros beetles and stag beetles, less noticeable species like drone beetles got neglected. It made me realize we should have assigned roles more carefully.

It seemed Team Z had run into something similar. But on top of the rhinoceros beetle---the one I gave her---Rei had also caught the highest-scoring jewel beetle, and that ended up being the deciding factor that put them in second place.

I was pretty sure I'd heard a scream during the competition that belonged to Rei, but what had that been about? It definitely hadn't sounded like the cry of someone excited to find a jewel beetle.

When I asked her about it out of concern, she said, ``There was an unbelievably unfortunate accident.'' She didn't tell me what kind of accident it had been.

That was how the second task came to an end. The total scores were projected onto the school building wall.

\begin{center}
Team X: 198 points (79 + 94 + 25)

Team Y: 190 points (74 + 62 + 54)

Team Z: 99 points (16 + 41 + 42)
\end{center}

The lower the score, the better you had done. While there wasn't much difference between Team X and Team Y, both teams had scores nearly double Team Z's. Then came a shocking announcement.

``Tomorrow, the final task---the third task---will be carried out by nine people, including three competitors selected from Team Z. As announced, it's a time-attack format where `the first team to get the trophy wins'! I'll explain the detailed rules before we begin. The start time is set for 10:00, but...''

This was the important part.

``The scores from the second task will be added directly to the start time in minutes. That means one point equals one minute! In other words, Team X will start at 13:18, Team Y at 13:10, and Team Z at 11:39!''

Between Team X and Team Y, an eight-minute difference would still make for a good match. But Team Z would be able to start moving more than an hour and a half earlier.

\textit{With this, it was like the match had already been decided from the start.}

``Team Z, please decide on your competitors by the end of dinner. And Team X and Team Y, come see me after this. There's something I want to tell you. That's all!''

Mizasaki-kun and the other first-years all started talking at once. In a situation where victory was practically theirs for the taking, it looked like they were already starting to discuss who would be best suited as the final runners. Leaving that clamor behind, the three of us from Team Y headed over to Hongo-senpai.

``We have to decide our representative ourselves, don't we?''

Hijiri-kun's words reminded me. We still had to choose a boy-girl pair to light the campfire. We'd been told the deadline was the end of the second task. In other words, that meant right now.

Hongo-senpai was waiting for us near the center of the field. Behind her, upperclassmen wearing work gloves were carrying and stacking square timbers. This was going to be the venue.

``Is it really okay over here?'' a boy who looked like a second-year asked Hongo-senpai as he carried a timber on his shoulder.

``Yep! We moved it a bit for safety! I've already got permission from the teachers too!''

Mikage-senpai rushed over and started directing the assembly of the campfire. The three members of Team X arrived too, and Hongo-senpai turned back toward us.

``Geez, you guys are really having a hard time, aren't you? Are you seriously all just going to lose? You're the selected members, so get it together. I said I'd treat Team Z to yakiniku, but I didn't prepare that many meal vouchers. If you lose, I'm the one who'll be stuck scrambling for some ugly excuse.''

Watari-kun frowned at the rather irresponsible remark. Hijiri-kun asked:

``Does that mean we still have a chance of winning from here?''

``If it's you guys, you can definitely win. Or rather, if you lose, your names will go down in history. As losers, that is.''

Provocation after provocation.

This time, Togakushi-kun clicked his tongue.

``Now then, enough small talk. Have you decided who's doing it?''

Needless to say, she meant the two who would light the campfire. Hongo-senpai picked up a torch that had been placed on the ground. It wasn't lit yet.

``Just hold this torch together and light the kindling. Everyone will be watching from the cafeteria terrace, and photos of the lighting will be kept in the Faculty of Science album and passed down through the generations. Now then, volunteers!''

After an explanation that made everyone feel self-conscious and hesitant, naturally, no one raised a hand.

\textit{It was one of my body's bad habits that my arms started itching at times like this.} I glanced at Mikage-san to see how she was reacting. There were only two girls here anyway. One of us was inevitably going to have to do it. When our eyes met, Mikage-san smiled and nodded, and then she raised a hand---or rather, she didn't. She grabbed Delta's hand and raised it for him.

``As a result of our discussion in Team X, Delta-kun has volunteered.''

``Huh?''

``Oh, so it's one person from each team? Then there's no one but Rio-chi for his partner.''

Delta's small protest was completely ignored, and all eyes turned to me.

``Ah, well... if no one else minds, I don't...''

``Alright, settled! We usually argue about this every year, but this time it was nice and quick! Now, please head to dinner!''

$\delta$

``Sorry, did you hate the idea?''

Rio asked, looking genuinely apologetic. \textit{I was the one who wanted to ask that.}

``I hate standing in front of everyone more than anything, but if Rio's up there with me, I feel a little more at ease.''

``Then I'll take the lead!''

\textit{Rio, who could joke around like that so naturally, really did have a gift for being one of those `people of the sun.' If we'd both kept hemming and hawing, the mood could've turned awkward, but thanks to her, that topic came to an end.}

The selected members headed to the cafeteria a little later than the others. The cafeteria at Tsunanagai High School technically had a kitchen attached, but apparently it hadn't been used as an actual cooking facility in a long time because it wasn't profitable. The setup was that bread and bento were sold at the shop in front of the cafeteria, and you could eat them inside. The wall facing outside was all glass, and beyond it was a wide terrace seating area. That terrace seating area, overlooking the dark school grounds, had been expanded as much as possible for tonight. It looked like several tables and chairs had been brought out from inside. Students were already sitting at many of them.

We tried to sit with our own groups, but there were no seats left where three of us could sit together. I ended up sitting next to Mizasaki, who waved me over.

``Actually, we just decided on Team Z's competitors.''

I could tell just from the look on his face. Mizasaki had definitely been chosen too.

``So we'll be enemies.''

``Formally, once dinner's over. By the way, the other two are sitting across from us.''

Sitting across from us were Osawa from the physics club and a certain chemistry club student who had represented them in the biology competition.

``Nanbu from Class E, chemistry club. Looking forward to tomorrow, Delta.''

Apparently Mizasaki and Osawa had already let my nickname slip before I even had the chance to introduce myself as Izuta.

``Izuta. Nice to meet you.''

Nanbu was a slender boy with silky black hair and an unmistakably indoorsy vibe. In contrast to the blond, frivolous-looking Osawa, he seemed like the serious type. I asked Nanbu:

``Did Team Z choose its competitors from the people who took part in the second task?''

``Yeah. It leads to less arguing that way. One person from each competition. I was in the biology competition.''

``Apparently Nanbu plans to choose biology. Even though he wasn't exactly great at insect catching.''

That made me a little curious.

``Are you aiming for the life sciences?''

``In a sense. Medicine.''

I see. If you're aiming for medical school, there are plenty of people who choose biology instead of physics.

``I don't know whether I should be telling Delta this, but this guy's actually pretty good. On the last exam, he ranked in the top ten in the grade. If Togakushi hadn't joined the club, he would've been a selected member.''

``It's embarrassing hearing that in front of someone ranked fourth in the grade.''

Just as I was starting to feel uncomfortable, an announcement came: ``Everyone, please come and get your bento!'' I stood up to get mine. There was a hamburger steak bento loaded with fried sides and a Makunouchi bento packed with small side dishes; I chose the latter without hesitation. Mizasaki and Osawa chose the former without hesitation. After hesitating for a moment, Nanbu followed their lead.

By the time everyone had gotten their bento, the upperclassmen who had been setting up the campfire joined us, and every seat that had been prepared was filled. Science Department students, the three advisors, and the three guests who had chosen to stay behind. I didn't count them, but there had to have been more than enough to fill two classrooms. It was already past 20:00, and the high schoolers had long since hit the limit of their hunger, so the moment Mikage-senpai finished his brief greeting, everyone dug into dinner.

Maybe because he'd been helping with the setup, Kurauchi-san---one of the guests---arrived at the seat diagonally across from me that Nanbu had secured, with a pair of work gloves hanging from the pocket of his work clothes. As I listened to him talk with the members of Team Z, I realized that Kurauchi-san, a former chemistry club member, was deeply admired by Mizasaki and the others. Even though they'd supposedly only met this morning.

It was probably because of the blunt way he spoke.

``In all my three years, there wasn't a single time I thought I liked an event like the Faculty of Science Ori.''

I hadn't expected to hear something like that from a sincere-looking man in his thirties. But Mizasaki and the others seemed completely absorbed in what he was saying. Even the usually busy Mizasaki had stopped his chopsticks mid-air.

``People call it a festival for introverts or a sports day for science geeks, but the reality is the exact opposite. In the end, those multi-talented types from out of town---the ones who can do everything---show off their overwhelming skill, earn their status as the popular kids, and eventually become club captains or student council officers. I think this is nothing more than a stepping stone for them.''

I felt like I understood. From what I'd heard, the first challenge shown on the broadcast had looked like a complete one-sided game. Team Y had moved through the checkpoints with staggering efficiency, while Team X had struggled just to keep up. Mizasaki had even gone so far as to sympathize with me.

``That's why I like how they set up this year's Faculty of Science Ori. First off, it's not club-versus-club. You don't have to be a generalist; you can split up the work and compete as a team, just like Delta-kun and his friends.''

Still holding his chopsticks, Mizasaki leaned forward.

``When it was club-versus-club, how did you clear tasks outside your own specialty?''

``Unless you were an all-rounder in math and science, you couldn't solve them. I guess it's similar to university entrance exams. That's exactly why the people who could do everything stood out so overwhelmingly.''

``Ugh.''

Osawa made a face, making no attempt to hide his disgust at such a grotesque system.

``It's a microcosm of society. You'll understand even better once you get to university. There are mountains of people who aren't just better at studying than you, but are also eloquent, good-looking, and athletic. Those are the ones who succeed in job hunting. Naturally, they climb the ladder at their companies, and by their late twenties, they're buying foreign cars that cost over ten million yen.''

It was a rude thought, but Kurauchi-san definitely didn't look like that sort of person. \textit{Mizasaki and I would probably end up feeling the same way eventually. Or maybe we were already feeling it---given how this year's Faculty of Science Ori had split the teams up in a way that clearly made certain people stand out.}

As I was lost in thought, Kurauchi-san suddenly looked my way.

``Sorry, Delta-kun, but I'm rooting for Team Z. This time, even the non-selected members were given a chance to strike back. I want to see the underdogs pull off a reversal.''

$\gamma$

By the time I had effortlessly polished off the excessive amount of fried food served with my hamburger steak bento, an announcement was made that they were about to light the campfire. \textit{My heart immediately began to throb in my chest. I pictured acetylcholine being released from the endings of my parasympathetic nerves.}

Mikage-senpai called for us, and I stood up at the same time as Del-chan. Realizing there might be crumbs from the fried food stuck around my mouth, I hurriedly wiped my lips with a wet towel.

As we headed toward the grounds, I passed near Del-chan's seat and noticed something. He had hardly touched his Makunouchi bento. Not just the parsley---he'd even left the cherry tomato behind.

``Are you okay?''

``No. I'm counting on you to lead.''

\textit{He probably thought I was asking whether he was nervous, so he gave me a joking answer.}

Led by Mikage-senpai, DSLR in hand, we headed toward the wood pile. Once we left the terrace, the clamor faded instantly, replaced by the silence of the forest at night. The square logs stacked in a well-crib pattern in the middle of the dark grounds felt like something eerie intruding on an otherwise ordinary scene.

As we approached the wood, Mikage-senpai handed each of us a utility lighter.

``See those magnesium ribbons around chest height? I want both of you to heat the tips with these at the same time. They're turbo-style, so the flame comes out straight like a burner. The ribbons have little notches cut into them, so they should catch fire in less than ten seconds. Once they do, step away right away.''

``What happened to the torches?''

Delta-kun asked the question that had occurred to me as well.

``They weren't strong enough for this. We changed plans.''

Delta-kun turned his back to the terrace and shielded the lighter with his body as he tested it. A blue flame, like a well-ventilated gas burner, hissed out with force. I tested mine too. The child lock was still on. That was close. \textit{It would have been pathetic if I'd been the only one fumbling when the time came.}

``Alright. Go ahead whenever you're ready.''

Mikage-senpai stepped aside and dropped to one knee, aiming the camera at us with practiced ease.

``He said to go whenever we're ready...''

``Let's go on three, two, one.''

``Right.''

The two of us approached the silver magnesium ribbons sticking out from the stacked timbers. To make it obvious, ``This $\downarrow$'' had been written on the wood in chalk. It was Hongo-senpai's handwriting. \textit{It was a little late to be wondering this, but why on earth did a campfire need magnesium ribbons?}

``Three.''

I said it while looking at Del-chan, and he nodded.

``Two, one.''

We counted down together and pulled the triggers on the lighters. We really did end up in a pose like we were cutting a wedding cake together, only with blue flames in place of a knife.

As we kept both flames trained on the magnesium ribbons, they finally burst into a brilliant white glare. The magnesium had begun to burn. I heard the rapid-fire \textit{click-click-click} of Mikage-senpai's shutter, followed finally by a flash.

The white-burning ribbon shortened like a fuse. We didn't know what might happen, so we backed away to keep our distance.

``Stay further back. You should watch from the best seats for a while. I'm going to focus on the shoot.''

Mikage-senpai gave us a small smile and ran toward a tripod set up in the darkness.

\textit{If we went back to the terrace, we were guaranteed to get teased (I didn't personally mind, but I figured Del-chan would hate it), so we stayed out on the dark grounds and watched the magnesium burn.}

When the white flame of the magnesium ribbon entered the depths of the wood pile, something incredible happened.

A loud \textit{shuuu} sound rang out, and then orange sparks sprayed high into the air. The sparks kept their shape as red-hot grains as they fell onto the wood and the ground. Even after hitting the dirt, they continued to glow for a while.

Cheers erupted from the terrace.

``A thermite reaction!''

Realizing what the sparks really were, I blurted the words out without thinking.

``So that's why they went out of their way to use magnesium ribbon.''

It needed a much higher temperature than an ordinary torch could produce. A thermite reaction happens when metal oxide powders, like iron oxide or copper oxide, react violently with aluminum powder and generate immense heat. Because the aluminum strips away the oxygen, pure iron or copper is produced in a molten state. Once the reaction starts, it continues in a chain, but getting it started requires a temperature as high as a magnesium flame.

``I should have known a science-lover's campfire wouldn't end with just burning wood.''

``This is amazing! It's so science-y! I wonder if there's more.''

Even as I spoke, the red-hot products ignited various parts of the wood, and the fire began to spread. Red, green, and blue flames began to mingle with the orange fire.

``Flame reactions, huh?''

``I wonder if the red one is strontium?''

``That green might be boron, given the cost. And the blue is...''

``Probably copper. Copper chloride.''

\textit{I'd heard that talking about flame reactions while watching fireworks was a classic science-geek cliché, but I never imagined I'd be having that exact conversation while staring at a campfire.}

``We really are science geeks, aren't we?''

``Was talking about flame reactions in summer a little too stereotypical?''

The wood began to burn in earnest, and the orange flames became dominant. Even so, colorful flames flickered through the gaps, as if splashing the fire with pigment. Strange colors---the colors of science.

A nostalgic memory resurfaced.

``Come to think of it, I feel like the first experiment I ever truly tackled was the flame test.''

It was so long ago that I wasn't even sure how old I'd been. I remembered the colorful sparks erupting from the handheld fireworks gripped in my small fingers, and the sour smell of gunpowder smoke.

``Starting with fire? You were quite the dangerous kid.''

``Right? I don't remember the details well, but I think it was before I started elementary school. We were setting off fireworks as a family, and apparently I asked, `Why does the color change?' Then my father brought out some methanol fuel we had at home and said, `Let's try it out.'''

``He's a good father.''

``He took education seriously. He got all sorts of things ready, and together we dissolved the things I picked into the methanol and lit them. I was so surprised when the potassium chloride burned purple.''

``You had potassium chloride at home?''

``Supplements. The next day, we went to the bookstore, he bought me a children's encyclopedia, and we looked up the results.''

``Knowing you, I bet checking the results was the best part.''

``Yes! How did you know!?''

As if Del-chan had opened the floodgates, the words came spilling out.

``The results we'd supposedly discovered all by ourselves were already written in the book. And when I actually tried the things the encyclopedia described, the exact same thing happened right in front of me. It felt more magical than any fairy tale.''

It was only natural, of course, but that was what had struck my young heart the most.

``I thought, `This world is amazing. It's as if someone came up with all the rules; even the structure of the tiniest things is all properly laid out. And the more you learn, the more you can use those rules yourself.' Once I realized that, I fell in love with experiments instantly.''

Had I gone on too long? When I looked at Del-chan, he was looking down slightly.

``\dots\dots I'm sorry.''

``Eh?''

``I'm sorry for calling a precious memory a stereotype.''

His apology flustered me. I hadn't meant it that way.

``No, not at all. I didn't mind. I'm the one who said `science geek' first. I'm sorry for making you listen to me ramble about something weird.''

``It's not strange. It's important.''

Del-chan looked unusually serious. He looked straight at me as he spoke.

``You have to be the one who treasures your own feelings of `love' most of all.''

It was only then that I finally realized it.

It was a very simple thing.

\textit{Del-chan was the person who had affirmed and tried to protect my feeling of ``love'' more than anyone else.}

\textit{I was sure that was why I had fallen in love with him.}

$\delta$

Iwama looked more lively than ever as she talked about flame reactions.

Perhaps it was a trick of the strangely colored flames, but her eyes were shining with a hue I had never seen before.

My eyes were drawn to her profile. To that smile of hers that wasn't quite perfect---a smile that looked a little broken.

\fullpageimage{9.jpg}
\thispagestyle{plain}
\vspace{1cm}

I loved the way Sakura never hid her feelings of ``love.'' \textit{Unlike me, who had lived however I pleased, Sakura had lived by answering the demands of others---and because she was someone who had never been able to say she liked what she liked, the way she expressed those emotions seemed more precious than anything.}

That was why I regretted my own careless remark.

``I'm sorry.''

``Eh?''

\textit{Iwama didn't seem to mind at all, but I still couldn't stop myself from apologizing.}

``I'm sorry for calling a precious memory a stereotype.''

``No, not at all. I don't mind. I'm the one who said `science geek' first. I'm sorry for making you listen to something strange.''

\textit{She was probably just being considerate, but I hated myself for making her say that.}

``It's not strange. It's important.''

\textit{I couldn't forgive myself for making Iwama say something that denied her own feelings of ``love,'' even a little. I was supposed to have decided I would never make her feel that way.}

``You have to be the one who treasures your own feelings of `love' most of all.''

\textit{I didn't want her to worry about me. I wanted Iwama to simply keep watching the beautiful flames. Because I wanted to keep looking at her profile.}

It was then that the campfire underwent a sudden transformation.

By the time I noticed something was wrong, the flames had already swelled. Without a moment's pause, a roar far beyond the sound of mere crackling wood shook my eardrums and rattled my very bones. Then the blast of heat hit. My body was already moving on its own. Without a second to care about personal space, I threw myself over Iwama.

In the corner of my vision, I saw red-hot wooden debris floating high into the night sky.

They rained down onto my back and the nape of my neck.

$\gamma$

I couldn't help thinking he didn't have to protect me. In fact, I'd wanted to be the one to protect him. Our backs weren't that different in how sturdy they were. Del-chan didn't have to be the one taking the hits from the wood fragments falling toward me.

Fortunately, Del-chan wasn't injured. I was so worried that all I could do was repeat ``I'm sorry, are you okay?'' over and over, but Del-chan only gave me a smile as if he were perfectly fine.

It was hard to believe it had happened at all. The campfire had literally exploded.

For a prank, this crossed the line. Mikage-senpai's hair was singed in places from the falling sparks. Even so, Hongo-senpai didn't seem to care much. They worked together to put out the fire with extinguishers that had been set up around the area, then started moving the students since it was time for the baths.

``Delta, Gamma-san, were you two okay?''

Mizasaki-kun ran up to us where we stood on the grounds and asked with a grave expression.

``Yeah. We're okay. What about everyone else?''

``We're all fine. Hongo-senpai told us not to leave our seats. Even though the flame reactions were far away and hard to make out. It must have been because they were planning an explosion. If they were going to pull a surprise like this, they should have at least moved Delta and Gamma-san farther back.''

As someone who loved chemistry, Mizasaki-kun seemed unable to hide his irritation at how dangerous the setup had been.

``It was pretty dangerous.''

``No, `pretty' doesn't cover it. Dangerous experiments are one thing, but you shouldn't perform experiments you can't control. I thought the senpais understood that much. Honestly, I'm disappointed in them. Hey, Delta, you're really not hurt, right?''

``Yeah. I'm fine. My ears are still a little muffled, though.''

``Don't push yourself, seriously.''

I went back to the terrace seats with Mizasaki-kun. Most of the students had already been moved out; only the selected members and the Team Z competitors remained. According to Osawa-kun, they were going to use a single minibus to ferry everyone to a public bathhouse. Apparently, we were in the last group because of the numbers.

Once he knew we were safe, Hijiri-kun said he'd help with the cleanup and ran toward the campfire. Some of the upperclassmen were tidying up along with the faculty advisors and the three guests.

``Can I go help too?''

``No, Gamma-san, don't. Hongo-senpai said the competitors for tomorrow have to stay here. There's no need for you to go out of your way to help. Especially after you got caught up in it, Gamma-san.''

After a moment of silence, Watari-kun spoke up.

``Who did it? Was it the Physics Club? Or the Chemistry Club?''

``Probably not the Chemistry Club. For the campfire, I think the Physics Club was in charge of the stacking while the Chemistry Club handled the contents. I even heard that Hongo-senpai changed the details at the last minute.''

As Osawa-kun spoke, Nanbu-kun countered him.

``An explosion of that scale can't be tested indoors. It would be impossible to rehearse without using the Physics Club's facilities.''

``Ah, now that you mention it, that's true.''

After Osawa-kun said that, the three of them fell silent in thought.

\textit{You can't control an explosion without knowledge of both chemistry and physics. I wondered whether the two clubs had prepared it together, but I didn't say so out loud.}

Del-chan, who would normally have offered an opinion at a time like this, stayed completely silent.

Not knowing what to say, all I could do was sit beside him.

$\delta$

While waiting for the minibus to the baths, I fought nausea the whole time.

It was fortunate that my stomach was empty, since I'd barely been able to eat my bento. But I felt like stomach acid would surge up the back of my throat if I opened my mouth, so I couldn't speak. Iwama watched me from beside me with a worried look.

\textit{It was pathetic. It had been the same when we entered the mountains at night. I was the one who was a coward, and Iwama was the one who pulled me along. For all that I was a creature of the shadows, I was no good with darkness.}

\textit{And yet, I had stepped into that darkness of my own accord.}

\textit{Into a gloom where not even moonlight reached.}

The campfire explosion was probably not unrelated to the scaffolding collapse. Even for the Faculty of Science Ori, known for its brutal trials, I couldn't believe two life-threatening incidents would happen back-to-back by mere coincidence. Some form of malice had to be involved.

\textit{If I had simply fallen from the scaffolding and died, how much better would that have been? But this time, Iwama had been put in danger. That was something that never should have happened.}

\textit{If Iwama were to be hurt because of me---the mere thought was terrifying. If Iwama ended up paying the price for what we did during Golden Week, I wouldn't be able to forgive myself even in death.}

\textit{This was the second time in my life I had ever felt this way. The first had been only two years ago. It was when my younger sister, Asahi, came down with a high fever from the COVID-19 I had probably brought home, and started saying her throat hurt too much for her to even drink water.}

\textit{I was still able to drink water myself, but I was so scared my stomach couldn't even keep that down. To think that I was so powerless, unable to do anything but watch as something precious was about to be lost before my eyes. To think that I had a heart so weak it could only tremble in fear.}

\textit{I hadn't changed at all since that summer in my second year of middle school.}

\textit{I didn't need strength like Hijiri's, but I at least wanted mental fortitude like Iwama's.}

\textit{What should I do now? How could I make sure no one else got hurt?}

As I stared down at the floor, I longed for enough clarity of mind to even think about it.

$\gamma$

The last minibus, carrying the next day's competitors aside from Togakushi-kun, along with the three guests and Mikage-senpai, left the school shortly after 9:30 \textsc{pm}. Togakushi-kun, Hongo-senpai, and Hyakuzawa-senpai were apparently heading back to the dorm for out-of-town students right next to the school (which was called ``Pandemonium'' for some reason).

I had assumed we'd be driven all the way to the bathhouse parking lot, but we were dropped off partway there. Apparently, Tokumura-sensei, the Biology Club advisor who was driving, had suddenly remembered an errand. The minibus made a U-turn as soon as it dropped us off.

``It's close, so shall we walk? I'm sorry to make even our guests walk.''

Mikage-senpai, his face still smudged with soot, spoke cheerfully and started off at the head of the group.

We got off right where the road led into the heart of the Chuo Shopping District. At the end of the street we were heading down stood the Symbol Tree, draped in illuminations that sparkled and flickered. It was the tree lit from 7:00 \textsc{pm} to 10:00 \textsc{pm}---the basis for the ``alibi'' that had been practically non-existent.

``That tree brings back memories. At Christmas, it gets decorated like crazy.''

Amid a group that wasn't in a very good mood, Bakuma-san spoke jovially. Claire-san, walking beside him, responded jokingly.

``Did you use it as a meeting spot for dates, by any chance?''

``Ahaha, I wonder.''

``I heard you were a quarterback, Bakuma-san. You must have been very popular.''

``Who did you hear that from? Well, that's true, but Claire, unlike high schools in the States, American football clubs aren't popular in Japan at all. I bet only the members and the managers even knew who the quarterback was.''

``Oh, so your girlfriend was a manager then?''

``You're quite the detective.''

The intimate romantic banter between the handsome man and the beautiful woman felt like something from another world. \textit{It was probably because of the explosion, but in the end, no one openly brought up Del-chan and me. Of course, that was much better than having a fuss made over us.}

We turned right at the Symbol Tree. That was when I noticed it---and I was surely the only one who did.

What was written on the sign had changed since noon.

\begin{center}
This illumination will be lit from 3:00 \textsc{pm} to 10:00 \textsc{pm} on Sunday, July 21st only.
\end{center}

Apparently, the lighting time was being moved up specifically for the next day. However, no reason was written.

\textit{In the first place, why had Tokumura-sensei balked at the short drive to the parking lot?}

While I was still wondering what that meant, we arrived at the bathhouse.

$\delta$

The bathhouse we visited was Natural Onsen Nagayu, a place my family used occasionally. The peak rush had already passed. Since we were the last group to be brought over, many students were already done. The spacious bathing area, with a sauna, a cold plunge, and multiple open-air baths, was easy to relax in.

Even so, Hijiri came over to me as I sat in a corner of the open-air bath. We were close enough that our shoulders almost touched.

``That was dangerous.''

He kept his voice low so the other customers around us couldn't hear. Even so, it was heavy with gravity.

``The matter is urgent. Could you come with me to the sauna?''

He probably wanted to speak in private. \textit{With my brain still feeling shrouded in fog,} I followed Hijiri.

We didn't go into the high-temperature sauna meant for large groups, but into a lower-temperature mist sauna. There was already one person in the small space, which could only seat six. It was Mikage-senpai.

``Hey. Sit closer. We don't have to worry about being overheard here.''

Hijiri sat next to Mikage-senpai, and I sat down beside him. Warm steam softly enveloped my whole body.

``Let me start by scolding you. You could have come to me for advice sooner, you know.''

Following Mikage-senpai's remark, Hijiri turned to explain things to me.

``I haven't shared the details yet, but I've informed Mikage-senpai of our concerns.''

``About the message, too?''

``I told him the fact that we received one. I haven't shared the actual content.''

Mikage-senpai gave a slow sigh.

``I know full well why you don't trust me. Nagisa did something awful during club recruitment, after all. The matter during Golden Week didn't go well, either. But I think the time is fast approaching when we'll need to join forces, properly and completely. This is no time for infighting.''

``For someone asking us to trust him, there still seem to be things about the Faculty of Science Ori you haven't told us. First, give us some information that makes us feel you're worthy of that trust.''

Mikage-senpai gave Hijiri a deep nod as he held firm in the negotiation.

``In my defense, I didn't fully grasp what was happening myself. Nagisa doesn't believe in reporting, sharing, or consulting. She wants to handle everything alone, saying things only get more complicated when other people know the situation and add new variables. It was the same this time. That's a failure on my part. I am truly sorry for that.''

Mikage-senpai bowed his head through the steam. Hijiri moved the conversation along as though the apology didn't matter.

``The message sent to us, the scaffolding collapse during the first task, and the explosion at the campfire. You can state with certainty that Hongo-senpai was not involved in any of these, correct?''

``Yeah. Of course. She wasn't involved.''

Something about the way he phrased it bothered me. Hijiri must have felt the same way, as he pressed further with a grim expression.

``Then first, could you explain the reason the scaffolding accident matched the contents of the game?''

``Certainly. It's simple enough. That was Nagisa's idea of a precaution.''

``A precaution?''

``Yeah. By building a scaffolding collapse into the game's content, you all ended up being careful when you crossed it, right? Nagisa said she had factored that in.''

``Wait, that's bizarre. Does that mean Hongo-senpai knew in advance that the scaffolding would be tampered with?''

``It seems she expected it. If you think about it, it makes sense, doesn't it? As Hijiri-kun also predicted, there was a strong possibility that someone was plotting to make the Faculty of Science Ori fail. And if there was anywhere an accident could be staged during the first task, that scaffolding was really the only option.''

That might well have been true. Anywhere else, the only real risk would have been a traffic accident.

``Nagisa intentionally built an obvious weak point into the course design to draw the enemy's attack there. And someone---though I don't know who---apparently took the bait exactly as she intended.''

If I believed that, then one mystery was solved. The accident on the scaffolding wasn't an imitation of the `Faculty of Science Ori Murder Case.' The order was reversed. The contents of that murder case had been constructed as a countermeasure against a crime that might happen.

But another question surfaced. Hijiri pointed it out.

``If that was possible, you could have prevented it. You could have checked the safety of the scaffolding repeatedly. You could have set up hidden cameras to capture irrefutable evidence of the tampering. Why didn't you do that?''

``To tell the truth, we did have a hidden camera set up. Except for the period between 12:15 and 13:10, when a moth on the lens kept anything from being recorded, it didn't capture any suspicious movement.''

Looked at the other way around, that meant any tampering done to the scaffolding during that window wouldn't have been caught.

``Why just a camera? You could have set up foolproof precautions.''

Even Mikage-senpai shrank his shoulders at Hijiri's harsh interrogation.

``It's hard to say, but... I think she felt it would be a waste to stop it. If an accident did happen, and she had the evidence in hand, she might be able to gain leverage over the culprit---and maybe even the person behind them, right? I suspect Nagisa had even that in her calculations.''

In other words, even if I had been seriously injured, that too would have fallen within Hongo-senpai's expectations.

While I sat there in total disbelief, Hijiri, surprisingly, seemed convinced.

``Making us stay on our guard while letting the culprit roam free so she could seize on their weakness. That was a pretty bold move.''

``I certainly never would have done anything like that. I won't ask you to forgive her, but I hope you can at least understand. As the price for having a mind that surpasses ordinary people, Nagisa is a little... lacking in the human heart department. There are times when she seems to think of her comrades' sacrifices as necessary costs.''

Senpai ran his fingers through his hair. Part of it had been burned short in an unnatural way.

I thought Hijiri would get angry on my behalf, but instead he pushed the conversation forward.

``Understood. Next, then, is the campfire explosion. I heard from the people in the chemistry club that Hongo-senpai changed the plan at the last minute.''

``That's right. She moved the setup farther from the school building than originally planned, and changed the approach from lighting the wood first to igniting the magnesium ribbon directly. So we used a turbo-type utility lighter instead of the traditional torches.''

``What was the purpose of that change?''

``To prepare for a possible explosion, she said. If it had been close to the school building, there was a risk of the fire spreading or windows breaking. And if the wood caught fire first, there was a chance it could explode the moment ignition took hold. The ground isn't soft enough to dig into on a whim, so if someone were going to plant explosives, the only place for them would be inside the wood.''

This was the second time I had been hit by disbelief. Hijiri put it into words.

``Does that mean Hongo-senpai even knew explosives were there?''

``It's not so much that she knew, but apparently it was just part of her safety planning. It only stands out because an explosion really did happen, but there were plenty of other minor last-minute changes too. Like replacing all the reagents for the chemistry competition with brand-new ones.''

I finally found the strength to speak and opened my mouth.

``She should have just cancelled it. The campfire, I mean. If there was even the slightest possibility that explosives had been planted, and a chance she might miss them, she shouldn't have lit the fire at all.''

Both Hijiri and Mikage-senpai looked at me. I felt as though I was the only one seeing it differently.

``Delta-kun, I understand how you feel. I could have lost my sight. Gamma-san could have been caught in it, too. But that campfire is a tradition that's been going on for decades. You can't just cancel it as dangerous without even explaining the circumstances.''

``Izuta, I agree with senpai on that. Our goal, after all, is to get rid of the troublemakers and make the Faculty of Science Ori a success. What would be the point in letting the sabotage win?''

``Even if there's a possibility that people might die?''

``Yes. If you avoid every possibility of people dying, you won't be able to do anything.''

``Isn't it a matter of degree? We'd already been hit by one malicious attack!''

``That's exactly why. We must never yield to terrorism. We must not give evil an opening it can exploit. Those who do evil will surely be punished in the name of justice. That is a fundamental global principle, isn't it?''

\textit{Hearing that unwavering reply, I finally understood. On this point, Hijiri and I would never truly understand each other. This time, Hijiri wasn't going to share my outrage over Hongo-senpai's actions.}

Because Hijiri had chosen Hongo-senpai's side.

``Understand this, Delta-kun. If this were just a Science Department tea party, I would have cancelled it without hesitation. But the Faculty of Science Ori is an important traditional event, and it's also a vital fundraising occasion where we invite outside guests. If we can secure donation prospects, we can restore the Science Department's standing within the school to some extent.''

He didn't explicitly add, ``The status that fell because of your actions,'' but I understood the implication perfectly well.

Still, I couldn't accept it.

``Do you intend to keep this up until someone dies? This is the kind of situation where calling the police would normally be the obvious thing to do.''

``If we called the police, the Faculty of Science Ori would be cancelled. That would be exactly what the culprit wants. We're not going to keep doing this until someone dies. We're going to see it through without letting anyone die.''

I wondered why we were so incapable of understanding each other.

``I'm sorry, but I can't understand this anymore. Are tradition, donations, and the department's status really things you want to protect even at the risk of human lives?''

No one answered me right away. The steam was thick, and I couldn't clearly make out the expressions on the two men's faces.

``...Then Delta-kun, let's look at it another way. Suppose we give in here, and the Faculty of Science Ori is cancelled and ends in failure, just as the enemy intends. What then? The culprit, who has already aimed their malice at us twice now, will get away scot-free, and they'll think, `the same trick will work again.'''

Mikage-senpai explained it in an entirely gentle tone. He was certainly right about that. I had no words in return.

``Our task is clear. We fight, and we win. We stop every act of sabotage before it happens, and we identify and catch the culprit. Just as you fear, Delta-kun, if there's a second time, there will likely be a third. But you could also say that would be our chance to catch the culprit.''

``But we don't even know who's doing it or how, right?''

``We already have several pieces of physical evidence. If we think it through, we should be able to narrow the culprit down.''

Senpai held up two fingers. Folding them down one by one, he spoke.

``First of all, I've arranged for the scaffolding we secured to be delivered to the school tomorrow morning. And we've also analyzed the residue from the campfire explosion. What was used was an improvised bomb made from a mixture of ammonium nitrate and aluminum powder. They likely increased its explosive power by sealing it in a glass container.''

Hijiri nodded as if he had no particular doubts, but something caught on me.

``How can you know that? Even after it exploded?''

``I'll show you tomorrow. We have a secret analysis device at our clubroom.''

``So, do you have a lead on the culprit?''

Before I could ask for details, Hijiri pressed the conversation forward.

``It would be someone who was able to tamper with the scaffolding and was involved in setting up the campfire. We can narrow it down quite a bit with just that.''

``What about the possibility that it was one of the invitees?''

Hijiri then got my consent and told Mikage-senpai about the contents of the message cards.

That he and I had each been given one half of a black card on the same day. That the cards contained a warning that an impostor was hiding among the invitees, along with a challenge to find them in secret.

``...That's important information. But on one point, if we assume everything you're saying is true, then Bakuma-san and Kurauchi-san---strong suspects though they are---aren't the ones who planted the cards. On that Saturday, the two of them were helping us prepare for the Faculty of Science Ori.''

``If there's an accomplice, it's entirely possible.''

``That's true. But it's strange. Why would the culprit go that far and send a message beforehand just to put you on your guard? Was it meant to be a challenge? If it was done by an invitee, that person would have exposed their own plan to sabotage the Faculty of Science Ori to a ridiculous degree of risk.''

Mikage-senpai's reasoning was sound. If they wanted to make the Faculty of Science Ori fail while pinning the blame on the department itself, it was hard to imagine they would send a message in advance prompting us to suspect outsiders. The disadvantage was too great, and there was virtually no benefit. But more than that, I was curious.

``Bakuma-san and Kurauchi-san knew in advance what we were going to do at the Faculty of Science Ori, didn't they?''

``Yeah. Since they're alumni, they've been helping us for a while now. In that sense, they're quite suspicious. The idea of targeting the scaffolding would have occurred to those two ahead of time, and they could have planned in advance how to hide a bomb in the campfire.''

Hijiri leaned forward and asked.

``What specifically did they help with? I already heard that Bakuma-san arranged for the contractor to set up the scaffolding.''

``That's about it for Bakuma-san. He's more of a humanities type---or rather, the athletic type. Kurauchi-san provided metallic materials like gallium and bismuth, as well as materials for thermite reactions. Through his company, of course.''

Mikage-senpai stopped Hijiri before he could open his mouth again.

``I know what you want to say. The bomb's components included aluminum powder. But that alone would be weak evidence. Aluminum powder is a hazardous substance, but if you want to get your hands on it, you can still buy it even if you don't work for a chemical manufacturer.''

Mikage-senpai rose smoothly to his feet.

``Let's head out soon. First, be there tomorrow morning to witness the verification of the scaffolding. We'll start from there.''

I was already drenched in sweat and close to my limit. The three of us left the mist sauna.

Mikage-senpai poured water over his head and went straight for the cold bath. Hijiri, however, said that cooling off outside would be better, and after rinsing himself with warm water, he led me back out.

``I'm sure that wasn't the conclusion you were hoping for. I'm sorry for dismissing your feelings, Izuta.''

Hijiri gave that apology as soon as we sat down in adjacent deck chairs. It was true that my feelings had been dismissed, but since there was no point in saying so, I remained silent.

``Of course, it's not that there was anything wrong with what I said. But I'm well aware that your argument is correct too, Izuta. That's the kind of person you are. You have imagination, a sense of responsibility, and above all else, you're very kind. I want you to stay that way, without changing.''

In other words, he was likely saying that even though our opinions had clashed and his had carried the discussion, he didn't mean to reject me, and this wasn't a falling out.

``People don't change that easily.''

``You're right. I know that better than anyone.''

Hijiri gave a resigned smile, then continued.

``When the scaffolding incident was followed by the explosion, and you and Iwama-san were put in danger, I surprised even myself. The only thing I felt was pure anger. There wasn't a shred of fear in my heart the way there was in yours, Izuta.''

``If I'm killed, are you the type who won't shed a single tear, Hijiri?''

``Probably. I wouldn't have the luxury of crying; I'd devote all my energy to finding the person who killed you, Izuta.''

``Then I can die in peace.''

Even as I spoke sarcastically, I was remembering Iwama during Golden Week.

\textit{Thinking of Iwama, who had boasted that if being afraid didn't improve the outcome, there was no point in fear.}

\textit{Both Iwama and Hijiri surely had minds fundamentally different from mine.}

``Science types would probably get mad at me for saying this, but I believe the human heart is more powerful than a nuclear reactor. Whether you let that power emerge naturally without forcing it, or control it and put it to use for the sake of a desired result... that's where we are fundamentally different.''

The former was me, and the latter was Hijiri. I reacted like an ordinary human being. I was afraid of the dark, and I felt terror when someone precious was exposed to danger. But Hijiri wasn't like that. He didn't fear the dark, and when a comrade was in danger, he used his anger as fuel to hunt down the person responsible.

\textit{People who walk in the sun must live in a way where that sort of thing is required of them, until it becomes second nature. He likely had no choice but to feel emotions for other people's sake---the emotions others demanded of him. Because if he didn't, he couldn't be a hero.}

My heart was wavering.

``...I'll follow you and Mikage-senpai this time. But let me say one thing.''

Hijiri nodded for me to continue. I stood up and said just one thing.

``Other than us, absolutely no one can be allowed to get hurt.''

$\gamma$

While I was in the carbonated bath with Mikage-san, Claire-san came over to us.

``May I join you?''

There was no reason to refuse, so I nodded right away, but I worried whether I had managed to hide my surprise. Of course, I knew it was wrong to stare at other people's bodies. But Claire-san was something else. In a place that made me question whether it was really okay to go to high school with piercings still in, there were silver piercings. More than one of them, too. It was a relief that they were in places that would never be visible outside her clothes.

\textit{Was this normal in America?}

``Those are pretty stylish,'' Mikage-san remarked, unfazed. Since we were in the bath, the only thing she could have been referring to was the piercings.

``Hehe. Thank you. I really hate tattoos, but I like these. They actually don't hurt as much as they look.''

Even with her saying that, I still couldn't imagine ever wanting one myself. Especially the ones lower down.

``You dress up even underneath your clothes,'' I said timidly, and Claire-san answered with a bright smile.

``When I look at myself naked in the mirror, my eyes always go to the sparkly parts. You didn't notice these, right?''

Claire-san lifted her hips slightly and leaned toward us.

That was when I noticed. Around the area where the piercings were, there were several small round marks about the size of a fingertip. Were they burns? Her beautiful white skin looked even paler there, while the outlines were slightly darker. They looked almost like bubbles floating on her skin.

After staring a moment too long, I remembered it was a place I had no business looking at and averted my eyes. But---I wondered. Why did she have burns in a place like that? In a place that should never be visible under clothing.

The burn marks looked about the right size for the tip of a cigarette.

``Don't make that face, Rio. It ruins your pretty face! It's all in the past now. I don't even see it in my dreams anymore. It was ten years ago, after all.''

``Was it an ex-boyfriend?''

\textit{How could you even ask that, Mikage-san...?}

``Ahaha, you two shouldn't let yourselves get caught by bad men.''

After saying that, Claire-san narrowed her eyes as though remembering the past.

``My country was a very terrible place. That's why I left.''

Claire-san had left America and was now working in Japan. \textit{I wondered what kind of experience she'd had over there ten years ago. I hoped Japan wasn't a terrible place.}

I didn't know how she interpreted my expression, but Claire-san peered into my eyes through her long eyelashes.

``Don't worry. I didn't come here this time to look for a boyfriend or anything.''

Of course. Naturally, she was probably just teasing us to lighten the mood.

``But you seemed to take a liking to Izuta-kun,'' Mikage-san said.

\textit{What had gotten into you, Mikage-san? Was she always this aggressive in conversation? Was she the type to get bold once she took her clothes off?}

``Oh, Sho? He certainly is a cute boy. If no one has caught him in three years, maybe I'll throw my name in.''

With an ``Ahaha,'' Claire-san winked at me as I stood there stunned.

``I'm joking. I'll be saying a proper goodbye to Sho tomorrow, anyway.''

$\delta$

That night, I had a dream.

In a flower field where colorful blossoms bloomed like a painting, Iwama was laughing happily. Her gaze, which had been turned toward someone else or a large crowd, eventually shifted to me. That perfect ``Did you see that smile?'' expression everyone knew softened gently in that moment. Iwama ran toward me. A warm wind was blowing.

Suddenly, that wind was swallowed by pitch black. It was a blast. An impact that shook my skull. As the blast vanished as if it had never been there, the scenery returned to the bright flower field. Iwama was standing right there beside me, just as before.

With that smile meant only for me still plastered across her face, the top half of her head had been gouged away---

I woke up.

I had been lying in a sleeping bag on top of a cushioned sheet spread over the hard classroom floor. The Faculty of Science Ori apparently included an overnight stay at the school under the pretext of conducting the annual disaster prevention equipment inspection. It was about as comfortable as a disaster drill.

I left the classroom, careful not to step on the guys sleeping nearby. In the dark hallway, I took several deep breaths to steady my ragged breathing. \textit{What a dream I'd had.}

``Bathroom?''

Mikage was standing there in a jersey. Her hair was down.

``...Something like that.''

``I'll go with you.''

\textit{Apparently, I had the kind of constitution that kept blessing me with chances to go to the bathroom with girls.} I followed Mikage as she immediately started walking ahead. Mikage went up the stairs.

``Is the bathroom downstairs not good enough?''

``We can't have a secret conversation in a place everyone uses.''

``You're planning to have a secret conversation in a bathroom?''

``Is that a problem?''

More than it being a problem, since we were different genders, one of us would be committing a crime. Even if we used the multi-purpose bathroom, it would be a disaster if someone saw us.

My concerns were off the mark, as Mikage kept climbing the stairs. She passed the fourth floor, the top level, and opened the door leading to the rooftop. The door had a small bolt on it, but it wasn't locked.

``What about the bathroom?''

``Maybe you didn't really need to go in the first place?''

That was true enough. We wandered over to the fence. The wire mesh only came up to about chest height, perfect for leaning on with our elbows. A bright moon hung in the western sky. It was almost full.

``There's one thing I want to ask you.''

Under the moonlight, Mikage began in a suggestive tone.

``Delta-kun, ten years ago, did you ever strip a pretty white girl naked and burn her with cigarettes?''

``What are you talking about? I was only six back then.''

``I see. By the way, do you have any tattoos?''

``Do I look like I do?''

``You can't know for sure until you actually look.''

Mikage stared intently at my upper body.

``I'm not taking my clothes off.''

``That's a shame.''

I had no idea what, exactly, she'd suspected me of, but apparently her doubts had been cleared. Mikage fell silent for a while and looked up at the moon. \textit{I figured she still hadn't gotten to the real point yet.}

``Hey, Delta-kun. Want to join forces with me from here on?''

The sudden offer caught me off guard.

``Aren't we already on the same team?''

``That's not what I mean. To do what needs to be done at this school, will you work with me?''

Part of me thought it was an overblown way to put it, but I hated how literally I understood it.

``\dots Team up with Hijiri. I can't do much.''

``Oh, I'll absolutely be making use of Hijiri-kun. But he's not the one I want. He only moves according to his own convictions. What I want is someone who stands where I stand, someone who'll help me move the people on center stage from behind the scenes. Someone who'll run through the dark backstage with me.''

``You make it sound like you want to become some kind of fixer in the shadows.''

``If my brother retires, I'll have to take over eventually.''

She didn't deny it. \textit{Was she serious?}

\textit{Did she understand how hard it would be to shoulder that responsibility in a place this abnormal?}

``You don't need me for that.''

``Delta-kun, you're already past the point where you can stay uninvolved.''

I had no response. She was right. I had already stepped deep into the darkness.

``My brother told me everything earlier. I can help you. We can share our purpose, our information, our feelings---everything---and fight together. I won't force some ruthless version of justice on you the way Hijiri-kun would.''

``I appreciate that, but I'm sure I won't be as useful as you think.''

``No. That's not true.''

Mikage slowly turned toward me. Her profile was lit by the bright moon.

``Because I know there's a wolf inside you, gentle Delta-kun.''

``At most, it's probably just a puppy.''

Mikage shook her head.

``This is just my personal theory, but the gentle big brother type is the strongest.''

Still looking up at the moon, just shy of full, Mikage continued.

``A truly strong wolf protects the pack. It risks its life to protect its own family and companions. Not for itself, and not for the world, but for the sake of what matters most to it---that's when it reveals its terrifying strength and fights. I think my brother must have seen a wolf like that in you, Delta-kun.''

``I'm not as devoted to little sisters as your brother is, and I'm not that strong either.''

``Have you never found it strange? Whenever my brother or that woman had something important to discuss with Delta-kun, why was I always there too?''

I thought back.

When I protested to Hongo-senpai over Iwama's club choice.

When Mikage-senpai and Hongo-senpai told me the full story behind the Tengu Festival Incident.

Mikage had been right beside me, silently listening to everything. As though it were only natural for her to be present at those confidential meetings.

``\dots Now that I think about it, that is strange.''

``My brother wanted us to share secrets and join forces. And he knew we inevitably would.''

``You say we share secrets, but I don't know any of your secrets.''

``Then I'll tell you one.''

Mikage pushed herself away from the fence, spun lightly, and slipped behind me in one fluid motion. Her hands came to rest on either side of me, just outside my elbows. I felt her weight against my back. Then she whispered in my ear.

``My brother will tell me anything if I ask. Even something like this---the trophy for the third task will be placed at the highest point in the school. Which means, there.''

She pointed to the top of the door leading to the rooftop. A small space raised even higher than the roof itself. It certainly was the highest point in the school building.

``That's... if you know that in advance, it's unfair.''

``Our goal isn't to win as Team X. Our goal is to remove the saboteur without putting anyone in danger, and bring the Faculty of Science Ori to a successful close. And for that, I'm sure we'll need this information.''

I thought it over. Knowing the destination of the third task meant knowing where the other competitors would be headed. If we wanted to eliminate the saboteur without exposing anyone to danger, then we could deliberately go somewhere else and make the saboteur want to target that location instead.

\textit{So we bait the culprit out.}

``Don't you think that's a pretty good idea?''

``\dots Watari's on Team X. I don't want to drag him into this. He's an important friend to me, for all that.''

``I know. Let me help you figure out a way forward.''

Still holding me from behind, Mikage used one hand to tilt my chin upward.

Whether I liked it or not, the moon filled the center of my vision.

``Tomorrow night, the full moon will be out.''

As though she were introducing me to the world of night, Mikage kept making me look at the moon.

\textit{Maybe it was the moon I had been searching for all this time without realizing it.}

``If it's the two of us, I'm sure we can build it. I'm sure we can come up with a truly special logic.''

\fullpageimage{10.jpg}

% ==============================
%        Chapter 4
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Chapter 4\\
    The Two Vs
\end{center}
\label{sec:ch4V3}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Chapter 4}
\vspace{1cm}

$\delta$

Early in the morning, while most of the students were still asleep, Hijiri---who said he hadn't slept a wink---woke me up and took me to the area behind the school grounds. It was the place where I had happened to run into Iwama in the spring and ended up going to look for cherry blossoms with her.

Mikage-senpai and a second-year from the Physics Club, Hyakuzawa-senpai, were already waiting.

``Good morning. Those just arrived.''

Mikage-senpai pointed to a pile of metal pipes and treadboards stacked nearby.

``Don't worry. Ringo-chan is fine. She's trustworthy, and she's essential for this verification.''

It was a muggy morning, but Hyakuzawa-senpai had shown up in this lush green spot wearing loungewear. Specifically, a tank top and dolphin shorts---a pretty revealing outfit. She was even wearing sandals.

``You should have told me the first-years were coming, too.''

While muttering her dissatisfaction, Hyakuzawa-senpai slapped and crushed a mosquito that had landed on her thigh without even looking at it.

``Oh, didn't I mention it? Well, it's fine, isn't it? Delta-kun, Hijiri-kun---this Ringo-chan here is the `secret analysis device' I told you about yesterday, the antithesis of every scientific trick.''

It was an exaggerated way to put it, but this was the person who could split a potato rolling fifty meters away clean in half with another potato she'd launched herself. There was probably some reason for the claim. I started by asking a question.

``Is it true that you were able to identify the raw materials and structure of the bomb from yesterday's explosion?''

Hyakuzawa-senpai exhaled a weary breath.

``It's true. You want to know how I did it, right? To put it simply, from the airborne by-products. Plus, minute glass fragments mixed into the sand. If I go into the details, it'll turn into a fifty-minute lecture, so do you want to hear it?''

She said it in a tone that suggested she really didn't want to explain. Mikage-senpai provided a supplement.

``You two already know Ringo-chan's special skill pretty well. She gave a flashy performance yesterday, after all. But actually, that's not where the essence of this girl's ability lies.''

``Where does it lie, then?''

It seemed this was something even Hijiri, a member of the Physics Club, didn't know.

``It's not calculation. It's analysis. Ringo-chan has eyes that can distinguish the slightest differences in color, a nose that can sniff out even cyanide compounds, a tongue that knows the taste of tetrodotoxin, and skin that can sense minute differences in temperature---her whole body is a precision analytical instrument. She is a treasure of humanity.''

``Please don't go blabbing about people's secrets. Especially when you stubbornly refuse to share anything about yourself.''

``Now, now. I don't have anything I could call a special skill like that, so it can't be helped.''

``Tetrodotoxin should be tasteless and odorless, though.''

When I cut in to point that out, Hyakuzawa-senpai gave a wry smile.

``It makes your nerves prickle. Want me to let you try some sometime if you're that curious?''

``...I'm fine, thanks.''

\textit{I figured it was best to take Mikage-senpai's words with a grain of salt, but after yesterday's incident, there was no doubt that Hyakuzawa-senpai---who was from outside the prefecture---possessed some kind of extraordinary talent.}

``Convinced now? This is just my guess, but I think the explosives were sealed in glass because after an explosion, glass shatters into fragments as fine as sand, which makes the evidence hard to find. The culprit is quite calculating.''

If it were sealed in metal, fragments would remain. It would immediately become obvious that someone had planted a bomb that wasn't supposed to be there. \textit{As expected, the culprit wanted to make it look like an accident caused by the Science Department.}

Hijiri turned his eyes toward the scaffolding materials.

``Have you already finished the analysis on these?''

``We're just about to start. The treadboard that fell is the one with the river mud on it.''

Mikage-senpai pulled one of the treadboards from the bundle of materials. It was the board that had fallen into the river when I stepped on it yesterday, and which Bakuma-san had retrieved afterward.

``And these two short pipes were part of the framework supporting this treadboard. Looking at the footage, it seems the joint holding one of these pipes came loose under Delta-kun's weight, and the treadboard dropped toward the river.''

Mikage-senpai showed us a video on his smartphone. One joint had come off, and a pipe was hanging down clumsily. In other words, this joint had been loose.

``Which joint was the one that came off?''

When I asked, Mikage-senpai shrugged his shoulders regretfully.

``It seems to be missing. Maybe it fell into the river and got buried in the mud, or maybe it was taken away.''

Hyakuzawa-senpai silently operated the screen of Mikage-senpai's phone to enlarge the video, staring intently at the hanging pipe. Then, without hesitation, she picked up one of the two pipes lying at her feet and examined one end of it. She then turned her back to us and did something.

\textit{To me, it looked like she was licking the pipe.}

After spitting on the ground, she turned back to us.

``I've figured out the trick. It's wax and gallium.''

Hyakuzawa-senpai said it matter-of-factly. Mikage-senpai's eyes widened.

``I see! It was stuck to the pipe, wasn't it?''

``Yes. In trace amounts. The gallium soaked into it rather than merely sticking to the surface.''

\textit{So that was it. I understood completely. I'd save for later the question of whether someone could really distinguish wax and gallium just by licking them; what mattered now was that there was a possible trick involving those two things.}

``Is the melting point of wax around fifty degrees Celsius?''

When I asked, Hyakuzawa-senpai nodded.

``It's probably around sixty degrees, but at fifty, it'll start to lose its shape.''

\textit{I see. If that was the case, the joint could be detached without anyone noticing. It was a time-delay device cleverly designed around precise scientific knowledge. In other words, the culprit was...}

``Wait, Izuta. I'm embarrassed to say it, but I'm probably the only one who isn't following along.''

Seeing the confusion on Hijiri's face, I started to explain.

``It wasn't a teleporter. It was a trick that could be pulled off with modern technology---''

$\gamma$

It was 1:00 p.m. Team Y's start was less than ten minutes away. The starting point was the school gate. Once the time came, we could head straight out of the school.

``We're about to start, but do you have a minute?''

Del-chan, who had changed into athletic wear just like us, called out to me. Team X was scheduled to start eight minutes after Team Y.

``Of course!''

As if avoiding Hijiri-kun's and Togakushi-kun's eyes, Del-chan moved a little ways off. We faced each other head-on. Del-chan's black eyes stared intently at me through his lenses.

``This is the perfect chance to show what you can really do. Please, give it everything you've got.''

\textit{Whatever I had expected him to say, it turned out to be words of encouragement.}

``Yeah, I'll do my best. You do your best too, Del-chan.''

``Of course. As for the strategy, stick to what we discussed. Other than that, I want you to go all out.''

``Really? If I go all out, things might get pretty crazy.''

I said it jokingly, but Del-chan nodded with total seriousness.

``That's exactly what I want. There's no need to hold back, even in front of Hijiri or Togakushi. I don't care at all if I, or Mizasaki and the others, end up looking inferior. Stand out as much as you want and become the star of the Science Dept Ori.''

``But me, the star...''

As I stammered, Del-chan spoke with strength.

``I think you shine brightest when you're completely absorbed in what you love and not holding back for anyone. Please, let that radiance shine as much as you want and make this final competition unforgettable.''

\textit{Hearing him say that to my face made my cheeks burn.}

``...Th-thank you. I got it.''

\textit{Since he had gone out of his way to say that to me so seriously here, this had to be how Del-chan truly felt. He clearly understood what had been holding me back. On top of that, he was fully validating my ``likes'' and giving me a push.}

\textit{He was telling me to put everything I loved on full display in this match.}

``Well then. I'm looking forward to it.''

With that, Del-chan returned to Team X. I went back to the school gate as well.
