Hijiri-kun had the LiveU strapped to his back and a palm-sized video camera in his right hand. I carried the backpack we'd been given yesterday. It was a little heavy since it contained spare batteries and drinking water for the three of us.

Regarding the third task, Hongo-senpai had given us an explanation at 10:00 a.m.

``The final battle, the third task, is `Engineering Orienteering!' The rules are simple. Follow the clues scattered throughout the town toward the goal, and the first team to get their hands on the Championship Cup wins!''

Then, senpai explained the special rules for this occasion.

\begin{center}
\textbf{Special Rules for the Third Task (Immediate disqualification for violations!)}
\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\item No running
\item Stay together as a group of three
\item Do not stop the camera
\end{itemize}

The third rule was the important one. This time, there wouldn't be a camera crew following the teams; instead, we had to continuously transmit the footage we filmed ourselves back to the school. Fortunately, Watari-kun from Team X, Hijiri-kun from Team Y, and Osawa-kun from Team Z had received special training (?) in the Physics Club and knew how to handle filming. A Physics Club member from each team was assigned to the camera. Through follow-up questions, it had been confirmed that a brisk walk, as long as one foot stayed on the ground, was permitted, that it was fine to go to the bathroom alone, and that it wouldn't be a problem if the camera stopped briefly for a battery replacement.

1:09 p.m. Only one minute remained until the start.

Team Z had started ninety minutes earlier, carrying luggage with almost the same contents as what we'd been given yesterday (except for the one-day bus pass), along with the flip phone and calculator obtained in the second task.

\textit{But if my guess was right, my calculations said we could still catch up. The rule requiring a thirty-minute lunch break applied to the third task as well, but since noon had come before our start, we were told that eating our bento boxes inside the school would satisfy that requirement. And above all, there was that gimmick.}

``Are you ready?''

When I called out, Hijiri-kun and Togakushi-kun nodded firmly.

Hongo-senpai blew a sharp blast on her whistle.

``Let's go!''

Our first destination was already decided.

\textit{I had already solved the code riddle written on the back of the investigation materials I'd obtained in the first task.}

$\delta$

After breakfast, I called out to Iwama to stop her.

``I'd like to talk to you for a bit, just the two of us. Is that okay?''

``Yeah, sure! Where to?''

``How about the empty lot behind the biology room? It's better if we aren't in the public eye.''

Since I couldn't exactly invite her to the bathroom, it ended up sounding rather suggestive, but Iwama followed along without a second thought. Both of us were in our athletic wear. We sat down right there on the slightly raised grassy slope.

``Del-chan, don't you look a little better?''

``Yeah. It's because I ate a solid breakfast.''

Last night I'd had less than no appetite, but this morning I'd eaten like a new man. \textit{I was in top form.}

``The mystery of the code written on the back of the investigation materials---you haven't solved it yet because you're still lacking information, right?''

When I broached the subject, Iwama looked a bit troubled before nodding cautiously.

``Actually, yesterday, Kannabi said something to me that sounded meaningful. That it's simple if you can see the whole picture, and that if I want to solve the code, I should try talking to Iwama.''

Iwama looked a bit surprised. And for good reason. Right now, we were enemies. In any normal sense, talking about the tasks would be strictly forbidden.

``I didn't really know what she meant, but did she say anything similar to you, Iwama?''

``No. To begin with, the two of us never got a chance to talk alone yesterday.''

\textit{The fact that she'd given Kannabi a beetle still seemed to be a secret as far as Iwama was concerned. Knowing her, she had probably forced the beetle on Kannabi as they passed each other and then hurried off at once.}

\textit{Of course, I couldn't say a word either about how I'd given Kannabi a jewel beetle.}

``What did you think, Iwama, after hearing that?''

``Um, the whole picture, right? I wonder...''

``Sorry for bringing up something weird. It must be hard to talk about when it feels like betraying your teammates.''

``Don't apologize. But you're right, the tasks are a little hard to talk about... Why not try asking Rei again?''

``I don't think she'll be speaking to me for a while.''

``Eh? Why?''

``There was an incredibly unfortunate accident.''

Iwama seemed willing to accept that explanation. The conversation fell quiet. I searched for an opening.

\begin{center}
Find the path by relying on a voice you cannot hear.

Listen closely, borrowing the giant's ears.

Across coordinates stretching endlessly over the land, invisible waves show the way.
\end{center}

This was the entirety of the code Team X had. But it couldn't be solved with this information alone.

``Team Z seems to have already figured it out. Since they were only watching through the cameras, they shouldn't have seen anything more than we did. There shouldn't be any need to do something like heating up the investigation materials to reveal hidden ink.''

``...But right now, we're lacking information.''

``And Kannabi from Team Z is telling us to look at the whole picture. Which means---''

``That Team X and Team Y each have different information?''

As expected of Iwama.

``That's what I thought too. The fact that only Team Z figured it out while we're still missing information means each team is holding key pieces of the puzzle without realizing it.''

``But that's strange. We were supposed to have visited the same checkpoints, and Hongo-senpai said the exact same information was in the exact same places...''

``That's the thing.''

---The investigation materials are provided in two completely identical sets, both front and back; please take only one set.

They'd made us read that over and over during the first task. So how could we have ended up with different information?

``I happened to hear something from Mizasaki. Apparently, the camera crews for the first task were just the two teams following us and one team stationed at each checkpoint.''

---The cameras were only the ones following Team X and Team Y, and the ones waiting at each checkpoint. They were all handheld by the cameramen.

``Eh? Then something's wrong. There were six or more cameras.''

Iwama leaned forward, suddenly animated. Exactly.

---Camera Six, can you show the places it's okay for the selection team to see?

Mikage-senpai had certainly called out like that when he showed us the sub-control room.

``Weren't there four checkpoints? We thought we'd visited the exact same three places, but in reality, each team visited one different location.''

``The tunnel! Del-chan, did Team X go to a tunnel?''

``Yeah. We went to the Koshizaki Tunnel.''

``I knew it! The one we went to was the Iizaki Tunnel. Why didn't I notice? If Team X had gone there first, there shouldn't have been two options left.''

``...What do you mean?''

``In the tunnel, we had to choose between liquid metal and bismuth and place it on the periodic table, but if Team X had been there first, one of those options should've already been gone, right?''

``I see, that's true. Once an option was chosen, the system didn't restore it.''

At the station Team Y had visited first, one of the composite resistance problems had already been solved, and at Kannon Cave, the center of gravity for the three evergreen oaks had already been dug up. Of course, since Team Y had been ahead in everything except the tunnel, they probably had no way of knowing for sure that the system didn't restore options.

``So you mean even the test questions for Problem III were different?''

``Most likely. Was Team Y's problem also about DNA?''

Iwama looked thoughtful for a moment, then reached into her pocket and pulled out a small, folded piece of photocopy paper.

``Yes. This is the sequence from the start codon to the stop codon.''

I read it. Beside it was the character string she had apparently deciphered.

\begin{center}
ATG ACA CAC CGG GAA GAG CAC CTG GTC AGT TAA

THREEHLVS
\end{center}

``...It's different. We had THREEQTRS, which meant `three quarters,' or $\frac{3}{4}$.''

``We read ours as `three halves,' so that made it $\frac{3}{2}$.''

``So the base sequences in the problems were different?''

``Then the DNA had mutated.''

A mutation... I guess you could describe it that way. If the base sequence changes, the resulting amino acid sequence changes as well. That's something that happens all the time with real DNA. Building differences into a DNA-themed problem like that---the person who wrote these questions has style. If each department head prepared one question, then maybe Karato-senpai was the one who made Problem III. She's not to be underestimated.

``The problem statements themselves were different, we visited different checkpoints, and I'm sure we got different investigation materials. The code had four lines in total.''

Iwama thought for a moment longer, then pulled another piece of paper from her pocket.

Three lines of the code were written there. And the final line was one I hadn't seen before.

\begin{center}
Seek the path by listening to unheard voices.

Listen closely with the help of a giant's ears.

From the bridge where water does not flow, eighty million words whisper.
\end{center}

``This was the third line written on the back of the investigation materials we got in the tunnel.''

``Just as I thought, they're different. Ours was like this.''

I borrowed a pencil from Iwama and wrote Team X's third line beside it. At last, the whole picture came into view. Once I focused on just the last two lines, something interesting jumped out.

\begin{center}
At the coordinates where six repeats forever, an invisible wave points the way.

From the bridge where water does not flow, eighty million words whisper.
\end{center}

``It wasn't `land' (陸)! If you line it up with the `eight' (捌), you can see it. This is `six' (六)! It's the formal form of the kanji!''

``So that's what `eighty million' meant! It's a radio frequency! 80 megahertz! FM!''

Putting the two together made everything click. It had been built as a riddle from the start.

``Then the coordinates where six repeats forever would mean...''

As I tried to recall the map, Iwama spoke up.

``It's probably the station. The station was $\frac{2}{3}$, so in decimal form that's $0.666$...''

``There was an overpass at the station. One that crosses the tracks instead of a river---a bridge where water doesn't flow.''

Iwama beamed.

``So all we have to do is go to Tsunanagai Station and pick up the 80 megahertz signal from the overpass!''

$\gamma$

For me, after devouring anything science-related I could find, electronics felt like a doorway into science I could open even at home. When you put together a bunch of inorganic parts that couldn't do anything on their own, they turned into a circuit that could do surprisingly clever things. It almost felt like magic.

More than anything, I still vividly remembered making a homemade germanium radio. Just by combining a few simple parts, without even using a battery, voices would come spilling out of the unseen air. To think there was that much information flying all around me! It really did feel like I was borrowing a giant's ears to hear voices I normally never could.

I was having so much fun that I listened to the radio constantly, to the point where my father scolded me for it.

``If you use an FM transmitter, you can send out any audio source you want as an FM signal over a small area. I think they set it up so it can only be picked up from the overpass.''

We couldn't use the bus today. After hurrying to the station along our usual route to school, we immediately climbed the stairs to the overpass. I already had my radio ready to go. It was tuned to 80.0 megahertz, right in the FM band. Since ``mega'' meant million, that was exactly ``eighty million'' hertz.

I'd been put in charge of the third task. Togakushi-kun said he wasn't very good at anything that couldn't be done on paper, and Hijiri-kun didn't know much about hands-on engineering either.

``Iwama-san's the right person for this one. Let me film your big moment.''

That was what he said. With the camera trained on me, I put the earphone in my right ear and stepped out front.

The earphone looked a bit clunky. The monaural earphone I'd been given at first was only twenty centimeters long, which was nowhere near long enough to use as an earphone antenna. To receive FM clearly, I needed about a meter of metal---roughly one-fourth of the wavelength.

That was why Del-chan had cut off the right side of a one-meter stereo earphone and given it to me. He cut the monaural earphone in the middle, stripped the coating from the plug side, and soldered it to the right side of the stereo earphone, where the conductor had been exposed the same way (the solder and soldering iron had been provided in the waiting room). That gave us a monaural earphone more than a meter long.

The sky was clear. The merciless summer sun beat down on the overpass. Looking at the sea beyond the bypass, I focused on the sound coming into my right ear through the earphone.

In another ten minutes, Del-chan and the rest of Team X should arrive here. I wondered who would wear the earphone then. Watari-kun was in charge of the camera, so it would be Del-chan or Mikage-san. I hoped it would be Del-chan. He would probably put the other half of the original stereo earphone in his left ear and listen closely, just like I was doing. With a slight delay, we would surely hear the same sound. Using the same earphone.

\textit{It was almost like we were a couple sharing wired earphones---but maybe I was overthinking it.}

And then... I heard it!

It sounded like they were using VOICEROID. A woman's voice was repeating the same words.

【\dots\dots Circle the Central Library once. It can only be seen with colored glasses.】

``I heard it!''

Hijiri-kun, who normally would've demanded the answer right away, didn't reply because he was too busy filming my face. Togakushi-kun asked quickly.

``Where to next?''

``Tsunanagai City Central Library!''

$\delta$

``Let's have a man-to-man talk.''

After handing the earphone over to Iwama, I called out to Mizasaki. Mizasaki nodded readily.

``Of course. Let's take a walk outside.''

As we changed into our shoes and walked around the school building, Mizasaki spoke first.

``Hey, Delta, you aren't still helping Asahi-chan change her clothes, are you?''

``Don't be stupid. She's in her third year of middle school now.''

``Good. Well, Navi-san told me to make sure, just in case.''

\textit{It seemed I'd gotten tangled up in a terrible misunderstanding. That had been a truly unfortunate accident---in fact, it was the first thing in my life I wouldn't have been able to forget even if I'd wanted to. And I had no intention of ever doing anything like that again.}

``I wanted to talk about the competition.''

When I brought it up, Mizasaki's expression tightened slightly. It was a look I didn't see often.

``What, is this already a declaration of defeat?''

``Something like that. It doesn't look like Team X can win anymore. The gap between us and Team Y is obvious, and we're a hundred minutes behind Team Z.''

Mizasaki puffed out his chest proudly.

``We won the second task by a landslide, after all. We were pretty amazing, weren't we?''

``Yeah. You were amazing. Coming up with salicylic acid...''

``Well, that was a bit unfair to Delta and his team. I got the idea after seeing Togakushi from Team Y get headache medicine, but Team X had no way of knowing about that.''

``It's a no-holds-barred competition. That's exactly how we should be playing, isn't it?''

``True. So, now that you've admitted defeat, what do you plan to do?''

``Apparently, Team Y still plans to beat you guys.''

For a few steps, he said nothing. \textit{Mizasaki must have really meant it when he said he wanted to win.}

``...You mean they have a calculation for how to win?''

``At least Iwama seems to think so. Apparently, the real battle starts at three.''

``Three o'clock? What's that supposed to mean? By then, Team Z will probably be long finished.''

``That doesn't seem to be the case. There's some kind of trick. Do you think Hongo-senpai, as the game master, would let a team with such a clear advantage steamroll the final task? There's bound to be a huge upset.''

Mizasaki gulped.

``By telling me that, what do you want, Delta?''

``You don't need to worry about us. So no matter how rough things get for you, don't lose heart, and keep the pressure on Iwama. No matter who wins, I think that'll make the Science Dept Ori more exciting in the end. It's better if the competition stays heated right to the very end, isn't it?''

Mizasaki let out a quiet ``heh-heh.''

``It's not like you to care more about the event than winning or losing. But I get it. There might be some delay tactic that keeps us waiting until three. In that case, I'll just sit back and listen to the radio while I wait.''

$\gamma$

``Wow, those actually look pretty good on you!''

Though he'd been reluctant, I had Togakushi-kun put on the sunglasses from the backpack. I thought they'd suit him better than they would me. Hijiri-kun's camera just wouldn't stop rolling. I wanted to avoid having a large crowd see me wearing sunglasses.

`It can only be seen with colored glasses'---in other words, that meant sunglasses.

``What meaning does this have?''

``Try tilting your head from side to side while looking at the blue sky.''

Togakushi-kun tilted his head without hesitation and spoke as if convinced.

``Polarization?''

``Yes. The light reaching us from the blue sky is polarized, so its brightness changes depending on the angle.''

``How so?''

Hijiri-kun said only those few words, then moved to my side and asked for an explanation while filming my profile.

\textit{I felt like I was being interviewed.} I explained while walking.

``Sunlight is originally made up of light in many different colors, but some of it gets scattered by molecules in the atmosphere. That's Rayleigh scattering. Since blue light, with its shorter wavelength, scatters more easily, that light gets bent toward us from the sky, making a clear daytime sky look blue.''

Since I didn't know how much Hijiri-kun---or rather, the people on the other side of the camera---already knew, I started from the basics.

``So the light bent by that Rayleigh scattering is polarized light, meaning the waves vibrating in a certain direction become stronger. The polarizing sunglasses Togakushi-kun is wearing are made to let through only light vibrating in a specific direction, so the brightness of the blue sky changes depending on the angle you view it from.''

\textit{Was that getting the idea across? Really, it would've been faster to draw a diagram showing light as a wavy line and the sunglasses as a fence that only lets waves through in one direction, but there was no time for that now.}

``So there's something in the library that can only be seen through these polarizing sunglasses?''

``Exactly! It's probably something that uses a polarizing plate.''

A polarizing plate is a sheet that, like Togakushi-kun's sunglasses, only lets through light vibrating in one direction out of light vibrating in all sorts of directions. It's gray and translucent, and it's used in everyday things like LCD screens. When you stack two of them together, you can see through them if their orientations line up, but if they're turned ninety degrees from each other, no light passes through at all. That's because the polarizing plates absorb light from every direction.

That's why, when you look at an LCD TV screen or a digital watch face while wearing these sunglasses, they can turn pitch black depending on the angle. Using that mechanism, something that only appears when you wear the sunglasses had to be hidden somewhere around the library.

We arrived at the library. Since we'd been told to circle it, we didn't go inside and instead walked around the outside.

I immediately spotted something strange.

The terrace where I'd eaten a parfait with Del-chan. One of the tables under the parasols looked out of place. A large monitor had been placed there, glowing a blank white.

This was it.

The polarization properties of liquid crystals can be controlled by voltage. By using liquid crystals to control whether light from the backlight passes through the polarizing plate, an LCD screen adjusts the color and brightness of its pixels.

In other words, if you remove the polarizing plate from the surface of an LCD screen, all the light that has passed through the liquid crystals but hasn't yet been filtered comes straight out of the screen. The whole screen turns pure white.

``Togakushi-kun! What do you see on this?''

When I called out, Togakushi-kun noticed the monitor, then took off his sunglasses for a moment. He handed the sunglasses to me with a satisfied look on his face.

``It'll be faster if you just look.''

I hesitated for a moment, but curiosity won out, and I put on the sunglasses. Hijiri-kun darted around and captured my face perfectly. \textit{That earnestness in everything he did was what made Hijiri-kun so impressive.}

The moment I looked at the monitor, I knew this was the clue. What had looked pure white turned into a vivid screen through the sunglasses. Just as I'd thought, the polarizing plate on the surface had been removed.

But something was off. It was just an ad for a summer-limited parfait.

``What does this mean...?''

``It's probably camouflage. It'd be a problem if ordinary customers could spot the message at a glance.''

He had a point. Polarizing sunglasses weren't particularly rare. Especially not in this sunlight. It would cause confusion if some unrelated passerby happened to see a suspicious message.

``...Then that means something's hidden.''

I scanned over it, but nothing stood out. The only thing that looked suspicious was the QR code in the bottom right corner. In small letters, it said ``Touch here for the guide!''

Guide... not detailed allergy information, but a guide. On top of that, ``touch'' was a strange way to phrase it. You could take it to mean scanning the QR code with your phone and tapping the link, but I'd never seen it phrased that way before.

Just as it said, I pressed the QR code with my finger. It didn't seem to be a touch panel, so nothing changed on the screen. But something felt strange.

``Hey, look at this.''

I had Togakushi-kun press the same spot. Hijiri-kun also pressed nearby with his left hand to check.

``It's vibrating.''

``A low-frequency sound we can't hear is coming from a speaker on the back.''

``An unheard voice! This is it!''

The three of us kept touching the screen and realized the vibrations followed a pattern.

``...Morse code!''

Since Hijiri-kun happened to have memorized Morse code, we were able to decode the message immediately.

\begin{center}
LISTEN TO THE SONG OF THE SHINING TREE
\end{center}

$\delta$

By the time we finished moving the equipment, it was nearly ten o'clock. None of us could leave yet, but the third task had already begun. After receiving the rule explanation from Hongo-senpai in the audio-visual room, Mikage and I entered the student council room together.

Naturally, the room was empty. Mikage-senpai had let us use it as a special exception.

The student council room was cluttered with piles of documents and all sorts of mysterious items. I moved two chairs with casters near an empty desk, and Mikage and I sat down facing each other.

``What if Hijiri-kun was the student council president, Izuta-kun was the vice president, and I was the treasurer?''

``Give me a break. Mikage aside, I'm not cut out for a high-ranking role like that.''

``Is that so? We could have the school exactly the way we want it, though.''

Mikage rested her elbows on the desk, propped her chin in her hands, and looked at me playfully. \textit{She looked perfectly at home in the student council room. I wondered if she had a bit of a lust for power.}

In any case, we had to plan. Prevent the interference, secure the culprit, and bring the Faculty of Science Ori to a successful conclusion. We couldn't afford to fail. We needed to build a flawless line of reasoning.

``The rules for the third task are fine as they are. It was worth negotiating with Mikage-senpai.''

``Yeah. And what we need next is time.''

``That's the hardest part. The plan requires at least twenty minutes. During that time, the third task must not end. In other words, we have to stop Iwama and Togakushi.''

``It comes down to how we deal with the top student's serious effort.''

``Do you have any good ideas?''

Mikage fiddled with a red dial lock for a while as she thought. She said she had swiped the dial lock from the treasure chest behind the station during the first task. Mikage was surprisingly shrewd. Since they had messed with us, she apparently thought we ought to return the favor sooner or later.

``I'd rather you didn't spread this around, but...''

Without waiting for me to nod, Mikage continued.

``I've analyzed Togakushi-kun in my own way, and I figured something out.''

``What's unusual about his brain is how fast it processes information.''

``Roughly speaking, I think he can process information about four times faster than we can, even at full power.''

``Really...?''

\textit{I wanted to ask the Creator or someone if that was even within human limits.}

``Yeah. He can even finish exams in a quarter of the time it takes us, as long as his hand can keep up. Even when studying, he can handle four times as much in the same amount of time as us. That's why he excels in every subject.''

``His Japanese score seemed only mediocre, though.''

``I think he probably had points deducted because his handwriting was messy. Minor deductions in other subjects were probably the same. The Japanese teacher was especially strict about sloppy characters.''

I remembered the grumbling Watari had mentioned. So that was it.

---That teacher who's so picky about kanji is the problem. Deducting points just because a stroke wasn't hooked right\dots

If that was true, then Togakushi was capable of scoring nearly perfect marks in every subject. His talent went far beyond exceptional.

``How are we going to buy time against a monster like that?''

``He's not a monster. He's human, in the end. If we prepare properly, we can beat him.''

Showing more confidence than ever, Mikage explained her idea to me.

``First, we'll set things up so they have to walk around. As long as they're human, there's a limit to how much they can cut down the walking time. Then I'll prepare four problems that would take me forty minutes to solve at full power. We'll make it so this opens when they solve them.''

Mikage showed me the dial lock. It was four digits.

``But with four digits, wouldn't that come out to forty minutes in total?''

``No. If it's him, I think he'll only solve two and then brute-force the remaining two digits. That would be faster.''

``I see.''

\textit{An RTA runner would absolutely think of something like that.}

``...Do you think you can make the problems?''

At my question, Mikage smiled softly.

``Maybe I've spent all that time doing mountains of annoying calculations for the sake of this very day.''

$\gamma$

Listen to the song of the shining tree.

There was only one ``shining tree'' that had left a strong impression on us. The tree in the Chuo Shopping District, the one in the background of the Cheki photo used as evidence, and the one we had been forced to see on the way to the public bathhouse.

It was a fir tree wrapped in decorative lights that were set to turn on at 15:00 today.

\textit{Hongo-senpai was a calculating person, so she must have set up a barrier that would make all three teams start at once, keeping the winner unknown until the very end. The song wouldn't start until 15:00.}

We arrived at the tree at 14:40. Exactly an hour and a half had passed since the start. Mizasaki-kun and the rest of Team Z were already there, staring at us in surprise.

``Whoa, Gamma-san, you guys are fast! Are you serious? You made up about eighty minutes.''

``Did you just arrive too, Mizasaki-kun?''

``Well, yeah. About ten minutes ago. But it's weird---even excluding the thirty-minute lunch break, we should've still had an hour's lead. Does that mean you solved the Hachimangu task that fast too?''

I didn't know anything about Hachimangu. Togakushi-kun answered immediately.

``Don't underestimate us too much.''

It was a bluff. Togakushi-kun patted my shoulder, and the two of us turned away from Team Z.

``They had flip phones. They used a free hotspot at the library to scan a QR code and took a different route. Because they ignored the part about the `unheard voice,' they fell into a trap and ended up taking a detour.''

``So, Hachimangu isn't related to what comes next?''

``Most likely not. If you're curious, you can ask them later what they did.''

That sounded like it might be difficult. There wasn't much time until the illumination turned on. And we still weren't ready---not ready to borrow a giant's ears and listen to the song of the shining tree.

A sideways glance at Mizasaki-kun's team showed they were deep in a hushed discussion. They didn't look like they had the necessary tools ready yet. Hijiri-kun had apparently found a good angle to capture the whole tree, because he was filming Togakushi-kun and me from a short distance away.

I brought it up with Togakushi-kun.

``The lights come on at three. I think what we do from here will decide the winner. There's something I'd like to work on beforehand, if that's okay.''

``You've already figured out what that code meant?''

``It's still just a guess, though...''

Since it would've been embarrassing to ramble about my idea beforehand and end up completely wrong, I still hadn't shared my theory with Togakushi-kun or Hijiri-kun. But I was reasonably confident. And if that theory was right, we needed to use what we had on hand to make some `tools.'

``There's something I want to try. But I think I'll have to break some of our belongings.''

$\delta$

After listening to the FM radio at Tsunanagai Station and decoding the Morse code at the library (since none of us knew the conversion table, we wrote down the signals for the time being, and I hurriedly decoded them using a book in the library while pretending to go to the bathroom), it was nearly 15:00 by the time we reached the Symbol Tree in the Chuo Shopping District.

I was already drenched in sweat from hurrying through the summer streets.

The area around the tree was a small plaza. Since it served no real purpose except as a meeting spot, there weren't many people around. I spotted the other two teams right away.

``Listen to the song of the shining tree''---a likely solution had already occurred to me, and I'd already shared it. But we were missing the parts we needed to listen to the ``shining.'' In the worst case, I'd just have to borrow some from Mizasaki.

``Oh, looks like the whole cast is here.''

Osawa from Team Z called out flippantly as we arrived. His blond hair, which usually stuck out in every direction, was damp with sweat and plastered down.

Nanbu from the Chemistry Club looked exhausted as he waved us away.

``We're in the middle of a strategy meeting. Sorry, but could you stay back?''

We had no choice but to head to the other side of the tree. The three members of Team Y were huddled together, working on something. Hijiri had set his equipment on the ground and was filming them with a wide shot. Seeing that, Watari immediately set down the LiveU he'd been carrying, placed his camera on the ground, and fanned the back of his gym shirt as if he were being roasted.

``So, Delta, how are we going to get a solar cell?''

``Mizasaki and his team have a calculator. Calculators run on solar cells. If we take one apart, we should be able to get one.''

``I wonder if they'll let us borrow it.''

I could only stay silent at Mikage's point. \textit{Would an enemy really hand over a solar cell?}

I checked our belongings once more. A map. A compass. A pass case. A \textsc{g-shock}. Sunglasses. A flashlight. A portable radio. Earphones.

``Is there any way we could take the \textsc{g-shock} apart?''

``Do you think you can take it apart here?''

Watari shook his right arm. It was a sturdy-looking watch. Taking it apart and removing the solar cell would be a daunting task. Besides, I had no confidence in putting precision equipment back together. Irreversible damage would lead to disqualification.

The only thing we hadn't used yet was the flashlight. It was cheap, so it could be twisted apart. A tail switch, a compartment holding three AAA batteries, and a green circuit board with three tiny bulb-style LEDs attached. Unfortunately, it didn't seem able to generate power from light.

\textit{Then what was this flashlight supposed to be for? Catching bugs? No, we'd already been lent a separate, powerful flashlight specifically for that. Then for what?}

``There are only thirty seconds left, but have you figured out the solution?''

Hijiri walked over, showing off the \textsc{g-shock} on his left arm. Watari didn't budge.

``You really are a guy who gets under my skin every single time.''

``Sorry about that. If you beat me in an arm-wrestling match, I'll tell you Iwama-san's idea.''

``Huh? You want me to snap that right arm of yours?''

While the two Physics Club members were talking ``amicably,'' Iwama and Togakushi stood near the tree with some small device in hand, pulling one of the nearby LEDs from the illumination toward them. A ceramic earphone was in Iwama's ear. It was the monaural earphone she was supposed to have cut off from the plug.

Mizasaki and the others were on the other side of the tree, so I couldn't see what they were doing. But they would probably reach the right answer. All they needed was an earphone and a solar cell. Once the lights turned on, we'd be the only ones in trouble.

And then---15:00. Even though it was still bright out, the tree's lights came on, and at the same time, the chime announcing the hour played from the speakers.

``Too bad. You're out of time. As thanks for the earphone, I'll give you this.''

Hijiri handed me an LED he had removed from the flashlight's circuit board.

$\gamma$

LED stands for Light-Emitting Diode. It performs the simple task of emitting light when current runs through it in one direction, but it also has the properties of a photodiode, meaning it generates current in one direction when it receives light.

As Del-chan had pointed out, it's similar to how a motor can be used as a generator.

Both solar cells and LEDs share the same structure: a semiconductor pn junction.

When I heard ``the song of the shining tree,'' the first thing that came to mind was optical communication. The tree lights were flickering and twinkling. I thought that maybe those flickers were the song. I wondered if the senpais had arranged with the shopping district people to embed musical information into the lights.

A solar cell would've been convenient for receiving the light from the illumination, but we didn't have one this time. So I used an LED instead. LEDs were built into the flashlight we were given at the start.

I removed an LED from the circuit board and connected the ceramic earphone's wires to its two legs. Then I used that LED to catch the light coming from the tree's LEDs. It was an extremely simple setup.

The moment the lights turned on, I knew we'd succeeded.

A singing voice came through the ceramic earphone. I could even make out the words clearly.

Wanting him to share the excitement, I handed the earphone to Togakushi-kun too. After listening for a few seconds, Togakushi-kun nodded.

``Nice, Iwama.''

At that moment, everything simply felt fun. \textit{I had never imagined there could be a place where the things I loved could shine so brightly. It might have been the first time those lights had ever looked so beautiful to me.}

``Let's go!''

At my call, the three of us set off together and took the lead.

The tree was singing.

【Look for it---the highest point in the school. Who will be the first to grasp the championship trophy?】

$\delta$

We set off last, power-walking to make up for the delay.

Mikage and I consulted with each other, intentionally letting the camera following us from behind overhear.

``The highest point... is it the rooftop?''

``No, that's not it,'' I said with confidence.

``The back mountain is part of the school grounds. It's the summit of the back mountain. That's where the championship trophy is.''

Mikage thought for a moment, then held up two fingers.

``There should be two courses. The path passing by the Meoto-zakura, and the cliff path the mountaineering club uses for practice.''

``Let's take the cliff route. The area around the Meoto-zakura is closed because of fallen trees.''

``What about the camera? Can they film while climbing?''

``With Watari's muscles, it'll be a breeze.''

I heard someone click his tongue. \textit{I ignored it. My own breathing was starting to get heavy too.}

Power-walking was even more grueling than I'd expected. Since the school sat on a hill, the road was one long gentle slope. My leg muscles felt like they were going to scream. I struggled to keep up with Mikage, who kept walking with a cool, composed expression.

As we entered the final stretch---the row of ginkgo trees before the school gate---I caught a brief glimpse of Team Z's backs. But they vanished through the school gate at once.

``Looks like Team Z headed toward the school building?''

I shook my head at Mikage's question, gasping for breath.

``The back mountain is higher than the rooftop. We can still win.''

We didn't go through the gate and instead veered off to the side. We passed the trailhead to the Meoto-zakura and headed farther back, toward the area directly behind the school. A steep slope of exposed, crumbling sandstone came into view.

We pressed on without hesitation. Halfway up, it turned into a climb on all fours. There was a single chain, likely installed by the mountaineering club, and we used it to pull ourselves up.

The chain was only secured by rusted bolts. Figuring it was best not to put too much weight on it, we decided to climb one at a time.

Once we finished the climb, the school rooftop visible through the trees was far below us.

$\gamma$

We were the first to arrive. We changed our shoes, entered the school building, and began the final sprint up the stairs.

Just as we reached the roof, an unexpected obstacle blocked our way.

The door was locked. Strictly speaking, the lock itself was open, but a small latch linking the door to the wall had been fastened shut with a red dial padlock. We needed a four-digit number.

The method for finding that number was posted on the door. The problem was written in pencil on a sheet of copy paper.

\begin{center}
\textbf{Final Question}

Search the school building. The key opens with ``East, West, South, North.''
\end{center}

``Is there still more?''

Togakushi-kun immediately spun on his heel. I followed.

``What does it mean? I wonder if East is the first digit, West is the second, and so on?''

``Probably. Let's start with East.''

The compass came in handy. Heading farther and farther east, we reached the Martial Arts Hall. The clue was posted on the eastern wall of the first floor. It was the same kind of copy paper again.

\begin{center}
Find the 32nd decimal place of $\sqrt{7}$.
\end{center}

``Am I allowed to get angry now?''

Togakushi-kun's pale temples twitched.

``Do you think you can do it?''

``Naturally. I slept all morning, after all. Sorry, but give me ten minutes, plus some paper and a pencil.''

$\gamma$

Thinking there were no moves left, they were on the verge of giving up. Would they have to steel themselves for a desperate last resort? The thought crossed their mind.

Just then, a timely voice came through the speakers in the audio-visual room.

【It's the summit of the back mountain. That's where the championship trophy is.】

They were wrong. The highest point on the school grounds was obviously the rooftop.

To make matters worse, they had started climbing the chain section---used only by the mountaineering club---instead of taking the normal hiking trail. The camera clearly showed the chain. It was secured only by unreliable bolts. It swayed every time weight was put on it.

The screen switched to hands extracting the square root using the digit-by-digit method. Although the speed was incredible, they were still only at the seventh decimal place. Team Y would probably win, but it would still take twenty minutes before they got their hands on the championship trophy.

The plan struck like a bolt of lightning.

Anticipating something like this, they had chosen a seat where they could leave immediately.

Putting on the face of someone heading off to wash their hands, they slipped out of the audio-visual room.

$\delta$

After making our way along the mountain path for a while, I accidentally dropped the video camera I was using for the broadcast.

I quickly covered the lens with my pass case so only audio would be transmitted.

``Is anything showing?''

``It should be fine. The screen is black, but it's still transmitting. The camera hasn't stopped.''

We had estimated that after twenty minutes, the culprit would decide the time had come to put their plan into action. During that time, I would have Togakushi keep solving the problems Mikage had prepared while we pretended to continue the game with a camera showing nothing.

After I dropped the camera, the three of us split up. I headed straight for the spot where I had stashed my equipment beforehand. A camouflage sheet was laid out in the thicket.

Pulling back the sheet, I quickly checked the equipment. First, the camera and lens. I had attached a 1000mm ultra-telephoto lens, which looked like a cannon, to the Alpha 7 we had used during the Golden Week training camp. Since the lens was heavier than the body, I used the tripod collar attached to the lens to mount it on the tripod.

The tripod was a TT-66, stable enough to support an ultra-low angle. With the legs spread wide, the camera was set at a height just above the ground. I lay flat on my stomach so I could bring my eye to the camera, then covered myself from head to back with the camouflage sheet to stay hidden.

I had already trimmed the thicket so I could hide the lens inside it. Since it was in the shade, it wouldn't catch the sunlight.

I turned the power on and looked through the viewfinder. Since there were several branches in the foreground, I used manual focus. I adjusted the focus and brought the bolt holding the chain, several dozen meters away, into view.

Holding my breath, I watched the same spot through the binoculars I had prepared. It was just like bird photography, except the thing I was waiting for wasn't a wild bird.

It was the culprit.

$\gamma$

The closest place to the Martial Arts Hall was the cafeteria to the north. The door was unlocked. When I went inside, I saw a piece of copy paper pasted on the north wall. Running up to it, Togakushi-kun let out a sigh.

\begin{center}
Find the 35th decimal place of $\sqrt{11}$.
\end{center}

``Do they think this is the Math Olympiad or something?''

``Can you solve it?''

``Naturally. I'm used to it by now, so eight minutes should be enough.''

I handed him a new piece of copy paper and a new pencil. The pinky-side edge of Togakushi-kun's pale right hand was completely black as he took them. It was from scribbling numbers nonstop until just now at a speed that would put a certain TV-drama physicist to shame.

``Do you think you can handle three more?''

``No, this is the last one. I'll brute-force the remaining two digits.''

$\delta$

There was a good chance they wouldn't come. Trying interference that hadn't been part of the original plan carried a high risk. And since this was the third time, they could easily assume we'd be on guard.

But the culprit came. They must have come in fully committed. They kept checking their surroundings, but they didn't seem to imagine a lens was trained on them from inside the thicket.

I tossed aside the binoculars and pressed my eye to the camera's viewfinder. I immediately adjusted the focus.

I lined up the center of the lens with the space between the culprit's eyebrows and pressed the shutter. That was the first shot. Then two. Then three...

Snapping back to my senses, I started filming the culprit climbing the rock face. Once the culprit reached the bolt holding the chain, they started looking around again, taking their time.

I could tell from the movement of their mouth that they were calling out to someone. Had they confirmed that no one was there?

Finally, the culprit took a monkey wrench out of their pocket. They adjusted it to fit the bolt head and started turning it. The red circle indicating recording was lit up inside the viewfinder.

\textit{I never thought it would go this well. I felt such intense excitement that I half thought the adrenaline flooding my body might start leaking from my pores.}

\textit{I had filmed the moment of the crime.}

\textit{This video would be definitive evidence. It was like holding the power of life and death over the culprit.}

\textit{Along with the trembling in my finger, I realized that a tool like a camera could even steal someone's life.}

The culprit tried to hurry down the cliff. Someone called out for them to stop.

I stopped recording, swapped to a normal lens, attached a directional microphone, and headed toward the scene.

$\gamma$

Finally finished solving the North problem, we headed for the rooftop once again.

Fortunately, we didn't run into Mizasaki-kun or the others. No one was in front of the door leading to the rooftop. The door was still latched. It seemed we really were the first to arrive.

``I'm opening it.''

Even as he said it, Togakushi-kun already had a hand on the dial lock.

He set the top digit, corresponding to East, to ``1,'' the answer from the Martial Arts Hall, and the bottom digit, corresponding to North, to ``2,'' the answer from the cafeteria. After that, he brute-forced the middle two digits.

First, with the second digit fixed at 0, he rotated the third from 0 to 9, tugging down on the padlock each time to see if it would open. It didn't work. Next, he set the second digit to 1.

As luck would have it, right at the very end, the lock opened at ``1962.''

``Yes! Nice, Togakushi-kun!''

I couldn't help letting out a cry of joy. This was the climax.

When the rooftop door flew open, the still-dazzling summer sunlight seared my retinas. Still half-blinded as I stepped onto the rooftop, I looked around at the floor. Where was the championship trophy?

Then, when I turned around, I realized it. That was it. The area around the door leading to the rooftop was one level higher than the rest. A ladder leading up was attached to the wall.

``Over here!''

I called to Togakushi-kun, who was still blinking, while already grabbing the ladder. Since I was in gym clothes, I didn't have to worry about anyone seeing underneath. I climbed up in one burst.

The joy I felt when I poked my head up onto the roof and saw the golden trophy with two handles, shaped exactly like a championship cup, is almost impossible to put into words.

My brain flooded with more dopamine than ever before.

\textit{I never knew it could be this much fun to throw myself into something I loved and get results.}

The three of us gathered around the trophy. Togakushi-kun looked at me.

``Iwama is the leader. Take it, quick.''

I had no reason to refuse. The camera was on me. I nodded and reached out.

``Ready! One, two...!''

At my shout, I grabbed one handle of the championship trophy.

At that exact same moment, Watari-kun's left hand gripped the other handle.

$\delta$

``What are you doing?''

From the top of the cliff, Hijiri called out to the culprit.

``...Hijiri-kun? Why are you somewhere like this?''

``I'm the one who asked first. Please answer me, Bakuma-san.''

The culprit---Bakuma---wore a breezy smile as he scrambled up the chain section with easy movements. He came face-to-face with Hijiri on the narrow patch of rock at the top.

``I came to call you back because you guys went the wrong way.''

``That's strange. I just saw you loosening the bolts.''

``The bolts?''

\textit{I could practically see the desperate excuses taking shape inside his head.}

Of course, I was capturing everything on camera.

``Ah, they were loose, so I was tightening them. I thought it would be dangerous to leave them like that.''

``Is that so? In that case, there shouldn't be any problem with you putting your weight on that chain and climbing back down right now, right, Bakuma-san?''

There was a brief silence.

``...Well, naturally. But where did Izuta-kun and the others go? Why are you here?''

``It's a very classic switch trick. When we left the tree in the Chuo Shopping District, Watari and I swapped cameras. I don't think you could've noticed just by watching the footage.''

``Why would you do that?''

``It's interesting, isn't it? At the very end, once all of you were convinced Team Y had won, you'd suddenly notice Watari gripping the trophy at the same time. In this Science Dept Ori, Team X and Team Y join forces and win in a tie. It makes for a dramatic finish.''

There was a rule that you had to move in groups of three, but it never specified that those three had to be your own team. And if the rule was ``the team that first grasps the championship trophy wins,'' then if members of two teams grasped it at the same time, it would count as a tie.

With that, the selected members had outwitted even the game master and seized victory through cooperation---

That was the story for public consumption.

\textit{The real objective, of course, was to keep Watari from getting dragged into this. But since we couldn't suggest a switch without a reason, the official line was simply that ``it would be interesting to win together like that.'' Our heading for the back mountain could simply be explained away as a feint to lure Team Z the wrong way.}

\textit{It was a last-minute logical cover story meant to keep the incident contained among the people involved while still carrying the Science Dept Ori through to a successful finish.}

``Now, Bakuma-san, here's my second question. Why did you do this?''

``Do what? I only came to pick you guys up---''

Hijiri rejected that outright.

``No. Yesterday morning, while checking the scaffolding in front of Kannon-kutsu, you planted a timed device. You tucked wax-coated gallium into the joints where no one would see it.''

``Huh? Gallium? What's that?''

``There's no way you don't know. Your family home is in Kochi, so you're from outside the prefecture. Whether you were in the humanities or a sports club, you wouldn't have gotten grades like yours without knowing something as basic as element 31, gallium.''

``Ah, I learned about it in high school. But putting gallium into scaffolding? That makes no sense.''

``Shall I explain? Gallium melts at 30\textdegree C. When the sun rises and the temperature climbs, the gallium melts. Then, once sunlight hits the scaffolding, the wax---with its melting point of 60\textdegree C---starts to melt too. As a result, the gallium planted there slowly corrodes the joints.''

This was what I had explained to him, and Hijiri was repeating it mostly correctly.

``Gallium has the property of working its way into metal over time, making even hard metals brittle. The gallium planted in the morning had seeped in thoroughly by late morning, so when Izuta tried to cross, the joint broke. When it was my turn, it hadn't seeped in enough yet, so it didn't break. That's how it worked.''

Bakuma opened his mouth to interrupt, but Hijiri cut him off with a raised hand.

``The scaffolding that hadn't broken in the morning broke in the afternoon. Naturally, everyone would suspect the cause had to lie somewhere around noon, during that gap. Bakuma-san, you didn't go to Kannon-kutsu then because you said the car was too big, which kept suspicion off you. Instead, Kurauchi-san, who went in your place, would come under suspicion. That's how it worked.''

``Even if that's true, that doesn't mean I did it. Calm down.''

``The second time was the bomb planted in the campfire. Unfortunately, there's no evidence left for that. But as someone who works in construction, you could easily have gotten your hands on knowledge about explosives. Did you use not just gallium, but aluminum powder too, specifically to frame Kurauchi-san?''

``I'm sorry, but let's leave it at that---''

``Anyone can get gallium by mail order. And Bakuma-san, you brought us cold watermelon. You were using a cooler box, weren't you? In this season, transporting gallium means keeping it in a low-temperature environment. A cooler box is perfect for that, isn't it?''

Finally, Bakuma cut Hijiri off sharply.

``Look. If you're as smart as you say, then you should know the difference between necessary and sufficient conditions. I might fit the conditions of the culprit you're describing. But that doesn't make me the culprit.''

``That's exactly why I had you come here.''

Hijiri crouched down, picked up the chain at his feet, and yanked it hard. With a violent noise, the bolts came free. Hijiri let go, and the chain went clattering down the cliff with an unpleasant metallic clang.

``Look behind you. I've been filming everything, right from the moment you started tampering with the bolts.''

Bakuma turned toward us and looked straight into the camera. He had noticed me hiding in the shade of the trees.

``You've already lost. Please tell us the truth. What was your motive for sabotaging the Science Dept Ori?''

Caught between Hijiri and me, Bakuma's expression darkened, and he reached a hand out toward me.

``Give me the camera.''

And he started closing the distance between us. \textit{Was he going to resort to force? This was unexpected.} I hurriedly backed away.

But Bakuma stopped halfway. Hijiri had him by the belt from behind.

``I won't let you lay a single finger on my friend. Now, Izuta. Hurry, get down the mountain.''

Bakuma spun around with quick, agile movements. Hijiri reacted instantly and let go. As Bakuma tried to come after me, Hijiri lunged at him. Bakuma quickly parried his hand and threw a strike straight at Hijiri's stomach. Hijiri knocked the blow aside from the side. Bakuma had probably meant to end it with a single strike, but once it was blocked, it turned into a full-blown scuffle.

I instinctively swung the camera toward the sudden brawl. It was like filming a choreographed fight scene for a detective drama. On the steep slope with its terrible footing, Hijiri fought desperately against the bigger Bakuma.

``Don't film, just run!''

Hijiri's roar snapped me back to my senses, and I scrambled down the steep, wooded slope. \textit{This was enough. Hijiri was fighting to let me escape. It would all mean nothing if I didn't get away with the evidence.}

The crunch of crumbling rock made me look back. I saw Hijiri sliding down the brittle sandstone near the chain section where the chain had come loose. The camera, which I had kept rolling, followed my gaze. While keeping Hijiri at the edge of the frame, it also clearly captured Bakuma standing at the top of the cliff.

This, too, was conclusive evidence. A conclusive record of Bakuma pushing Hijiri.

A heartbeat later, a chill ran down my spine---\textit{Wait, was Hijiri okay?}

Hijiri's slide had stopped on a flat rock jutting out like a small ledge. I rushed toward him. But out of the corner of my eye, I could also see Bakuma scrambling quickly down the cliff.

\textit{What should I do? Was it really okay for me to just keep running? To leave Hijiri behind?}

\textit{I didn't have the strength to fight someone like Bakuma. One punch and I'd be knocked out. And Bakuma was closing in. This was no time to hesitate. I had to think.}

In a split-second decision, I pulled the SD card and reached Hijiri's side just as Bakuma arrived.

``Stop. Give me the camera. I won't treat you badly.''

``\dots\dots Don't give it to him.''

Hijiri's voice came out as though squeezed from the back of his throat. He was conscious. \textit{I felt a wave of relief.}

As I slowly moved to hand over the camera, Bakuma snapped his eyes to it.

``It's not recording. You pulled the memory card. Hand it all over.''

He'd seen through it. \textit{But I couldn't hand over the evidence. What should I do\dots\dots?}

\textit{Clink.} The sound rang out.

A chain looped around Bakuma's neck. Just as Bakuma instinctively shielded his neck and turned, his long legs flew up into the air in one fluid motion.

I saw Mikage slip her back beneath his body. It was probably some variation of a shoulder throw, maybe an ippon seoi-nage. Dragged down by the chain around his neck, Bakuma's body rolled over Mikage's back, flipped upright, and slammed down onto the rock on his back.

\textit{To be honest, I felt an even deeper chill than I had with Hijiri. I thought she might have killed him.}

``It's okay. He's not dead.''

With her wrists still crossed around the chain, Mikage calmly tightened it around Bakuma's neck.

Without a word, all the strength drained from Bakuma's body in a matter of seconds.

``\dots\dots Hey.''

``It was just a carotid restraint. He only passed out.''

As she spoke, Mikage pulled zip ties from her socks, knelt down, used her knee to roll Bakuma onto his side, and expertly bound his thumbs behind his back.

\textit{I decided not to ask where on earth she'd learned techniques like that, at least not today.}

``That was amazing, Mikage-san. I couldn't do a thing.''

Hijiri was slowly pushing himself upright. He apparently had enough room to spare for post-match commentary.

As she pulled a monkey wrench from Bakuma's pocket, Mikage smiled.

``It's thanks to you dropping the chain.''

Figuring it wouldn't look right if I stayed silent, I spoke up too.

``Is it over?''

Hijiri stood up, cradling his right arm.

``Yeah. We win.''

$\gamma$

``The winners are Team X and Team Y! What a shocking ending! In any case, congratulations!''

Hongo-senpai called out to the three of us after we returned to the audio-visual room, and a grand round of applause broke out for us.

The one I really cared about, Del-chan, still hadn't come back yet. He'd said something about acting as a decoy for Team Z, but where could he have gone? The broadcast footage was no longer playing on the screen. In its place, a large image was displayed of the moment Watari-kun and I grabbed the trophy at the same time.

Truthfully, I had wanted to welcome this moment with Del-chan.

It was Del-chan who had proposed the alliance before the third task. After we shared information to decode the cipher, he took out a set of stereo earphones and made me a proposal.

``Want to form a united front?''

It sounded like an attractive proposal. Del-chan explained it to me seriously.

``A cipher that can't be solved unless all four lines are together---I think that's Hongo-senpai's way of telling us to cooperate. We're already behind Team Z in both items and time. It wouldn't look good if we lost like this. You want to pull off a comeback that makes everyone gasp, don't you?''

I was all for it. As Hongo-senpai had said the night before, if Team Z won, the senpais would end up having to treat a ridiculous number of people to high-end BBQ. But they hadn't made any preparations for that---of course, that was just the official excuse; the truth was that I wanted to share the joy with Del-chan.

But since I couldn't make the call on my own personal whim, I consulted Togakushi-kun, whom I had woken up, and Hijiri-kun first. Togakushi-kun was reluctant, but Hijiri-kun thought it sounded interesting and jumped on board, so we decided to form a united front.

When I reported back to him, Del-chan smiled with a hint of mischief.

``I just thought of a special trick.''

And so the plan to swap the cameramen was settled in secret, and the six of us worked together to stage a dramatic victory. I felt a little bad for Mizasaki-kun and the others, but even Team Z was surprised by the unexpected ending and praised us.

And with that, the Science Dept Ori came to an end.

Just as the lively chatter in the audio-visual room was starting to grow almost too loud, Del-chan and the others came back with Mikage-senpai and Hyakuzawa-senpai. Apparently, after climbing the back mountain, they had nearly gotten lost on the way back. While Mikage-senpai was recounting the story in a funny way, I tried to go over to Del-chan---but someone got to him first.

``I'm leaving now. It's time to say goodbye.''

I had thought all the invitees had left after greeting the three of us, but it seemed Claire-san alone had stayed behind to wait for the other three to return. She turned a smile toward Del-chan and Hijiri-kun without even trying to hide her favoritism.

``I'm truly glad I got to meet you both. Please grow up into fine, handsome men.''

And then, to my shock, she planted kisses on both of them---though I'd prefer to think they merely touched cheeks---before fleeing the audio-visual room. She was like a passing phantom. Not just Del-chan, but even Hijiri-kun kept their eyes on her chestnut-haired figure until the very end, looking completely dazed.

\textit{I got a little angry.}

``Good job!''

I stepped into Del-chan's path and guided him toward the wall of the audio-visual room. We faced each other, just the two of us.

``A lot happened, but it was fun, wasn't it?''

I had meant to let out at least a small complaint, but those words came out together with an irrepressible smile. Del-chan smiled back and said, ``Yeah.''

It felt like my heart was tightening.

For some reason, his soft smile looked as though it might shatter at any moment.

\textit{I'm sure it was just my imagination. But I felt like I had to do something.}

\textit{Because of that---could I call it an excuse?}

``I'm glad we could win together.''

I---doing something I normally never would, giving in to the festive mood around me---hugged him for just an instant.

\fullpageimage{11.jpg}

\thispagestyle{plain}
\vspace{1cm}

% ==============================
%        Fragment
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Fragment\\
    Determination as a Generalist
\end{center}
\label{sec:fragDetermination}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Fragment}
\vspace{1cm}

Near my home, there used to be a small, family-run Western restaurant. It was famous for its soft, hand-kneaded hamburger steaks. When I was very young, my parents often took me there to eat, but the owner who stood in the kitchen was already quite elderly, and the place had closed down by the time I was in elementary school.

Every time I passed that building, which still retained a few traces of its former self, the first taste that came back to life on my tongue wasn't the delicious hamburger steak, but the rather unpalatable parsley.

My father was a man who never allowed leftovers. Looking back now, I suspect parsley that dry wasn't even meant to be eaten by customers, but even so, my father ordered me not to leave a single leaf behind.

The reason was simple. My father expected perfection from me. Or at least, he demanded that I strive toward perfection. He repeated his motto like a mantra: ``Be a generalist.'' This ``generalist'' didn't refer to an organism that could thrive on various foods or in diverse environments.

It meant a person who could do everything.

According to my father, in order to play a respectable role in human society, a person needed the ability to function in any situation. And a generalist with that ability---though the public often thought of such a person as someone who could do anything---was, in his view, someone who did everything, someone who never cut corners in anything.

Everyone has strengths and weaknesses. But if someone prioritized their strengths and neglected their weaknesses because of it, a hole would open up in them. To keep that hole from forming, one had to do everything. You mustn't leave behind even the tough parsley. The restaurant staff probably wouldn't have cared if I left the parsley, but if I did, I would become the sort of person with likes and dislikes, and someday that would turn into a hole. I would become the kind of person who neglected something simply because I was bad at it or hated it. Even if I had talent, I would end up a dropout of no use to human society. ``I can absolutely never forgive that kind of person''---that was what my father used to say.

My father was a leading-edge medical researcher. He ran a massive immunology laboratory, supervised dozens of students, and conducted research aimed at eliminating cancer from the world. At the time, he was the dean of both the Graduate School of Medicine and the Faculty of Medicine. He also held several concurrent directorships in academic societies. According to my mother, he hadn't just accumulated research achievements; he had also won quite a few power struggles to reach his current position.

My father had clawed his way upward, putting in every effort for the sake of the world and its people. That was probably why he couldn't forgive people who only did what they liked. Especially people who had the ability to do more, yet chose not to.

Raised by such a father, I became a child who could eat tough parsley with a smile. Having been given every opportunity in both academics and sports without stint, I felt I had lived an incredibly blessed life.

But if I were to voice one selfish complaint, it would be this: while I was allowed to do anything, I was never allowed to devote myself to any one thing.

My father, who was passionate about education, taught me about science. And I was drawn in by the magic of it. Science was magic. Encyclopedias and specialized books were grimoires. With almost exactly the same feeling as someone reading a fantasy novel about magic in rapt fascination, I tried to immerse myself in science.

My father put a stop to that. Though he had been pleased by my enthusiasm at first, he eventually began to look displeased. Then one day, he locked away my precious books and experimental tools in the storage room.

``That's enough. Rio, your enthusiasm is starting to run wild.''

It happened when I entered middle school and chose the biology club instead of the sports club my parents had recommended.

My mother, who took pity on me, negotiated with my father on my birthday the following year. On the condition that the items sealed in the storage room would eventually be sold at a flea market, she gave me sole access and the only key to that room.

``A girl has things she might want to keep secret from her father, after all.''

My father seemed unable to accept my mother's logic until the very end, but he eventually nodded. Beneath the Somei-yoshino in full bloom, he gave me one final warning.

``This cherry blossom is a symbol of the elite. Out of the hundreds and thousands of varieties that have been created, the most beloved one is celebrated and comes to dominate the landscape throughout Japan. In life, too, there is a mold that has been perfected over many years. Never forget that as long as you do not stray from it, you can keep walking the path of success.''

That was the moment I learned the meaning that had been embedded in my name.

My mother was quite the tactician herself; the books and experimental tools that were supposed to have been sold at the flea market had been left in the storage room exactly as they were.

From that day on, the storage room became my secret place.

A place to keep the things I ``liked'' that I couldn't show anyone.

On its wall now was the Katakuri Del-chan had given me, displayed as a pressed leaf specimen.

Even in high school, I ended up joining the biology club. My father didn't say anything. Maybe it was because my father himself had belonged to the chemistry club at Tsunanagai High School. My father had no right to object.

Even so, my father still hadn't given up on his Generalist Training Plan. I myself believed that aiming to be a generalist was both beneficial and admirable. Besides, I was suited for it. I could produce decent results in anything I tried, and I could even enjoy the effort. If I could do it, there was no harm in doing it. As long as all it required was the mindset of not leaving my parsley behind.

Searching for my own way of life while following my father's teachings---that was my current goal. I would neglect neither the things I had to do nor the things I wanted to do. I knew it was a very difficult task, but it had to be worth the effort.

I believed I could do it.

Because the person who had sworn he would make me happy was there with me.

% ==============================
%        Chapter 5
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Chapter 5\\
    Someday, Standing Upon the Truth
\end{center}
\label{sec:ch5V3}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Chapter 5}
\vspace{1cm}

$\delta$

On the afternoon after the Faculty of Science Ori, Hijiri and I were called to Cafe Sansetsu-mori. We were led to the private room in the back, a place I didn't have many good memories of. The Mikage siblings were waiting for us there, sipping a blend and a café latte.

The room smelled faintly fishy, and I soon saw why: a strange object sat beside Mikage-senpai. Inside a long, narrow cardboard box lay a large whole salted salmon. For some reason, the salmon was wearing a familiar blue vest.

``Is that a salted salmon?''

Hijiri asked as we sat down, and Mikage-senpai nodded.

``My apologies if the smell bothers you. How's your right arm?''

``It's a hairline fracture, but it should be healed by the end of summer vacation.''

Hijiri, wearing long sleeves despite the heat, rolled up his right sleeve. The cast was surprisingly modest for a fracture; I hadn't noticed it at all with his sleeve down.

It was from when Bakuma had thrown him down.

``We'll cover all the medical expenses. I'm sorry this happened during your summer vacation.''

``I'll just lie low and focus on my studies.''

At Mikage-senpai's gesture, we sat down across from the siblings. He got straight to the point.

``Bakuma-san spilled everything. Just as expected, it was Tsuruo's doing.''

Tsuruo was the head of a massive corporate conglomerate known as the CHOSEI Group. He was an old man who had graduated from Tsunanagai High School long ago; reportedly, he was the one who had established both the system for scouting out-of-prefecture students and the mechanism by which corporations invested in the school through the alumni association. \textit{Though I had never met him myself, I suspected Tsuruo held a grudge against us. It was because we had tried to pursue the corruption tied to the CHOSEI Group.}

``It's largely just as Hijiri-kun imagined. They were worried the Faculty of Science would use the Science Ori to gather donations and regain influence within the school. The order was to infiltrate the event and make sure it ended in complete disaster. It seems Bakuma-san himself had no personal grudge against you at all.''

\textit{No personal grudge---and yet there were people capable of doing things like this.} So I asked a question.

``Did they have some kind of hold over him?''

``Well, yes. That's probably true of most out-of-prefecture graduates, to some extent or another. They owe a debt to the CHOSEI Group, and there must have been times they needed help with job hunting or promotions. Before long, a noose ends up around their necks. Manipulating people through money and fear is Tsuruo's specialty.''

Hijiri frowned as Mikage-senpai explained all this as calmly as if he were making small talk.

``Is it fair to assume that Tsuruo still hasn't given up on interfering with Tsunanagai High School?''

``Unfortunately, yes. But he'll learn his lesson this time. We have the evidence. We got Bakuma-san to tell us everything. Thanks to you two, we've managed to get hold of their weakness, just as Nagisa wished.''

``If you do that, won't Bakuma-san be in danger?''

``That's why---and I'm sorry to you both for this---we quietly sent him overseas. Conveniently enough, the man is still single. He'll probably manage just fine over there.''

\textit{I didn't point out how much it sounded like something out of a spy movie. I was starting to get used to stories this unrealistic.}

``Mikage-senpai, are you planning to shield a criminal?''

``I figured Hijiri-kun wouldn't be satisfied with that. But it can't be helped. It would be a problem for us if Bakuma-san were `erased.' That's why you two must not say a word about his whereabouts to anyone. We're going to send Tsuruo a strong message to keep his hands off.''

Mikage-senpai gestured toward the salted salmon in the vest. Hijiri tilted his head.

``What does that mean?''

``It's been given a Japanese twist, but it's Sicilian style. Well, you two don't need to know just yet. It's a story from a slightly more `adult' world. We're showing them that we're serious too.''

After taking a slow sip of his coffee, Mikage-senpai smiled at us.

``You can rest easy. Tsuruo won't be making a move for a while. Our final summer as third-years is coming to an end soon. Do you understand what that means?''

``You and the others will be stepping down. Both as club presidents and as members of the student council.''

``Exactly. We'll lose our power. We're having Ringo-chan run in the next election as the Faculty of Science's representative, but the opposing candidates are too strong; she probably won't win. For a while, school politics will move in the direction Tsuruo wants. So I can guarantee that nothing will happen, at the very least, until next summer---until your own elections.''

\textit{He said it with such confidence that I almost believed him. Well, maybe it was fine to believe him.} Even so, there was still one concern of mine that remained unresolved.

``Did you hear anything about the advance notice?''

Mikage-senpai crossed his arms with a troubled look. \textit{Had Bakuma said nothing about that?}

``That remains a mystery. Bakuma-san said he knew nothing about it, and I believe he was telling the truth. There's no benefit in it for him to begin with. Besides, a gold-embossed card like that couldn't be made without ordering it from a professional, right? That only raises the risk of being traced. I simply can't imagine the culprit doing something like that.''

\textit{He was right. That was exactly why it felt so eerie.}

``It was delivered only to me and Hijiri. Don't you find that suspicious?''

``You mean the Golden Week incident. Of course, I'm not saying there's no connection. But that card didn't say, `I'm going to ruin the Science Ori.' It was more like, `Secretly find the impostor among the invitees.' I don't think you need to force yourself to see malice in it.''

The conversation ended with that vague conclusion.

We spent the rest of our coffee in peaceful quiet before the meeting broke up.

``Can I have a word at the end?''

As Hijiri and Aya were leaving the room, Mikage-senpai stopped me just as I tried to follow. I followed his gesture, closed the door, and returned to the table.

``What is it?''

``Well, I don't really like sounding preachy, but there's something I absolutely wanted to tell you, Delta-kun. I want you to look at this.''

He opened his laptop and turned the screen toward me. Inside a folder were several photos with exactly the same composition. \textit{I recognized them. Of course I did---they were the photos of Bakuma I had taken.}

``I was surprised. You have incredible skill. But, you know, these weren't taken in burst mode, and yet you took more than twenty of them. It's a little frightening when you think about it.''

Mikage-senpai clicked on one, and it opened enlarged. He began scrolling through them one after another.

``In every single one, the face is in the bottom half of the frame. I thought it was strange composition, so I gave it some thought. See? In every one of them, a vital point is right in the center of the photo. Between the eyes, the temple, the back of the head. I figured out what was going through your mind when you pressed the shutter. But, you know, this isn't right.''

``\dots\dots What's wrong with it?''

``Anger can be a powerful driving force. But what you need to protect what's precious isn't anger---it's reason. I'm giving you this advice because I have high hopes for you, Delta-kun. You mustn't let yourself be consumed by anger. Between what humanity has achieved through anger and what it has achieved through reason, which do you think has done more for future generations?''

I nodded. And having done so, I spoke.

``I just couldn't forgive him. A guy who used something precious to people to try to hurt what they held dear.''

A person who, of all things, would abuse science to steal away people's smiles.

Someone who turned beautiful colored flames into a destructive explosion.

``Yeah. I can't forgive that either. I've really had enough of murder tricks that use science.''

Mikage-senpai walked over and gently patted my shoulder.

``But keep those precious feelings tucked away deep in your heart. The moment it's turned toward a person, anger becomes an ugly, lethal weapon. It's precisely when you feel anger that you have to think about how to fight with reason.''

$\gamma$

Wagyu Yakiniku Shinnai was a high-end restaurant where every table had its own private room. A shuttle had been sent to pick us up from Tsunanagai Station. The six of us piled in and were taken to the restaurant, which stood on a hill overlooking the sea.
