The spacious private room had a large window overlooking the Pacific at night. I had expected us to split into Team X and Team Y across the table, but since Del-chan sat down immediately to the right of Hijiri-kun, we somehow ended up in the same pairings as the final part of the third task, just with the two Physics Club members swapped.

We each ordered a soft drink, and at Hijiri-kun's signal, we raised our glasses for a celebratory toast. His joke---``Since we won, let's go with `complete victory' instead of a `toast' that sounds like defeat. Cheers!''---was completely ignored. Perhaps it was because most of the group was on the quiet side.

First came small appetizer plates featuring an assortment of four different kinds of beef sashimi. It was the first time in my life I had eaten that much uncooked meat.

``As expected, they don't have liver sashimi. Looks like I won't have to turn into a cow.''

Hijiri-kun kept talking with a smile, but the atmosphere among the six of us never quite picked up. Whenever I did my best to respond to his hard-to-follow remarks, Hijiri-kun looked very happy.

\textit{Someday, I'd have to ask Rei to teach me the best way to talk with Hijiri-kun.}

The course moved from choregi salad to namul and kimchi, and by the time we reached the stage of grilling absurdly thick slices of tongue, the mood finally began to warm up.

Togakushi-kun, who had looked listless the whole time, unexpectedly brought up a topic of conversation.

``There's one thing that's been bothering me.''

Since he spoke quickly while chewing his tongue, I strained my ears, desperate not to miss a word.

``Why were there six meal vouchers inside the winner's trophy from the very beginning?''

``I was wondering about that too. Does that mean they knew we were going to team up?''

Watari-kun, who had been scowling the entire time, joined the conversation. Even though it was the perfect opportunity, Hijiri-kun didn't say a word, perhaps because all his resources were being spent chewing the tongue. I stepped in to help.

``But all six of those vouchers were dated July 13. If they knew we were going to team up a week in advance, wouldn't that be a little strange?''

``It would be impossible unless they had precognition.''

Del-chan said sarcastically.

In the end, the mystery of why there were six meal vouchers remained unsolved.

The yakiniku was delicious from start to finish. Everything was perfect, from the cold noodles with a hint of sudachi to the yuzu and lemon sorbet at the end. We paid with the meal vouchers---never learning the actual price---and left the restaurant.

The last thing that bothered me was that Hijiri-kun went home by taxi instead of taking the train, claiming he had urgent business. His nearest station was Sunamizu, the same as Rei's, and we had been supposed to take the train together. \textit{I didn't think he was actually avoiding me, but I still wondered why.}

\textit{Could it have had something to do with the fact that he was wearing long sleeves unsuited to the season, or that he had eaten with his left hand the entire time? Or the way Del-chan had stayed at his right side as if protecting him?}

$\delta$

【I have just one favor to ask, if that's okay.】

Hijiri had said that to me over the phone the night before the yakiniku dinner.

【It's about the yakiniku tomorrow. I don't have much freedom of movement in my right hand. Also, if someone were to bump into it by accident, I probably wouldn't be able to endure the pain, even by my standards.】

``Are you planning to hide your injury?''

【Yeah. It wouldn't look very good for a hero of justice to be injured, would it?】

I couldn't tell how serious he was being. \textit{I suspected he meant it at least half-seriously.}

【...I'm only joking about that part, but not much time has passed since then. I don't want anyone to think, even for a moment, that someone got injured during the Faculty of Science Ori. That's why I haven't even put it in a sling. Could you help me hide it?】

``Can you manage? What about your chopsticks?''

【I've been practicing with my left hand ever since I got hurt. I can use it about as well as my right hand now. As long as I eat slowly, I'll be fine.】

``What should I do?''

【I don't intend to ask for anything too difficult. Just help me casually by taking plates or grilling the meat so my movements don't look unnatural. Also, it would help if you could stay on my right side as much as possible so no one bumps into me.】

``That won't be a problem at all.''

【Thank you. For the time being, Izuta, you're my right arm.】

\textit{The phrasing sounded suggestive.}

``Only until that injury heals.''

【Of course, I'm not saying until death do us part.】

In the end, the evening of high-end yakiniku passed without incident. My heart went cold when Togakushi pointed out the number of meal vouchers, but I think we managed to smooth it over.

Hongo-senpai, however, was impossible to read.

\textit{If she had predicted this outcome a week in advance---was something like that even possible?}

\textit{And even if it was possible, she could have just put three vouchers in the trophy. Instead, she chose to put in six---whether out of laziness or out of a desire to show off that she had known all along.}

\textit{She was a complete black box.}

\textit{I couldn't read what she was thinking at all, and yet for some reason, the results were always correct.}

\textit{The fact that this Faculty of Science Ori had ended safely was also largely thanks to Hongo-senpai. It was like a prophecy woven into the problems, as though she had already calculated Bakuma's interference. The countless last-minute schedule changes that seemed designed to disrupt the culprit's plan. And even the thorough placement of cameras that had made carrying it out so difficult.}

\textit{If she had known there would be interference, she should also have had the option of not involving the invitees in running the event in the first place. But she hadn't done that. As a result, she successfully lured in Tsuruo's assassin, let us take him down, and succeeded in getting hold of the enemy's weakness---}

\textit{Someone like me could never fill that person's role. I didn't even want to.}

$\gamma$

The day after the yakiniku dinner was a Biology Club activity day, and while I helped Karato-senpai take care of the living creatures, the four of us first-years talked about our plans for summer vacation.

Between my Biology Club duties, the Faculty of Science, and my own life as a high school girl, my summer schedule was packed.

It was going to be an incredibly hot summer, but I was sure it would be a good one.

``Oh, right. Nagisa gave me the updated album, so maybe I'll let you have a special sneak peek.''

With that, Karato-senpai handed over a thick album. The cover was labeled ``Records of the Faculty of Science Ori.'' Though the two-ring binder holding the pages together was new, the first few pages were badly discolored, giving it a sense of history. The contents had probably been passed down through generations.

``Whoa, this is awesome! We've gotta get the data for this so we can play it at the wedding reception!''

Mizasaki-kun showed me this year's page with an excited expression. There were two photos. Both had the names of the people in them written in the margins. The top one was a group photo of the six winners. The bottom one showed Del-chan and me lighting the campfire.

It must have been taken right after the magnesium ribbon ignited. Our innocent expressions lit by the white flash, and the way we held the tips of our utility lighters together like a couple cutting a wedding cake, had been captured vividly in a superb composition. Mikage-senpai certainly knew what he was doing.

``Wow, that's embarrassing... This is going to stay in the records.''

I was so genuinely embarrassed that I didn't even have the room to react to the word ``wedding.''

Del-chan, his expression blank even as his cheeks were tinged a faint pink, made a safe comment.

``The light is a bit too white for a campfire.''

I found myself flipping back through the pages. I was a little curious. I wondered if my father might be in there too. When I saw the page from thirty-four years ago, a sound escaped my lips before I could stop it.

``Ah.''

There had only been one winner. The photo of the bespectacled boy clutching the winner's trophy was labeled with the name ``Iwama Touri.''

``Is this your father, Rio?''

Rei pointed it out right away. I nodded.

``Yes. Oh, had I only told Rei? Actually, my father is an alumnus of the Chemistry Club here.''

``...No way, can a coincidence like that even happen?''

Mizasaki-kun was staring at the album with wide eyes. I wondered if it was really something worth being that surprised about, but then I noticed Del-chan was wearing the same expression. But he wasn't looking at the winner's photo at the top. He was looking at the photo at the bottom, the one of a man and woman lighting the campfire with torches.

The name ``Izuta Kenji'' was written there.

``I think only Mizasaki knew this, but my father is an alumnus of the Biology Club here.''

``Your fathers... knew each other?''

``Obviously, Navi-san. After seeing this, it'd be a huge stretch to claim they didn't.''

\textit{I hadn't known at all. My father must have seen the class roster, and they might even have seen each other's faces at the entrance ceremony. I wondered why my father had stayed silent about it.}

\textit{And surely the same question applied to Del-chan's father as well.}

\textit{Why had both of our fathers hidden something so incredible?}

\textit{And while it was probably nothing more than a needless worry---just me counting chickens before they hatched---if, by some infinitesimal chance, there ever really were a wedding reception like the one Mizasaki-kun had mentioned, I wondered what kind of faces our fathers would make at each other...}

After making a fuss about destiny and connections from previous lives, Mizasaki-kun suddenly went home looking satisfied. Rei also suddenly remembered some plans (?) and went home with Mizasaki-kun.

Karato-senpai had vanished before I knew it.

Del-chan and I were left alone in the biology room with the album that had revealed that shocking truth.

$\delta$

``They probably had a fight or something. My father's the stubborn, eccentric type.''

``If anything, my father might be the same way...''

I didn't feel like going home and asking, ``Do you know someone named Iwama?'' \textit{It felt like there was something deeper behind all this.} Just in case, I took a photo of the relevant page with my smartphone.

Still, even in their parents' generation, ``Iwama'' looked every bit the honor student, while ``Izuta'' looked every bit the otaku. Since there had only been one winner, it must have been an individual competition that year. If what Kurauchi-san had said was true, Iwama's father must have been strong not just in chemistry, but also in biology, physics, mathematics, and engineering. My father, who probably cared about nothing but plants, wouldn't have stood a chance.

``Hey, I just thought of something.''

Rio changed gears and began flipping the pages toward the present.

``Maybe Shimomura-senpai is in here. You know, the creator of the `Shimomura Method' used to set tasks for first-years at the Golden Week training camp. Senpai said he was a genius who was top of his class, right?''

\textit{I saw. If the selected members were chosen in order of their exam grades, then of course a top-of-the-class genius would be there. There was a good chance he had won.}

Sure enough, it was there on the page from twelve years ago.

Regardless of how the groups had been divided, Shimomura Reichi-senpai was clutching the winner's trophy alongside a male student whose surname, Kamimachi, contrasted with his almost jokingly well. He was wearing black-rimmed glasses just like Karato-senpai's, and his unruly black hair fell to his shoulders. What surprised me was that he had deep-set features that made him look part Western. With such refined features, Kamimachi-senpai looked like he was grinning from ear to ear.

``Ah...''

Rio gave voice to her second surprise of the day.

``What is it?''

``Wait, no, is it just a coincidence? I feel like they look alike.''

``Who looks like who?''

``You know, Claire-san. Claire Larsson-san, one of the invitees.''

``No, but the name---''

I started to speak, but then a shock like stars bursting behind my eyes hit me. How was ``Larsson'' spelled?

It seemed Rio had arrived at the same thought. She took out a notepad and a mechanical pencil and wrote it down.

\begin{center}
RACHEL CARSON
\end{center}

Shimomura-senpai was apparently nicknamed ``Carson'' as a pun on his surname. His given name, Reichi, also sounded like ``Rachel,'' which brought to mind the biologist Rachel Carson, famous for \textit{Silent Spring}.

Rio began pulling letters out of that name. Claire. C, L, A, R, E.

That left H and CARSON. Rearranged into something plausible---

\begin{center}
CLARE RASCHON
\end{center}

It wasn't impossible that the children of classmates from thirty-four years ago might happen to end up in the same grade at the same school. But this latest coincidence could no longer be dismissed as mere chance.

\textit{Claire-san was Shimomura-senpai, the Biology Club alumna.}

``It was an anagram. But why did she come under a pseudonym? She's an alumna and should be fluent in Japanese, yet she acted as if she had no memories of the school at all and pretended to speak broken Japanese.''

``She even went so far as to fool the senpais.''

\textit{I didn't say it aloud, but I knew the reason. She had touched the third rail of the CHOSEI Group through the ``Bandori Mountain Protection Movement'' and had been forced to flee to America. There was no way she could have shown her face at Tsunanagai High School under her real name.}

\textit{That was why she had slipped in as an impostor. To meet Hijiri and me, the two who had carried out the work she herself could not. And just like when she had hidden the important documents in the back of the shelf, she had left behind a small puzzle. She had sent that gold-embossed card while looking forward to seeing whether Hijiri and I would uncover her true identity.}

\textit{Had she chosen such a misleading, ominous presentation because she thought that otherwise it would be obvious it came from someone who felt goodwill toward us, making her identity too easy to uncover?}

\textit{That message had nothing to do with the Bakuma incident. In the sense that it grew out of the Golden Week incident, they shared the same roots, but the person behind it and their motive were completely different.}

``She really is the kind of person who does things in an incredibly roundabout way.''

``It was the same with the Golden Week investigation. She might just be the kind of person who likes messing with her juniors.''

\textit{That was probably the case. Neither Hijiri nor I had lived up to her expectations, but I was sure she thought that was fine.} I recalled her parting words.

Those words had been meant for Hijiri and me alone.

`I'm truly glad I got to meet you both.'

\textit{She must have gone to considerable lengths to arrange all of this, and yet she left after doing nothing more than seeing our faces, without ever revealing who she was---she was quite an elegant person.}

\textit{It was too late to go after her. I didn't even know her contact information.}

\textit{She was probably already on her way back to America.}

$\gamma$

On the walk home, alone with Del-chan, I found myself thinking about Shimomura-senpai.

About what the words she had spoken to me in the bath on the night of the Faculty of Science Ori had really meant.

And about what had been done to her ten years ago.

`My country was a very terrible place. That is why I left.'

\textit{I had thought she was talking about America, but now the meaning had completely reversed.}

\textit{Because Japan had been a terrible place, she had left it and gone to America. The period ten years ago, when she was said to have suffered those burns, lined up with the time when Senpai had graduated.}

\textit{Why did Shimomura-senpai have to go through something so terrible ten years ago?}

\textit{She had only been trying to protect the forest where the giant flying squirrels lived.}

\textit{Could it have had something to do with the Tengu Matsuri Incident this spring?}

\textit{The more I thought about it, the more stars that should never have formed a constellation began to connect.}

The falling platform. The campfire explosion. Were those really just careless mistakes and near-misses? Could two things like that really overlap by chance?

Why had the square-root problem that toyed with Togakushi-kun in the third task been handwritten in pencil on a sheet of copy paper? Wasn't the period at the end of the sentence one of Mikage-san's habits?

Why had the red combination lock blocking the rooftop been reused from the first task? There was solder left on it. It was undoubtedly the same one Togakushi-kun had used to obstruct Team X.

If those really were Mikage-san's acts of sabotage, how had she known in advance that the winner's trophy would be on the rooftop?

What if something more important than the fairness of the orienteering had been in motion back then?

Had not only Mikage-san, but Del-chan and Hijiri-kun known about it too?

During the yakiniku, why had Hijiri-kun hidden the injury to his right arm? Why had Del-chan alone helped him, silently grilling meat for him?

Had the two of them gone through some danger where they could have gotten hurt?

\textit{I wanted to believe I was overthinking it. We were living such a wonderful everyday life. To think there might be something that could harm it. And that Del-chan might be involved in it.}

\textit{I began to feel a strange sensation, as though hot blood and cold blood were coursing through my body at the same time.}

\textit{It was surely just like that summer-limited menu item.}

\textit{Del-chan was keeping it from me out of sincere concern. So it would probably be better if I never noticed. Even so, I couldn't help searching for the truth. I wasn't capable of being that wise.}

\textit{When it came to the person I liked, I found myself wanting to confirm the truth, even if it meant using a few tricks.}

\textit{Because when I looked at him, I wanted to know everything.}

``I noticed one thing during the Faculty of Science Ori. It might be obvious, but...''

I spoke to Del-chan on the twilight road leading to the station. His profile stayed expressionless, as though he were suppressing something in his heart. \textit{I didn't actually want him listening with a face like that. Because this was supposed to be a bright topic.}

``Once you know the direction you're headed, you have to face that way first.''

It was one of the basics of orienteering. Del-chan smiled, as though the tension had finally left him.

``That really is a very obvious thing.''

``Because I might have been misunderstanding something.''

\textit{Because maybe all this time, I had only been trying to look at the person who showed me the direction.}

\textit{Because that might be why I ended up seeing things I didn't need to see.}

``Just like you told me, Del-chan, I'm going to give this path everything I've got.''

``I see. I'll be looking forward to it.''

``So keep your expectations high.''

\textit{I wasn't going to say ``Stay by my side forever'' just yet.}

\textit{Just being able to face the same direction was enough to make me feel fulfilled for now.}

\textit{Even if our gazes missed each other when we tried to look at one another, I was sure we would still be able to move forward together.}

% ==============================
%        Epilogue
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Epilogue\\
    The End of the Blue Era
\end{center}
\label{sec:epilogueV3}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Epilogue}
\vspace{1cm}

At the school gate at sunset, a woman who seemed to be the one who had summoned me was waving.

But my eyes were drawn to the man standing beside her.

To the man I was supposed to have cut ties with.

To the man who had once been my closest friend, the one I had eventually handed a farewell letter to.

``Why are you here?''

``For the same reason as Iwama. I was summoned by an inscrutable junior twenty-two years younger than us.''

That inscrutable junior said nothing, merely watching our reunion with a knowing look.

It had been since Izuta finished his master's degree and moved to Kyoto. We hadn't met for nearly twenty-five years.

``Looks like the Faculty of Science Ori is over. Our children should be coming out soon.''

``They're not elementary schoolers. I have no intention of greeting them.''

``Well then, let's watch them from the shadow of the ginkgo trees. Like Kugyo did.''

``Kugyo didn't watch anyone; he assassinated them. Besides, there were no giant ginkgo trees back then.''

``You remember that story well.''

I held back from pointing out that he was the one who had told me that story in the first place.

Voices drifted out from the school entrance. It couldn't be helped. We hid in the shadow of the row of ginkgo trees. Before I knew it, the inscrutable junior had vanished like smoke.

It was just the two of us.

The students were heading home. It wasn't exactly in good taste for two men our age to be watching them in secret, but the moment I spotted my daughter, my eyes turned to her on their own. The boy speaking to my daughter undoubtedly carried the blood of the man standing right beside me.

``Unlike us, the children seem to be getting along just fine.''

``They'll fall out eventually.''

``I wonder about that. I don't think they're enough like us for you to be so sure.''

After saying that, my former best friend turned the same look on me that he had worn in the old days.

``If it ever comes to a formal meeting between our families, try to wear a better smile on your face.''

He was a man with a talent for saying the most ill-omened things. I snapped back at once.

``I am absolutely never letting her marry into your family.''

Even so, I couldn't completely hide the faint smile tugging at the corners of my mouth.

% ==============================
%        Afterward
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Afterward
\end{center}
\label{sec:afterwordV3}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Afterward}
\vspace{1cm}

Building a life around doing only what you love is very difficult. Few people clearly understand what they like in the first place, and even if they do, they still have to face the question of whether they're suited for it and whether it's something society actually wants. That is quite a hurdle. If you aren't suited for it, you have to work brutally hard; if society doesn't want it, you have to study intensely and adapt. You might even end up in the paradoxical state of wondering, ``Why am I even doing this?'' only to circle back to your starting point and realize, ``Oh right. It's because I loved this.''

Pardon the personal reflection, but now that I'm nearing the end of my twenties, I've finally started to realize that what I've been pursuing all along is probably ``coming to know unknown worlds.'' I've always been captivated by science as a way of knowing the world through non-fiction, and by stories as a way of knowing it through fiction. In that sense, the work I'm doing now with this series may truly be my calling.

This time around, I packed as much ``science'' into this book as I possibly could. I trust that those of you who read Volumes 1 and 2 will be able to keep up. While I primarily studied biology, I also love engaging with science in a ``broad but shallow'' way. In Volume 3, I included plenty of topics not just from biology, but also from physics, chemistry, and even mathematics---which is actually one of my weak points. (A huge thank you to O-kun for answering my questions about those difficult fields.) I was finally able to bring in my electronics hobby as well, which made me realize all over again how glad I am that this is the ``Faculty of Science series'' rather than the ``Biology Club series.''

Lastly, I have a few announcements. Since space is tight, I'll keep this brief.

This series, The Science Notes of $\delta$ and $\gamma$, ranked 3rd in the New Bunkobon category of Kono Light Novel ga Sugoi! 2026! To everyone who has supported me this far, thank you so much. I intend to keep writing this series with all my heart in order to repay your kindness. I look forward to your continued support.

Furthermore! A manga adaptation by Tsutsumi Wrap-sensei is currently in the works! I've already seen the character designs and storyboards, and both the characters and the story are being brought to life with incredible detail. Please look forward to further updates. I'm eagerly awaiting the start of serialization myself.

And finally, I'm happy to share that the release of Volume 4 has been confirmed! Naturally, I hope to get it to you sometime in 2026. In this day and age, being able to announce future volumes so smoothly is a tremendous blessing. I'd like to express my gratitude once more to everyone involved and to all my readers.

Well then, let's meet again in Volume 4! (I'm sure there's a preview on the back page!)

\begin{flushright}
December 2025 --- Sakai Takuma
\end{flushright}

\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Melon Books SS\\
    Jew-Beetle Absolution
\end{center}
\label{sec:melon}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Melon Books SS}
\vspace{1cm}


One summer vacation afternoon, I invited Kannabi to a rather expensive confectionery called ``Seichiku Sabo'' near Sunamizu Station. It was just the two of us, but there was a reason for it. I needed to apologize and make amends for the incredibly rude thing I had done to her during the Faculty of Science Orientation.

``Which one's the most expensive?''

We were seated by a massive window overlooking a bamboo grove, and Kannabi was studying the menu---no, here they probably called it a tasting catalogue---laid out on the lacquered table.

``Don't worry about me. Just pick whatever you want.''

I'd be footing the bill. When I told my younger sister Asahi about it, she said I absolutely had to treat her to something delicious to make up for it, and then, with a rare concession---``As long as it's not Iwama-san''---she permitted me to go out to eat alone with a girl. Though, of course, she didn't really have the authority to dictate who her older brother dined with in the first place.

I had considered inviting Hijiri or Mizasaki along. But that risked letting others in on something that was supposed to remain known only to the two of us, and if I paid only for Kannabi while everyone else covered their own, it would look strange. Treating everyone, on the other hand, would inflict serious damage on my wallet. So, regrettably, it ended up being just the two of us for sweets.

``The special Japanese-style parfait seems to come in three tiers: Plum, Green Bamboo, and Pine.''

I looked at the menu. There were three gigantic parfaits that combined Japanese flavors like matcha and red bean paste. The Pine was the biggest, and naturally, the most expensive.

``Pick one you can actually finish.''

``I wonder why only Bamboo gets the word `Green' in front of it. I guess they wanted to work the shop's name in there.''

She ignored my advice---or rather, my request.

``Green Pine would be fine, but Green Plum kind of sounds unappetizing, doesn't it?''

``True. Sounds like it might contain cyanide.''

``The one with the shop name in it is probably their top recommendation. Shall we go with Green Bamboo?''

Kannabi ordered the Pine.

And on top of that, she ordered hot matcha. Ordering matcha here apparently came with yokan, so I decided I'd have that. Besides, I figured there was no way Kannabi could finish that parfait on her own. Without Mizasaki around, I could take the leftovers off her hands.

Kannabi rarely showed any change in expression, so it was hard to tell what she was thinking. I could only guess at her inner thoughts from her actions, but the fact that she hadn't hesitated for a second to pick the most expensive item suggested she had accurately read my genuine desire to atone.

``\dots The bamboo really is beautiful.''

``Should I take that as a confession of love?''

``I didn't say `the moon.'''

``Finding bamboo beautiful is a pretty unique sensibility in its own right.''

``Is there any other plant that grows so perfectly straight? The grove is so dense the wind itself looks dyed green. If you can't call a scene like that beautiful, then what word do you use?''

``Why does bamboo grow so straight?''

``It's their survival strategy. The nodes are already formed while it's still a shoot, and in early spring, each section grows with desperate speed. That way, the bamboo can monopolize the sunlight. To achieve that kind of speed and height, it sacrifices lateral branches and becomes perfectly straight.''

``As expected of Delta. A true plant professor. If you slice a bamboo shoot vertically, you get a pattern that looks like a ladder. Does each rung correspond to a node?''

``That's right. There's meristem tissue in each section. It allows them to grow many times faster than if only the tip were growing.''

``It seems like becoming hollow also improves efficiency.''

``Naturally. There's a limit to how fast a plant's body can grow, so when it grows quickly, the inside ends up hollow.''

I had already apologized that night; all that remained was to make amends. We broke the silence with unrelated topics, and before long, the conversation naturally drifted toward shared interests. I suppose that's the fate of science nerds.

``Now that we've talked about bamboo shoots, I'm in the mood for some good ones. Find us a nice restaurant before next spring. Ideally somewhere that does rapeseed blossoms, too.''

Was Kannabi planning to hold this over me for the rest of my life?

``If we're talking about digging up bamboo shoots, Mizasaki and Iwama would probably be interested too.''

``I'll just eat them.''

``Come on, you might actually enjoy giving it a try yourself.''

``Digging up bamboo shoots is a job for wild boars, isn't it?''

``Apologize to every bamboo shoot farmer in the country right now.''

The conversation veered toward the normal and the banal just as the matcha arrived. In a large ceramic bowl with a rough, clay-like texture, the high-grade matcha frothed with fine bubbles. The accompanying yokan also looked top-tier, sliced into three pieces.

``Now that I think about it, I don't actually know the proper procedure for drinking tea.''

``It's not like we're in the tea ceremony club. Just drink it however you want.''

I cupped the bowl in both hands. The walls were thick, so it felt heavy. A pleasant warmth seeped into my palms, and I tilted the bowl to take a sip. The aroma was rich. The bitterness was strong, but it suited the summer heat.

Kannabi cautiously touched the bowl with her fingertips but showed no sign of actually drinking it. Come to think of it, she had a hard time with hot things.

``The parfait's taking a while.''

``Maybe they're out buying red beans right now.''

``Or maybe they're still in the middle of milking the cow for the matcha ice cream.''

``My, my. You seem to have no qualms about saying the word `milk' in front of a lady.''

``Don't twist my words. If that's the standard, how are we supposed to function in the Biology Club?''

``Why wouldn't you be able to function?''

``Biology has plenty of terms with words like that in them. If you get embarrassed every time you hear one, you won't be able to read anything.''

``Like metamorphosis, complete metamorphosis, and incomplete metamorphosis?''

``You're not wrong, but don't deliberately say those words in a shop like this.''

``Why? Because someone might misunderstand?''

I couldn't answer. Though, considering why my sister had sent me on this atonement mission in the first place, maybe I really shouldn't have been casually tossing around words like ``milk'' since a moment ago. I resolved to reflect on that.

Metamorphosis generally refers to changes in an organism's form as it grows, but just as I was about to explain why such academic terms were ill-suited to a confectionery shop, the parfait arrived.

It was larger than Kannabi's face. At its core, it was matcha, red bean paste, and cream, but the glass was also adorned with things like chestnuts, nata de coco, and glutinous rice dumplings, topped with a sprinkle of gold dust. Beneath the glass was a transparent film that shimmered with rainbow hues like a soap bubble. I had no idea what it was made of, but the film itself displayed a faint tint of yellow. Golden light and iridescent light accented the subdued Japanese colors. This was what people meant by an Instagram-worthy dessert.

Kannabi pulled out her phone, turned sideways toward the bamboo grove, and snapped a photo of the parfait (probably to make sure I didn't end up as an obstacle in the frame).

``Well then, time to eat.''

She scooped up a little of the matcha ice cream from the top and tasted it. It seemed to be delicious; she took another small bite. Since she was only taking tiny amounts each time, the parfait looked completely untouched.

``What? You want some?''

``Not really. I just thought you were eating slowly, like you were savoring it.''

``I'm not good with cold things. They give me a headache.''

So she couldn't handle hot or cold. Mizasaki could devour anything regardless of temperature without a second thought; if only he and Kannabi could average each other out.

With nothing to do sitting across from her, I took a sip of my matcha and was suddenly struck by the feeling of a father sitting on a park bench watching his child play in the sand. But Kannabi probably wouldn't appreciate being stared at, either. I turned my attention instead to admiring the luxurious interior of Seichiku Sabo.

The space was built from dark-toned wood, with a color palette that leaned heavily toward black throughout. The tables were lacquered in deep black. However, mirrors had been placed in many spots, and the light fixtures used bright metals---perhaps to keep the atmosphere from becoming too dim. At least, that was my interpretation.

Hanging on the largest wall was an artwork depicting a bamboo grove. It was made of paper cutouts, with numerous bamboo stalks rendered in glossy green against a black background.

Then I noticed something strange.

The mirrors on the other walls reflected this artwork, but the bamboo in those reflections appeared in a shade of blue-green---more blue than green, in fact. No wonder the shop was called ``Seichiku''---Green Bamboo. What was causing this?

``What are you looking at?''

Kannabi, who seemed to have eaten barely any of her parfait, turned toward me.

``Go ahead and eat. Don't mind me.''

``I'm taking a break. The parts that were going to melt have already been dealt with.''

She took a sip of her matcha as she spoke, but it still seemed too hot for her, and she pulled away almost immediately. Being this sensitive to temperature really did seem like a struggle.

``Things look different through the mirror. Any thoughts on why?''

``Well, of course. Looking at something reflected in a mirror means you're viewing it from a different angle. Just like how a cylinder can look like a circle or a rectangle depending on the perspective, there are plenty of examples of shapes appearing to change when seen through a mirror. Optical illusions that use this mechanism are called `anamorphosis.'''

``I see. But this time, I'm more interested in the color.''

``Color? You're seeing a different color?''

``Yes.''

I pointed to the bamboo artwork behind Kannabi. She first looked at the green original, then at the blue-green reflection in the mirror, and repeated this several times before turning back to me.

``Heh heh heh\dots''

Kannabi wore a sly grin. I asked her,

``So you've figured something out?''

``No, I have absolutely no idea.''

That kind of line ought to be reserved for a certain genius physicist from a TV drama.

``It's just as Delta said---looking at the bamboo directly, it's green, but in the mirror, it's blue-green. Why would the color change?''

``Maybe the mirror isn't actually there, and on the other side of the wall, there's the same artwork but in blue-green\dots\ or something?''

``We checked before we sat down. The other side of that wall is just a regular hallway.''

True enough. So it was safe to assume that really was a mirror. Besides, it would be unnatural to sacrifice valuable floor space just to create a hidden compartment behind a mirror. If that were the case, they would have made it far more conspicuous.

``In that case, is it possible that this artwork uses a material that appears different in color when viewed directly versus through a mirror? If such a material exists.''

``At first glance, it seems to have a bit of a metallic sheen to it.''

``Yeah, but it looks slightly angled, so it's probably a film applied over the surface.''

``Like this pink film?''

Kannabi pointed to the iridescent placemat beneath her parfait glass. But that was strange. On the white plate, I could only see yellow.

``Pink?''

``Magenta, to be precise.''

Magenta---one of the three primary colors of printer ink. In layman's terms, a bright reddish purple. But that was a color that couldn't possibly be described as yellow.

``That's strange. All I see is yellow.''

``Are your glasses dirty?''

``That wouldn't change the entire color, would it? Though, if I had to guess one possibility\dots''

I straightened up in my seat and looked down at the placemat from a higher angle. What in the world---just as Kannabi had said, the placemat had turned magenta. I lowered myself and looked from the side, and it returned to the original yellow. I see.

``Let me borrow your parfait for a moment.''

``Augh\dots\ my parfait\dots''

Kannabi let out a half-hearted sigh as she watched me pull her parfait toward me. Was it keen intuition, or something else? She looked at the placemat.

``Well, Kannabi? Can you see yellow on the placemat near my hand?''

``Indeed I can.''

``This film changes color depending on the viewing angle. It's probably due to light interference.''

``Interference?''

``I don't fully understand it either, but when light passes through the upper and lower surfaces of a thin film, the refracted and reflected rays interact with each other, and it seems that only light of a specific wavelength becomes visible.''

``I still don't really get it.''

``Like the inside of an abalone shell, or the rainbow colors you see when you look at a pearl up close---that's light interference. The colors of bismuth crystals, and the green of a jewel beetle's shell---these colors that arise from structure itself are called structural colors.''

``In other words, it's not that a pigment absorbs certain wavelengths of light, but that the film itself only reflects light of a particular color. Right? Give me back my parfait.''

I returned it. Kannabi carefully removed the film from beneath her glass and held it up, tilting it left and right. From where I sat, I could clearly see the light passing through the transparent film transition from magenta to yellow.

``Simply put, that artwork is probably using the same kind of film.''

``Is that so? But the colors look completely different.''

``Think about it. Magenta is the complementary color of green. Yellow is the complementary color of blue-green. If the transmitted light is magenta, then the reflected light is green; if the transmitted light is yellow, then the reflected light is blue-green.''

``I see. It's subtractive color mixing.''

The light around us contains a range of wavelengths---in other words, it's a mixture of many colors. The human eye perceives color using three types of cone cells that distinguish red, green, and blue. Yellow is the result of the red and green receptors firing simultaneously. In other words, yellow is what you get when you subtract blue from white light. Similarly, magenta is a combination of red and blue---white light with green subtracted.

``Look at this.''

Kannabi moved the film from the white plate onto the black tabletop. What appeared on the white plate was the transmitted light---the light that passed through the film. What appeared on the black tabletop was the reflected light---the green light left behind after reflection.

Viewed head-on, it was green. Viewed from the side, it was blue-green. This was exactly the material we had been searching for.

``The background of that artwork is black. The light reflected in the mirror is offset by an angle compared to the light seen directly. This film perfectly reproduces the mechanism by which the bamboo changes color.''

``Exactly. And, if I recall, there's a word in Japanese for this phenomenon---something appearing in different colors depending on the angle you view it from.''

``You must be imagining things. Also, shouldn't you be eating that parfait?''

Kannabi stared at me for a long moment, hesitated, and then pushed the parfait toward me.

``Help me.''

I knew she wouldn't be able to finish it.

``Looks like saving the matcha was the right call.''

The parfait was expensive, but it was genuinely delicious. That said, I was full by the end of it. Mizasaki might have been able to polish it off with ease, but this parfait was probably designed to be shared.

As we left the shop and prepared to part ways, Kannabi turned to face me once more, looking me straight in the eye. And then she said,

``Thank you for going out of your way to treat me today. The parfait was delicious.''

The fact that she went out of her way to say that---could I take it to mean my sincerity had gotten through to her?

Or did she just want to say the parfait was good?

On the train home, I found myself thinking back over our conversation in the shop.

The word for something that appears in different colors depending on the angle---the word was \textit{tamamushi-iro}. Jewel-beetle color.

\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Gamers SS\\
    The Inome That Rises in the Cup
\end{center}
\label{sec:gamer}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Gamers SS}
\vspace{1cm}

``Mikage, you always order a café latte, don't you?''

On the way home from school, Mikage had called out to me. The two of us had wandered into a café called ``Sansetsudo.'' As we waited for our drinks, I cast about for a topic of conversation with the classmate sitting across from me, smiling quietly.

``Why do you think that is?''

Having the question turned back on me was unexpected, but it was better than sitting in silence.

``You don't like black coffee?''

``Buzz, wrong. You've seen me drink black coffee plenty of times, Delta-kun. And when I have drip coffee, I basically never add anything.''

True enough---whenever someone else was treating, she seemed to drink it straight.

``So you just like café lattes, then?''

``If you can't say \textit{why} I like them, you won't get full marks.''

``That's harsh. Give me a hint.''

``Hmm\dots\ just one, then. It doesn't really have much to do with the taste.''

Nothing to do with the taste? What other factor could there be besides taste?

Just as we spoke, our drinks arrived. In front of Mikage sat a café latte, its surface decorated with the most basic latte art pattern---a heart. I, as usual, had ordered the seasonal blend. Since it was summer, it was a blend that emphasized the refreshing acidity of citrus---or so the menu claimed. They had iced coffee too, but the air conditioning inside was strong, so I'd gone with hot.

I savored the steam rising from my summer blend (it did carry a citrus aroma) and thought.

``A café latte is a mix of espresso and milk, right?''

``That's right. Espresso blended with steam-heated milk. If there's a lot of froth, it's a cappuccino. Incidentally, drip coffee mixed with hot milk is called a café au lait.''

The heart in Mikage's cup was probably made possible by the fine milk foam unique to café lattes. If it wasn't about taste, then it was about appearance?

``Could it be that you like latte art? Or rather, are you the type who cares about presentation?''

``Not quite, but that's an interesting angle. I \textit{am} curious about the patterns that appear in the cup.''

Saying that, Mikage---for some reason---picked up my cup of seasonal blend.

``Actually, did you know? It's not just café lattes where heart-shaped marks appear.''

``No, I didn't.''

Mikage moved the cup and placed it near the window, where the sunlight fell. We leaned in together to look. The sunlight entering from the side reflected off the inner wall of the cup, and a shape resembling a heart emerged on the surface of the coffee.

``It's true. What's causing this?''

``The sun is a parallel light source. That means the inner wall of the cup receives light from a single direction. When parallel light rays reflect off a circular inner wall, the envelope of those reflected rays forms a shape called a nephroid.''

\begin{quote}
\textit{Mikage had been right beside me the whole time, silently listening to everything. As though it were only natural for her to be present at those confidential meetings.}

\footnote{\textbf{Translator's Note:} In geometry, an envelope is a curve that is tangent to every curve in a given family of curves. Here, the reflected light rays form a family of lines, and the curve that touches all of them is the nephroid (kidney-shaped) or cardioid (heart-shaped).}
\end{quote}

``So the light reflecting off the inner wall of the cup converges into a heart shape\dots''

``Something like that. Interesting, isn't it?''

``Very mathematical. Though strictly speaking, `nephroid' refers to a kidney shape, not a heart shape, right?''

``Good observation. The nephroid really is named for the kidney. If you use sunlight, what emerges in the cup is a kidney shape---maybe not the most romantic thing.''

So saying, Mikage moved the cup back into the shade and took out her phone.

``But actually, you really can make a heart appear, too.''

The phone's flashlight lit up. Mikage brought the light source close to the rim of the cup and shone it in. I looked---and a heart-like pattern, similar to the one before, emerged once again.

``Is this one different from the last one?''

``Yes. If, instead of a parallel light source like the sun, you use a point light source placed on the circumference, the envelope of the reflected rays forms a shape called a cardioid. `Cardio-' meaning heart.''

``I see. So that one really is a heart.''

``The fact that we saw this heart together---let's keep it a secret from Gamma, shall we?''

\textit{Such unnecessary concern. Though I wasn't about to go out of my way to tell Iwama anyway.}

As a side note, the reason Mikage likes café lattes is, apparently, ``because the texture is smooth.''

For a moment, an image flickered through my mind of a future Mikage boldly throwing back a beer---and then it vanished.


\end{document}
